O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	 O you, most dear son, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine along with its fulfillment, and I have made the end through its explanations and by its clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	 And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the manual work, namely "surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	 And because the manual work is foreign to our region and is alien in every way, thus the science has perished and been cut off, and nothing remains of it except for a few descriptions in ancient books that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	 And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed off and the science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	 Or it seems to me that I want to revive it together with the order of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and of abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 And I will bring together the forms of the cautery irons and other tools for the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them as necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	 And because no skilled hand masters are found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	 And it is necessary for one who undertakes this to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of them, and their course and the moving and resting veins, and the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	 And because Hippocrates said that the name with the name is much, but with the work it is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	 and likewise in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	 We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned should guard against falling into error and harming people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 in such a way that I have often seen many of these who involve themselves in this science and so abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	 Because I saw a foolish doctor who cut an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 which is why so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	 And I saw another doctor who extracted a stone from an old man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 and he carried away with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	 And I had already been called to remove it, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if one cut him he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	 And I saw another doctor who took into his care a duke of our land whose leg was broken and with the fracture had an open wound; 》
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	 and the doctor, full of ignorance, pulled on the fracture over the wound with strong forceps, leaving no gauze on the wound, and left it so for one night;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	 And he commanded him not to dislocate it at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 And so it remained until the leg was completely swollen and the foot came to gangrene.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	 I was called to go to him, and I hurried to dislocate the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 And when I dislocated it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	 But nevertheless the corruption had already taken hold in the limb, and could not be healed;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 And the corruption did not stop spreading through the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	 And I saw another doctor who opened an abscess, and then ignited it with his evil will.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	 For a cancer, when it is purged of black bile, one should not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that all the corruption can be completely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	 And therefore, dear son, you must know that manual work is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	 That is to say, work in which there is danger in many situations;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 And I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	 For which reason it is necessary that you guard against it, so that the foolish physician cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	 Therefore take up your weapons in caution, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you may come to safety and be praised.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	 And leave behind the fearful diseases with great certainty;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 And remove your weapons from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	 Galen says in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 Do not undertake to treat serious illnesses, lest you be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 "I have arranged this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	 The first chapter is about fire cautery and cautery with medicine of garlic, and the chapter is ordered from the head to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 and of the shapes of the instruments, and the irons for cautery, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	 The second chapter also concerns cutting and piercing, and cupping and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 and the chapter is ordered according to the shapes of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	 The third chapter concerns the restoration of dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 And it is ordered from the head to the feet, and of the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	 So that we remember the work, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of aid and harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	 I say that the qualities of help and harm are the longest speech and most subtle science, and the secret answers.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	 And about this many wise men have spoken, and they agreed on it.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 And their words seemed little to me, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	 I say that cautery helps universally in every condition where there is material, except for two conditions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 That is to say, a hot complexion without material and a dry complexion without material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	 In a hot and dry complexion together with material, some have argued and said that cautery is of great help there; 
et li autre dirent le contraire:	 et the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 that cauterization is not effective against diseases caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	 For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be treated with heat for hot diseases or with dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 and he who said the opposite says that cauterization is very helpful against hot and dry diseases in the human body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	 For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	 And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	 For I have found it true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	 And however, one should not interfere with it except for someone who has practiced it and knows through long experience the chapter on cauterization, the diversity of human complexions, the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the occurrences and duration of time;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 we have no fear of other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	 And all the doctors gathered and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	 And know, son, that cauterization with fire is one of the secrets of healing, and more beneficial than cauterization with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	 For fire is simple and does not spread beyond the member that is burned, and it harms no other member unless it can.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	 The burning medicines spread from one member to another, and they bring serious illnesses to the member.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	 And by chance kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 The fire, due to its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do so unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	 And this I have found through experience and the length of my service and study in the art, based on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	 and therefore I apologize for the length of this explanation, because it is not my pleasure to withhold from you the secret that lies in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives away diseases of the body, as the philosophers say in demonstrating;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	 or receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	 And know, son, that they agreed upon what time the cauteries should be done, and selected patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	 And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, because the harm that occurs is remedied by the aid of cauterization;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 and also if the cauterization is necessary for pain that is urgent and pressing, so that it cannot wait until a greater harm comes to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	 And never think of this, dear son, as the foolish doctors do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	 for an illness that is cured by cauterization does not return;
et il le dient ensi;	 and they say it thus;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 but it is not as they think, because cauterization is only a medicine that changes the temperament, and dries up the humors that cause pain, and it works more quickly than other medicines due to the power of its work and dominion.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	 And it can happen that the illness comes sometimes according to the temperament of the patient and the place of the illness and its strength.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	 and the superfluities are assembled in him by the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered in place where there is little superfluousness and moisture, such as cauterizations of teeth for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	 but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	 And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and this is true.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 but they do not believe that cauterization is worthwhile after medication, but their intentions are false, and cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in some illnesses and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	 Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort in medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	 The ancients said that cautery with a gold instrument is better than with iron, and they only said this because of the quality of gold and the height of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	 and they said that the site of cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not true because I have proven it, and I found that it is true in some men.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 and gold cautery is better than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	 And yet, when you heat a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot enough by the color of the gold, and it cools down quickly.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	 and if one heats it too much;
si font au feu;	 if it is done in fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 And thus there are enough obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	 And for this reason, we use the fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	 Or I have ordered this chapter from head to foot, so that the path may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	 of the olive-based cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	 This cautery is effective against moisture and cold in the head, and there are two types made for this reason: one is due to a disease called "soda," and the other is due to various humors that descend from the head to the eyes, ears, and cause many dreams, toothache, sore throat, and all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	 The shape of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged with a dissolving medicine, modifying the head for three nights or four, according to what the strength, the age, and the habit of the patient can tolerate;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 And then have the patient's head shaved.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	 And then have him sit crossed-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his feet;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	 Then place the root of your palm at the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 And where your fingers will be, there will bleed and warm the cautery which is called "olive," of which here is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	 And place it on the spot marked with ink, and make in descending and stretching your hand little by little while turning.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	 Then lift your hand immediately, and return to the place if you see the bone is not yet visible;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	 And if you do not see it, then repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	 After that, take a little silk, and put it in warm and soft cotton inside, and place on the spot, and leave it there for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	 After that, place a piece of moistened linen on top of butter.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 And let it sit until the burn is healed.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterward, treat the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	 And the ancients said that when a wound remains open longer, it drains more.
et por ce si aide mues.	 and for this reason, it is beneficial to move.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	 And some of them said that the cautery should be applied so long that part of the bone is burnt; and then scrape off what has been burnt from the bone, and let it heal.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	 And others say that the cautery should be left on for so long, and pressed so hard that it cuts into the bone as wide as a spindle whorl that women use in their distaffs, so that the humors may exit more.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	 and one must leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 afterward, one should cure and suture it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	 And these two methods of cautery do not seem to be good in every way, except in certain men where there is fear.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	 and it seems to me that I should leave him alone;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	 because the head is weakened by continuous natural dislocations, as we have seen in other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 and similarly when the patient's head is naturally weak, and the first signs of cauterization are more healing and beneficial to me, I then work with that together for salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	 From the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	 When chronic pain comes to the entire head and lasts long, then the patient should use herbs and pills called "coccium," and of purging the head and oils and poultices;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 and if one makes the cautery that we have previously mentioned, and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	 Take care if the patient's head is of a strong nature, and that it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Then cauterize under that cautery a little, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	 Then make a cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place that is called "vasculum";
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	 and this is the place where one applies cupping glasses;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	 and raise your hand so that you do not see up to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	 the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 and the cauteries of the horns should be finer than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is the shape:
dou cautere dou chief	 Of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	 When there is sudden pain in one part of the head and the disease spreads to the eye, and the eye is purged with purgative medicines, and other treatments have been done as I said in the classification of diseases, and none of this helps:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 Then he makes cauteries in two ways, that is to say with hot iron and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	 The cautery with hot iron is done by taking a piece of alder wood, removing the bark and shaping it into two points, then making an incision in the place where the pain is such that you can insert the alder wood under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	 and when it is inserted, tie and bind it well and leave it so for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	 and then untie it and pull out the alder wood, and let the wound remain so for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 then put a cotton cloth soaked in butter on the wound until pus comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 After the treatment with ointment, when it is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 And if you see it thus, do as with some burning medications that I have written in the twelfth treatise on burning medications.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 Le fer cautère est fait de cette manière.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Chauffe le cautère comme suit :
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	 And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a small bowl where there is a hole, and in the middle there is a small opening;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	 and place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and turn it lightly a little, until half of the thickness of the head is burned;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 and lift your hand so that the surrounding area does not burn, which is outside, and an abundance of blood will flow out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	 Afterwards, place cotton in vinegar, and apply it to the spot for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then place dampened cotton in butter, and then dress the wound with bandages until it is healed.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 And if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cautellare", then use all the point, and beware of cutting the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	 of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	 When you cure the migraine as we have previously said in the division of illnesses, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cautery of medicine and iron does not suffice for it, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it becomes white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	 and thus place on the painful spot a line of half two in length, and remove your hand once, and hold it so that you do not cut the artery and that you do not reach the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	 and beware of the jawbone that moves while eating, and let the nerve not move or spasm in the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, for there is great fear in cutting, and also for him who does not know how to do it, and who is not trained and experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	 and leave the work halfway;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it should be done in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And if you see that this cautery does not suffice for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	 And if you see, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, along with the cautery that has two knives.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 And this cautery is better and more helpful than that one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	 of the ear pain due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	 When ear pain comes from cold, and one has worked with solvent medicines and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pain does not move, then heat this cautery which is called "point," of which here is the shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	 Afterward, prick all around the sore ear or around both if the pain is in both, and move a little above the root of the ear after you have marked the place.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	 And let there be ten points around each ear.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterward, heal the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	 of mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	 The ulcer that must be cured by cautery is none other than those caused by inflammation, as we have said in the classification of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 And do not perform cautery on similar things that come from drying out and paralysis of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	 When you treat this type of injury that comes from the poison of serpents and from purging the head and gargling, and if it does not work, then you must perform three cauteries on the patient.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	 One at the root of the ear, and the other a little below the temple, and the third between the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	 And place the cautery on the part that looks healthy, and make a cautery at the top of the ear above a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a finger;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	 And leave the cautery there until half the head is burnt.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	 And it resembles the lancet that we have placed before, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary that the blade be a little larger;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 after curing the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	 When the stroke is old and you cure it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	 Two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one in the place that is called "vessels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the stomach's mouth;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 And let it be cared for as we have said before.
de litargie	 Of lead poisoning
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	 At this disease, it is necessary to give the patient large doses and pills that purify the brain.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	 After this, wash the head of the patient thoroughly, and place on the back of the head a mustard plaster as is written in the treatise on plasters.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	 And this is the manner of the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 Do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	 If he is cured in this way, good.
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	 And if not, let three cauteries be made in the middle of the head descending to the neck, and there should be two fingerbreadths between each cautery.

de la froidor dou chief	 of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	 It is necessary that the head be cleansed of hairs and what we have said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	 then shave the patient's head, after which make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each horn, one behind, and three on the spine of the neck.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	 And if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient can withstand it, and the disease is severe, make four cauteries on the spine of the back.

de l’epilempsie	 Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	 Those who suffer from epilepsy should not use cautery except those who are phlegmatic, and first it is necessary to purify the brain with years and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is strong and able to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	 And if it is a child who cannot endure it, give him a gargle and chew the brain often with good food.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	 After the king cuts off the head in the middle, make a cautery as we have said before, and a cautery on the vessel, and on each horn.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if the patient is strong and can endure it, make a cautery as I have said for those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive-shaped as I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	 If the patient is a child, perform the subtle cautery as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	 When due to melancholy there are superfluous or corrupt moisture and thick phlegm, then use the same cautery as mentioned for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	 And if due to melancholy the superfluity inclines towards melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give him something to drink that will purify his brain, as mentioned earlier in the chapter.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	 After washing the head of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	 then make a bandage of linen well made, like a circle, and place it on the head.
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	 And the patient should sit with their arms crossed, and be held firmly from all sides.
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	 then present the linen and wash it with old sheep's butter.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	 and heat [the linen] over a moderate fire, so that two can touch it without being burned. xspacexn
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	 then empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And do this for the patient once a week with good care until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 And if you see cauterizing it by making several points throughout the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	 This method of cauterization moistens the brain equally;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 And then apply moistened cotton in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	 from the fear of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	 When fear comes first to the eyes through the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something purifying for the head, and protect it from all moistness, and make them sweat in the bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	 Then command him to lift his head, and make a cautery in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the descent is on both eyes together, or one if the descent is on one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	 and cut all the veins and arteries that are under the skin, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temples;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 and beware of excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, staunch it with such power as you have.

et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 And sometimes one applies cautery or burning under the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	 du corps des larmes
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	 When tears are old and habitual and are on the veins or near the arteries that appear on the head's exterior;

dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	 From the body tears within the eyes

de coi ci est li forme:	 de ceo est li formes:

dou poil qui point l’oil	 because of the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	 Sometimes it happens that the hair of the eyes is turned towards the inside and pricks the eye, and one makes cauteries in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 This is to know about fire, or burning medication.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	 Or the fire cautery commands the patient to let the hairs grow long and equal;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so that they do not move until they are born.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	 When they are born and equal, then put the patient in your health;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	 After, let there be on the skin of the eyes a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Then put moistened cotton with egg white and mastic on the eye, then heat the cautery whose form is this:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	 After cauterizing on the face where you have a pimple or lesion, do so very carefully several times until the area is burned.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	 and the sign of the healing of the work is that you see the skin drawn back, and the hairs raised at the edge of the wound.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 then remove your hand, and leave it this way for three days, then apply a cotton swab dampened in butter until the scalding is gone.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 after the treatment of the burn until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	 And if after this the hairs come back and the skin is softened, then begin again with the cautery on that same spot, just as you did first.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	 and if the hairs are gone, then cauterize until the skin is raised to its natural place, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	 The cautery of burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are large and equal, then make a form from parchment like the leaf of myrtle.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	 Then take French soap and quicklime, one ounce of each, and grind them well together.
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	 And do it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread it over the form you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and place it on the paper of the eyes.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	 And if the disease is in one eye only, then work on that one alone, and if in both as well.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	 And place moistened cotton under the eye like egg white.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 And let the patient's head be in your hand and place your finger on top of the medicine, and press down the cup and move it every time the patient feels a sting from the medicine, for they feel a sting as if by fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	 When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	 And when the stinging has passed, lift up the area of skin, and look to see if you observe the flesh raised as if it were raised by the constriction of fire or by incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 and if it is so, then all is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	 If not, then apply more medicine to the area where the medicine has not worked, until your actions are equal and your eyes focused.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then place a piece of cloth soaked in butter over the burnt area until the heat subsides, afterwards treat the affected area with ointments called "diaphenes" and others until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if you need to take great care at your work that none of the medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	 And if the skin becomes soft afterwards, and the hair pricks in the eye, then begin the treatment again on that spot which has been softened by the proper paper, just as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 after the treatment until it is healed.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 And this is the shape of the mirto leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	 And know that men's eyes are diverse in size and smallness, and according to which you will constrain it;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 And the right way is not responded to him who has studied this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	 Of the cure of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	 When you cure a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your cures do not benefit, then it is necessary that you make him cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	 Command the patient to put his head in your lap;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	 and let the minister hold his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor lower his head.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	 After, place moistened cotton wool on the egg white or in the juice of pearlwort on the eye.
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	 After, heat the cautery which is such:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	 And it is hollowed out at the end like the quill of a feather, together with which is the cautery.
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	 If you wish, let it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, let it be like a tent.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 But nevertheless, this hollowed one is better suited for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	 After, press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus, and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	 And if it is closed, then incise it, and bring forth the head.
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	 Upon this, place the hot iron on, and hold your hand to the iron at the part of the nose above the eye, so that your hand does not make a mistake;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 and put the iron in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 Se tu arrives au début de la cautérisation jusqu'à l'os, ce serait bien.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	 If not, then repeat the ironing again once, or another if you need to, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	 afterwards put on moistened cotton in butter, and the cure of drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass that it is not healed, then apply a corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 and the king according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 Et il y a une manière de faire la cautérisation d'une fistule que certains des anciens ont mentionnée.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	 Attend to the fistula, and open the site;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 Afterwards, insert into the slit a subtle instrument shaped like this:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	 and make it to the size of a .3. of lead;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	 and hold your hand firmly on the instrument, and let the patient not move at all, until the melted lead runs to its end;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	 and it is necessary that you place on the patient's eye a cotton swab moistened in egg white or honey;
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 lead heals as well around the site of the fistula, and it heals wonderfully.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, then one must administer a perforation in the nose, and redirect the fistula back into the body of the nose according to its own proper place.
des crevaices en levres	 of cracks in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	 Often occur cracks in the lips which are called "poils", and similarly in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	 When you treat these cracks as we have said in sections, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery like this:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	 And place it quickly in those cracks until it reaches the bottom;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 afterwards, treat the site with ointment until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	 of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	 When an abscess occurs at the root of the throat or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, afterwards it causes putrefaction and a hole forms and it becomes inflamed and turns into a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	 And you treat it as we have said in sections, but it does not benefit at all:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	 Therefore, it is necessary that you use the cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	 After the opening or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron comes to the bottom of it, and in the deepest place;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do this once or twice, after treating as we have said in treatments, until it is healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	 And if it is treated thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 And if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	 of tooth movement
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	 When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine and it is of no use, then place the patient's head on your healthy side.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	 afterward heat the cautery whose form will come hereafter in such a manner that you place a reed on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	 and put the hot cautery inside hastily, and hold your hand steady so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	 afterward remove your hand and repeat the cautery according to your will.
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 afterward have the patient fill his mouth with salt water, and hold it for an hour and spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	 And in this way the moving tooth is confirmed, and the softened gum is restricted, and the corrupt moisture is dried out.
de la dolor des dens	 of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	 Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor,
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 And fire cautery and grease cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	 A grease cautery is such that you take cow butter, and put it on the end of an iron or copper spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	 then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent pole, and wet it in melted butter, and put it on the aching tooth quickly and hold it until it is cooled;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 and do this often until its power reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that wool and cotton in cold butter are moistened, and put on the aching tooth, and put hot iron on it until the fire reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	 The combined fire cautery is such that you take an iron or copper tube, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	 After heating the cautery, which will be formed later, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 Do this often, for the pain will be relieved that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	 And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter during this cautery, and then rinse thoroughly.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	 And make a cautery from whatever material you wish, according to what you have available.
et c’est li forme de la caine:	 and this is the shape of the cane.
des scrophules	 from scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	 When the scrofula are caused by cold and moist phlegm and do not respond to digestive medicines, then heat the cautery made of that which is described below, and it should have two openings for the smoke to escape from the other side.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	 And place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess.
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	 And if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it there for three days.
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	 And apply a cotton pad soaked in butter until the burn has healed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterward, treat the area with onions and vinegar until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The shape of the dog:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	 When moisture prevails in the channels of the brain, and especially when this comes from a cold temperament, then it is necessary that the patient be first purged with purging medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 Afterward, make a cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to go all the way to the throat, but only a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	 After that, make another cautery at the joint of the neck at the base of the spine, and let the cautery be called "clavicle," of which we have the form before;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and heal the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	 from the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	 When all and the illness of the scrotum are due to cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the illness is old, make two cauteries on the scrotum in close places;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	 and another cautery in the middle of the breast between the two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 and let the cautery be called "clavicle" according to the form that has been said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	 And if you wish, make a cautery by pricking the entire cautery that is called "point" as the form is here before in the disease of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And let the points be up to XXX, or around it.

Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	 Et parce que ces cautères sont plus légers, car tu en fais trois à la fois.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	 Quant à la dislocation de l'épaule
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	 Et pour réunir les deux parties de l'articulation, prends une bande et fais-en un nœud double autour du cou et de l'épaule, puis attache-la au sol ou à une autre partie fixe, de sorte que le patient puisse rester immobile.  Ensuite, remets doucement l'articulation en place avec tes mains, en appliquant une légère traction.  Après cela, fais un bandage autour du cou et de l'épaule pour maintenir la stabilité.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	 Then let the patient be made to lie on his back and on his side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	 then lift the heart which is inside the little hollow between the two fingers of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 and if the joint is dislocated inward, heat the cautery which has two wires like this, here is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	 and cauterize the heart until it pierces through to the side, and there will come the figure of the cautery along with four other cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	 and therefore the cautery is made with the three-wire cautery, because the figures of the cauterizations are six cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 and the wires are according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the three-wire cautery: ️
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	 And sometimes it is placed on this one nerve, which is why there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	 After, place on the cautery powdered with silk;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 After, make the patient rest, and let the limb remain undisturbed for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it is dislocated above, which happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thick part of the shoulder blade, or many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 Because the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When in the stomach come coldness and much moisture to the point that it alters his complexion, and he has many catarrhs, and with the usual methods of care he does not benefit, then it is necessary for the patient to be laid on his back, and extend his legs and hands. 
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	 After this, make three cauteries: one beneath the heel of the foot by the quantity of a finger, at all the cautery cavity, and two cauteries on the two sides such that the figure of the cauteries is at three angles, and there is enough space between one and another so that they do not join together when they exude pus;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 and let the cautery be so deep that it reaches the two parts of the heart, and let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without alteration:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	 And if you see one being cauterized with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	 and he who fears this cautery, cauterize by pricking and signing on the stomach at this point according to the amount that you see in advance;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 then cauterize with all the cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the treatment of the previous treatment, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	 When concerning the liver, pain comes from cold and moisture and great flatulence, so much that it is strongly displaced from its natural complexion due to excesses;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	 and the patient is treated with what we have said in sections, and it does not benefit him at all, so it is necessary that the patient be seated on his heels; keit
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	 And mark three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, beyond the hypochondria, there where the ribs of the man come.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	 And let there be between each cautery the thickness of a finger.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	 And let the cauteries be as long as the body, and do not press too much with your hand on the entire cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	 And only burn half of the head, and let the patient be upright on his feet.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	 And if he cannot, then let him be lying down, and extend his legs, and raise his arms;
et c’est li forme:	 And this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	 And if it is your intention, then cauterize these cauteries with the knife, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn the entire head, for you would dry out the whole body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And let it not come up to a boil, for the heart is very sensitive in that place, and you should know this well.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	 When there is an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	 if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not very strong;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 and if it is in the membrane, then the pain is insane.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	 And at that time when this treatment was done by the physicians, it was necessary for the patient to be placed on his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 and then sign the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a grape, for this is its shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	 And burn with a cautery until the heart is burned, and reach up to the navel, so that the entire abdomen is emptied.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	 after the treatment according to the treatment of the excrement, so that he may be healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 and it is not fitting that anyone use this cautery except those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and through whom many of these diseases have been cured at some time.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then he can work boldly, and yet it seems to me that it is better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	 The fire cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	 The ancients said that one should make for pleurisy cauteries from the roots of Aristolochia, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	 take a long root of Aristolochia, the longest you can find, and let it be dry, as thick and as long as your finger;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	 And place it in oil, and grasp it with fire, and apply a cautery between the collarbone and the neck, and two small cauteries a little below in the area under the chin.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	 And two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, slanting backward a little.
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	 And one cautery in the chest, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on the ribs of the chest on either side of the cautery that is between the shoulders.
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	 And do not press with your hand, but make it openly as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	 And some ancients said that some men use a cautery similar to a razor, and heat it and insert it between the ribs until it reaches that abscess.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And the pain jumps out, as we have said in the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work there is fear that the patient may die now, or a fistula will occur which cannot be healed.
de la mice	 of the urine
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	 When you treat the urinary disease as we have said in the division of treatments, and it does not benefit, then there are three methods of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	 The type of which one is such that you should make three cauteries, or four, aligning according to the length of the muscle, following the shape of the liver cautery as we have said before;
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	 And do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient be seated on his back;
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	 And another type of cautery is that you heat the cautery with two irons, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder;
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	 And lift the chest that is near the muscle, or the rib of the patient comes towards the left, and let the elevation by which you lift the chest be according to the chest, according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	 After he cuts out the two inflamed nerves so that the heart is pierced from the other side, then draw forth from the cautery, and thus there will be four of them.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 And if you see this, cauterize the entire cautery with three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 After the treatment when he has had pus for a long time, and this is different from the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	 Of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 Cautery is not useful for those with dropsy, except in the manner called "ascites".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	 When you cure according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your cure does not profit, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the abdomen, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the bladder, two behind the back on the spine, and one near the breast;
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 And let the cautery be very close to the tip of the heart.
