Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	 Afterwards leave the cautery open for a long time to expel corruption, and do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery;
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	 And healing would hasten, and the two intentions will be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	 The shape of the cautery for the belly should be the claw that we have shown before;
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	 And the one for the back should be olive-shaped, as it is placed here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	 Of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	 When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical, and are full of yellowish bile, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring toe;
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	 And lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	 And do not enter too deeply; thus, it would burn beyond the desired area. Let the cauterization be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	 Afterwards, make two cauteries on each leg at the tip of the little toe;
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	 And let the long cautery be one below the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg;
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	 And let the cauteries heal over for a long time without curing, as the wound heals.
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	 After the cure of other wounds that we have spoken about.
de la menoison	 of the humors
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	 When diarrhea comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by usual methods of treatment;
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	 And if you see the patient in good health and of strong virtue, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before concerning the stomach cautery, and also apply a circular cautery.
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	 And four subtle cauteries around the navel, each one a subtle lancet cautery, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	 And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, perform cautery on the armpit, and one cautery on each eye, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	 of the cure for hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	 When hemorrhoids are in the rectum, one or more, and they are old and of thick, cold, and moist corrupted humors, and they are treated as we have said by division, and it does not benefit, then make cauteries.
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	 Three on the spine of the back, those which are entirely below the anus, little by little in a triangle, and one cautery below the buttocks two fingers wide.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	 And if you think his stomach is chilled, and the food does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then one should make one large cautery on the stomach, as was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the bladder with all the cauteries slanting.
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	 And let the cauterization remain open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After curing the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	 of the fleshiness which is called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	 When you cut the throat, heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it completely ignited on that slit throat;
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	 and keep your hand there until the cautery reaches the base of the vein, so that the blood stops;
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	 do this once or twice, and if there is much throat slit, then cauterize each one as we have said;
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	 after curing with beneficial ointments until they are healed;
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	 and if you cauterize with a large cautery on varicose veins, it will be more helpful.
de plaie mal curee	 of an improperly cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	 When the patient cannot tolerate cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, then such a disease occurs that cannot be cured except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	 When a fistula comes to someone, and it is inflamed and emits foul-smelling pus and corrupt moisture, you should probe it with a very fine tent, and ensure that you know the depth of the entire tent.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	 After heating the cautery which resembles a razor, insert it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tumor has entered, and renew the cautery until that rotten and corrupt flesh is burned, once or twice or three times, depending on what is needed;
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	 And take care not to cut the nerves that are within, and of large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	 if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestines, beware of these places, and do not make these incisions except in a fleshy place, and think that it is not persistent;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	 after healing the place until it is healed, and if the place is old, and the material has been removed for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed;
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	 and if the materials are not removed, know that the place is too deep, and the bone at the bottom is corrupted;
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	 and so with one of those which we will discuss in its proper place.
de la maladie des reins	 Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	 When pain comes from the kidneys due to great flatulence and a woman does not desire sex, then it is necessary that you make a fire cautery on both sides of the kidneys with the same cauterizing tool we mentioned before.
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	 And if we make the cautery in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a row, and they will provide greater help.
de la vessie	 of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	 When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the opposite side of the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one to the right and one to the left, and each cautery should be as long as the length of a thumb.
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	 And if you perform the cautery on the back, or two, if you need it.
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	 And let the cautery be flat according to the shape previously mentioned.
de la marris	 against the retention
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	 When the womb is cold and moist, and it does not allow conception for this reason, and the flowers are corrupt and their ends delayed;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	 And when they come, there is great pain:
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	 Then it is necessary that one makes three cauteries around the navel, as we have said in the treatment of the bladder, and two cauteries on the back.
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	 And let the cautery be flat, as we have said.
de la hainche	 Of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	 When the moist and viscous humors descend to the hip joint, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that one thigh is longer than the other when measured together;
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	 And the place of separation is found visible, then you must cauterize the patient on the hip bone with a circular cautery, and mark before the place around the bone as it turns, so that the bone is inside the circle.
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	 And let the cautery be such as that used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	 And if this cautery is not present, then make three large olive-sized cauteries, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the hearts.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And care for it until it heals.
de la dolor de la hainche	 of hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	 When pain comes in the hip bone, and it is from coldness and moisture, and the patient has been treated for this as we have said in the treatment, and the treatment does not work, and the disease is chronic.
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	 Then it is necessary that you purge the patient of foul-smelling pills or other good similar pills containing thick humors.
Aprés li fai cautere;	 Afterwards, perform a cautery on him;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	 and the manner of the cautery is according to two methods:
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 that is to say, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	 Fire cautery is according to many methods, one of which is as follows:
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	 that you cauterize on the pelvis of the hip III triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them deep and large, and let there be between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	 sometimes a cautery is made in the middle on the top of the hip, for which there are IV according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	 And if you see it, then cauterize with the circular cautery that we have previously mentioned in the case of hip dislocation;
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	 but do it in such a way that the circle contains the entire hip, and all the flesh of the joint is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the manner in which one proceeds with sciatica, when the pain is located in the hip and does not reach as far as the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	 And if it goes as far as the thigh and leg, then make two cauteries there where the patient says the pain is located, and one cautery above the ankle, four fingers wide, a little to the left side;
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	 and let the cautery be a sharp one, and burn the thickness of the joint.
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two feet or near there, then cauterize where he feels the pain three points or four with the cautery called "point".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	 And if necessary, do more of them;
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	 And if the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with a knife or a circular cautery, and be careful in all your cauteries not to leave the cautery so that you burn the nerves and the large arteries, and do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 And I myself have seen many who have made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so that the entire leg was swollen, as well as the foot, and all the foot was pierced and corrupt.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	 After a treatment for a stomach ailment from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	 And if the pain is in two parts together, make a cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	 And the wise say in the cautery of the hip, which is thus: make such an iron and let it be at the tip as thick as a nail from a thumb, or somewhat less, and let it be serrated and let there be between each serration the width of a pea;
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	 And the hooks shall have two parts, and they shall also be like needles, and there should be one handle of well-made iron.
et c’est li forme:	 and this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	 And let it be heated until it is all red and glowing, and then place it on the thigh of the sick person, and turn it over on the healthy side.
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	 And cauterize once with the cautery, and leave it for three days.
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	 And then make a poultice of butter, and let the wound remain open for a long time.
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After treating with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	 Al-Bukhari said that we use the cautery rarely because of the fear of its gaze, and if we see anyone using it,
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	 And yet this is of the good cauteries, which one can bear, and there where it is appropriate.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	 The cautery of burning medicine is such that you should make the instrument with tines, on which descends the margin of the opening, and it should be of bronze or iron with one long side, and at the height it should have two noses, and between each there should be the width of a finger;
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	 And they should be open from below and above, and joined together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	 Afterward, place the box of the hip on the patient lying on his sound side, and then press your hand very high up on the hip bone;
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	 Afterward, place between the two circles of the awl hot iron that has been heated in the fire one bag [of powder], and let it stay for an hour, and the patient should bear the heat and burning of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	 For there is burning as if by fire;
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	 And when the burning has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and gently raise the hip, leaving it so for three days, and then apply butter until the blackness of the burn is removed.
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	 And leave it there for three days to allow for drainage of pus.
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And that would be the last aid after the treatment with onions until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	 And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, then make an instrument that is soft in the same way as you have done on the hip similarly;
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	 And this is the manner of applying heat, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	 Take quicklime and live coal, as much of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	 Or if there is a small opening outside where the tip of a razor can enter.
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	 And put another well-leaded pot on top of it, and put powdered alkali and chalk and sweet alum on top, so that there are two layers of powders above the razor blade when you have taken hold of it in your hand.
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	 And leave it like this until the water descends and reaches the bottom of the leaded pot, then take all that water and pour it onto chalk and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	 And then it will be very pure and can be used in many medical works and for other members' cauteries.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 For it does the same work as fire, and there are other medicines with which one can cauterize the hip well, such as castor, anacardium honey, and chalk mixed together with soap. 
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 And Galen tells us of a cure by which a man was healed of the pain in the hip and the sciatic vein, and he praises it greatly, saying that no other cure was done, and that he was cured with one treatment when this cure was done, and he bathed as instructed hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	 And says in this manner that you take fresh and dry litharge, and grind it very well with a little fat, and place it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and leave it.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And leaves it for three hours, by which time the patient should no longer feel the burning sensation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then have him enter the bath until his body is slightly warmed, and put him to bed, and all the pain will go away and he will be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 Et sachez que nul ne doit user de cautère de telles médecines, si ce n'est après l'évacuation du corps.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	 And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat hair, it helps greatly.
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the big toe of the foot and the other one called phalanx.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	 Afterwards, take dry goat hair, and hold it in the fire until it becomes coal, and put it on wool, and leave it until it is stained.
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	 and do so again, and do not stop doing this until you think by your sense that it reaches the hip, and that the pain is stopped.
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 And this manner of cautery is called "cautery of cheese".
de la dolor dou dos	 of back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	 When pain comes to the back, either from falling or striking or too great an evacuation, or from the appearance of cold matter spreading, in none of these cases is it worthwhile to use cautery, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	 It is necessary that, after the patient has been purged with foul-smelling pills or other similar substances, three lines of incense should be made on their back where the pain is located, and in each line place five cauteries or more, depending on the strength and quantity that the patient can endure;
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	 and let the cautery be done according to the cautery which is called "point";
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	 and if you wish, make three or four cauteries in the middle of the nail-shaped cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	 Many times this illness comes to young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow gait when they rise, and fear;
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	 And you will find at the end of the spine on the back, and it appears on top of other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	 When you see this and you wish to cure it, then you cauterize it with the cautery of celce according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 So that the cautery penetrates each part of the spine evenly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you wish, then cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery two or three lines long, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 After curing the place until it is healed as we have said, and beware that you do not apply cautery to a swollen place that is in pain from nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	 Of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	 When pain in the joints is due to moisture that spreads throughout each limb of the body, and when pain occurs in the feet, which doctors call "podagra," and when it is caused by cold and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterization in this manner:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	 make many cauterizations around the foot joint, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if it is necessary that you prick on the surface of the foot, make a cautery at the point called "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	 And if the pain reaches the knees and other joints, which often happens, then make three or four cauterizations on each knee from every side, with each cautery being olive-shaped.
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if you need more, do more, but do not keep your hand on it longer than the iron rod is hot.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 Et si les douleurs descendent jusqu'au genou et au dos, administrez-lui la cautérisation que nous avons mentionnée dans ce chapitre.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	 And if the pain is in the hands, make an incision around the wrist two lines long;
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	 and if there remains any pain in the fingers, then make an incision on each joint and on the back of the hand;
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 And if the pain reaches up to the ribs or up to the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and give them medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 Et car si vous prenez bien soin de lui et que vous purgez la fièvre, il sera guéri avec l'aide de Dieu.
de la routure dou syfac	 From the rupture of the shoulder
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	 When ulcers occur in the anus, and feces descend into the testicles, which is new, then it is necessary that when you see it cured, he does not eat anything that day;
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	 And instruct him to use things that cause flatulence, so that his feces descend from his stomach.
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	 Then make him sit on his back between your hands, and command that he hold his thighs until the testicles descend, and bring them to your fingers, and sign below the pubic bone on the wrist bone, and let it be similar to half a circle above the body.
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Then heat the cautery which has this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 until it is white and throws sparks.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	 Then return the testicles to their place;
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	 And let the attendant hold his hand so that they do not return back;
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	 And bandage the patient's thighs well and place a pillow and a bolt of cloth on his thighs, and another on the penis which he holds with his hands;
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	 Then place the cautery on the sign with all your hand, and hold it straight and firmly until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then begin again another time until you reach the bone.
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	 and be careful that the bubble does not burst when you make the cautery;
que tu ne le brulasses;	 that you do not burn it;
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 and that the patient may not die from this or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	 And it is necessary for the cautery of children to be fine according to their measure, and also large for adults according to their measure.
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 after three days, cure the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed.
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	 after curing it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on their back for forty days so that the wound may heal well.
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And it is necessary that its caregivers be weary for a long time, so that the boils do not break out when he tries to go into rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	 And after forty days, when he wants to get up, let a well-made sling be placed on him, and he should wear it for another forty days.
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	 And let him have good rest, working little and guarding against excessive drinking and eating, and against excessively loud laughter.
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I will say hereafter the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	 of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	 When ulcers come in other places and are recognized, and you see that they no longer grow, make a second cautery according to its size, and burn one-third of the heart.
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	 after the treatment according to what we have said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-pointed cautery like this:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first mark the place and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another below it, and then hold your hand in the middle of the entire cauterization tool.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cautery is lighter and more delicate.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	 of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes to any limb, from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and medical treatment is ineffective, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and strength and location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	 if it is healed from the first cautery, that is good;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 if this is not the case, commence another cautery on top of it, for such is the custom that it should move to the nearest limb, therefore you must perform the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	 of blending
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The messengers are sometimes helped by cautery with great aid, and likewise the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	 When you see it being cauterized, beware if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not move or remain, and you doubt that corruption will spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries on the head:
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	 I pierce in the crown towards the back of the head,
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	 and one on each of the two temples, and one behind on the occiput.
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	 and you leave it until your hand is soaked with the cautery reaching the bone, and enough to bring out the scabs so that the vapors of the gross humors can escape.
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 and cauterize over the bridge of the nose accordingly as it is described before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	 And if the disorder is spread everywhere;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	 and it is manifestly deteriorating, then you must cauterize with the cauteries that we have mentioned on the head, one cautery below the nose, two on the spine of the neck, six on the spine of the back, one large one on the buttocks and another beside it, and two on each shoulder. ︎
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	 And there are two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands.
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	 And beware of the nerves that are under the heel, lest you burn them;
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	 And sometimes one makes a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	 And know that the more cauteries I make, the more help I provide, and it brings him benefit;
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as the healthy ones do, because his body is already completely corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the members and the joints, as you will find them in the manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 After treatment, dust the place with flour of vetch mixed with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	 When swelling comes to some member and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauteries on the member according to its size and smallness.
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	 And let the cautery be a little bit inside the thickness of the heart;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then the curing of onions until they are healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	 And sometimes the cautery is done on the hand and on the foot and on the back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed;
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 however, let no one interfere with it unless he is knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	 from scars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	 When the disease called "albaras" is healed, and medical remedies have no effect on it, then it should be cauterized with a small, deep cautery, according to the thickness of the heart, until the paleness is removed and its color changes.
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	 then the remedy of flour from chickpeas and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of a pigeon and almonds, one part each;
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and all should be mixed together, and tied with a cloth, and placed on the wound until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	 The cure of cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When cancer first appears and you see it spreading, then cauterize it with the cautery that resembles a circle, all around the cancer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	 And nevertheless, the wise say that one should also apply cautery in the middle of the ulcer;
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	 and yet this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupt, and I have seen it happen before.
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 and a more proper thing is that it be cauterized around the edge with the cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	 Of the inflammation that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	 When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it is delayed in death due to the excess of its production or the weakness of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and he has little blood, or because of the time;
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	 And you see that it hastens death:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	 Then cauterize around it with many small cauteries, pricking.
aprés le laisse ensi.	 Afterward leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you see her pierce with all the cautery, then heat the cautery as follows:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And place your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it outside in such a way that the course of the corruption is made clear.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the treatment until he is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	 the fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 There is another manner of disease which is called "corrodens," and is nothing other than a gnawing away of the limbs, for it gnaws at the limbs just as fire does with dry logs.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	 If you see this disease in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire together, then heat the cauteries very small and large, according to what is necessary for the place where the disease is.
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 After that, cauterize it from all sides so that you burn away all the corruption and nothing remains of it, except that everything which is corrupt be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then leave it for three days, and put on the places that have been cauterized a poultice with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the treatment of tumors producing flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	 And if you see after three days that no hair grows, it is good;
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 and if not, then repeat the cautery on the spot where the corruption remains.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	 And this condition has sometimes been treated with astringent medicine instead of fire cautery;
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	 but nonetheless, fire cautery is more effective, and I have already described the treatment with astringent medicine in the section on wounds.
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	 of leeks that grow at the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 Often it happens that at the feet, on the outside, a disease grows which is called "clots" according to our intention, and it is a large hairy thing that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cautery for this disease is in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 That is to say, cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	 Fire cautery is that you heat the cautery as if it were a goose feather, and let it be made of good iron to the extent that it can fit the nail on all sides, and let there be subtle edges.
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	 After, place everything hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the head of the nail.
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	 And leave it thus for three days until it begins to emit pus;
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 Then make a poultice of crushed wild mallows with vinegar, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its base.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat the burn site by applying ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	 And if they are turned outward on the body, and this often happens in hands and feet, then you must apply a hot water cautery;
et est en teil maniere:	 and it is done in this manner:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	 take a reed of copper or iron, or a goose quill, and place it on the nail and the wart, that is to say, on warts;
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	 And put the candle on top so that it drips all around, then place a cloth of warm water there, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the candle comes to the base of the nail, and let the hot water find its deep way until the root;
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	 and let the patient endure a little the biting of the hot water for an hour;
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 then leave it thus, and it will be uprooted from all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 So do one after another, until you remove all those that are on the body, then treat the swellings that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	 treat the shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	 When someone trembles from cold of the nerves, or from tertian fever or another, then you must make four cauteries or five on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra;
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	 And for cautery on the foot, and above the stomach for the liver cautery;
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	 let it tremble, and the health of the cold illness will hasten.
des pustules puans	 stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes appear on the surface of the body washed with water, or stinking pustules, which come from large corrupted substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	 so it is necessary at first when they appear to make a cautery on each head of the pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, whose point is taken from the fire, or of long aristolochia root, or for the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	 And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow from then on, but the excesses from which they come are broken down, and they heal;
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 but it must be done after blood evacuation.
quant li artere est copee	 When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	 Many times there is a great loss of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound on the outside, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cautery of the member, and similar things;
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	 And it is very serious to stop it.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	 And yet when this happens to anyone, you must quickly place your finger on the wound of the vein, and press very hard until the blood is quiet under your finger, and no more drops come out;
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	 then heat several small and large olive cauteries in the fire until they are all red;
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	 then take one, large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	 And if it spurts when you remove your finger from the vein and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another one of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	 And do not stop doing one after another until the blood is drawn out;
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	 and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient;
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	 and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be stopped well, especially if the artery is large, except by one of the four methods that we have mentioned;
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	 or by cauterization, or by extracting it if it has not been cut, or by tightly binding with a thread, or by applying medications that have the power to stop blood;
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	 and let it be tied and bound properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	 Whoever manages this will use a tight bandage of cloth or place burning objects on it, or similar things, if it is not beneficial or possible otherwise.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	 And if this happens to someone and they have no physician or medicine at hand, then they should place their thumb over the wound of the vein as we have said, and press down firmly until it is stopped on the wound and on the vein;
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	 And do not move the finger, but moisten it with very cold water often until it is very cold and the skin is frozen and swollen and stiff.
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	 And make inquiries about what he needs for cauterization and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	 Here begins the second book on the treatment of hernias
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	 We have told you in the first chapter all about the disease for which one should cauterize with fire or burning medication, and the occasions and causes and instruments and forms of cautery;
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	 and I have placed this chapter from head to foot, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same method so that one may more easily find what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	 And before I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one concerning cautery, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	 For in the work of this chapter there is often evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	 where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many types of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	 if they are of such a nature that they will die quickly from their illness due to the madness it causes and the severity of its harm;
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 and one should fear them.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	 And there are some who give you their reason and say:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	 “wait, I am cured.”
et li maladie est despitouse.	 and the illness is disdainful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	 It is not appropriate for you to consent to those who come to you with this manner, but rather put more consideration into your honor than your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely concerning that which you are certain of, and from which you can gain respect and praise.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	 and use prognosis and diagnosis in treating your patients so that health may be restored;
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 and this will help you acquire a good reputation, glory, and fame.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	 Very dear son, may our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	 Now I have arranged this chapter for you by chapters, according to what is in the previous chapter on cautery, which I have discussed with you from head to toe, so that you can find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	 head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	 Know that this illness often afflicts children during birth, and when the midwife pulls too hard on the child's head;
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	 and sometimes it occurs due to an unknown cause, about which we know nothing.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	 And I have never seen this illness except in children, and for all those that I have seen, death was imminent;
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	 and therefore it seems to me that I should leave the work of treating such cases alone.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	 And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head swelled each day so much that it could no longer hold it; ‌
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	 And so much moisture gathered that he died, and this moisture is collected beneath the bone on the rib, between the heart and the bone.
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	 And the work is such that if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, you should cut a wide slit into the head.
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	 And it should be as long as two fingers, until the moisture has drained.
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	 And see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	 If the moisture is greater, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	 And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs are that you see the seams of the head open on each side, and the water jumps out strongly when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not respond to you:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	 then you must cut three slits into the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision, remove all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	 After bandaging the cuts with rags and powders, apply wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day;
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 Then unbind it, and treat the wound with tentes and dressings, and let the head be bandaged evenly, and then give the patient dry food of little moisture until the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	 And another method of incision is that you consider where the greatest part of the abscess appears, and the accumulation of pus;
car aucune fois est elle devant;	 for sometimes it is in front;
aucune fois derrier;	 sometimes behind;
aucune fois en destre;	 sometimes on the right;
et aucune fois en senestre.	 and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	 Cut then where the abscess appears, and the accumulation of pus, and make the incision according to your ability;
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	 And see that you do not cut the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	 and a vein flows with blood, so that the patient dies from bleeding and moisture loss.
de reume	 of inflammation
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	 When someone has a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or nose, and the illness is longstanding, and medical treatment does not help, then the final cure is to use cautery, with which two arteries will be cut.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	 Therefore, when you see him cut, it is necessary that the patient lean his head back;
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	 after which you rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then have the patient strain his neck against the entire cloth;
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	 then look where the veins beat, and the place of one and the other is after the ears, and a few are returned;
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 then mark the places thus, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula of two parts, so that the incised vein reaches to the bone, and this should be along the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	 And if you see, push the spatula under the vein and cut above it, cutting also as two halves across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	 And when the vein is cut, the blood constantly spurts out.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	 And if the artère does not open to the touch, then you must measure the width of three fingers, then take a saw and cut down to the bone;
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	 and what is needed of the blood let out is six-tenths, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the fullness of the artery;
puis regarde la plaie:	 then observe the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 if there remains on the bone no trace of pus, then shave it clean so that no such abscess may come; then constrain the wound and bind it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	 of headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	 When an ancient headache comes, and acute catarrh, due to the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and old foolishness and similar things, and he is treated by various methods of medicine and all this does not benefit him at all, then we will extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	 And the manner of extracting them is that the patient must pull back the hair from his temples and aim for the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its pulsation, and is little hidden outside except in certain men who are too cold;
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	 And if it is inflamed, let the patient constrict his neck with some cloths, then rub the area with some rough cloth, and rinse the area with hot water until the veins appear clearly;
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 Then take the spatula which is shaped like this:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	 Then peel off the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then draw it up with the tweezers, and make sure it is well separated from the tissues underneath each part;
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 And if the artery is thin, then wind it around the tip of the hook, and cut off that part according to the size of the two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 For if it is not cut, then the blood will not come out at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	 And draw blood for six times, until three.
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	 And if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread, so that putrefaction does not occur before the healing of the wound, and let the blood flow gradually;
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	 Then cut the superfluous tissue that is between the two ligaments at that very moment, and then, if you see fit, apply the cautery with the knife until the bone.
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	 And this is a good work, if the patient does not have fever and has a warm constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	 For the cautery helps to dry up the moisture:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	 Therefore, it is of greater help to moists.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	 Where for the extraction of arteries one should fill the place with old cotton and put on well-made bandages.
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And when they are unbound, then they should be cured with dry medicines that promote healing and with bandages, until they are healed.
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	 And if you cut the artery as much as you work on it, then hasten with the copper by cautery, or apply vitriol to the place and hold it in your hand so that the blood is staunched.
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	 And if you do not have this (vitriol) present, then place your finger on the spot until the blood is frozen, and rinse the spot with cold water until the bleeding stops, and hold it as needed.
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	 And that which is better and lighter in the extraction of the artery is for you to cauterize the wound with this cutting cautery from two sides, but let the cuts be well spaced to maintain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	 Car when the instrument is too blunt, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	 And there should be one finger's width of space between the two knives, and then when you have inserted the two blades, place the burning iron on it until it reaches the bone, and cut the wound in two places.
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	 And they should be separated between the two heads because they are not fused by this cautery at all.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	 tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	 When tears fall from the eyes and descend into the veins that are on the temple of the head, and medicinal treatment does not help at all, and you see the patient's face redden, and they feel a throbbing sensation in their forehead as if trembling;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	 And if the eyes are pale and moist so that the hairs of the eyelids have fallen out, and the eyelids are heated and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	 And the ancients called it "treatment for concussion", and what you must do is to cut off the hairs that the patient has on their forehead, then make three incisions in the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	 and let one of the incisions be like the two that are all in the forehead from top to bottom until the nape, and the other two on the ribs above the breasts, and beware of the incision of the arteries that are on the sides above the breasts.
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	 and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be three fingers wide across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 and have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping away the blood, then pour in the sharpened instrument from two parts where this form is:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	 from the incision which is in front of the temple up to the second incision.
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	 and scrape all the skin that is between the two incisions to the full thickness on top of the bone, then do the same from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then withdraw this instrument strongly.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	 Place in the first cut the instrument called “scraper,” which is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And put the sharp side towards the flesh of the heart, and the soft side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	 And cut all the vessels descending from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to what opens from the heart, and then make another cut in the middle of the split until the other defect.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	 And then draw out the blood equally, and press on the place for the blood taken;
