puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	 Then put in each split a tent of old cotton, and put on wet cloths with wine and oil and vinegar, and make sure that no abscess comes there;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And on the third day untie the bandage, and apply a large compress of boiled water, then treat with ointment of basil and rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	 of the humor of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	 When to some people comes acute catarrh usually, and you see the eyes watery and small, and weakening the sight, and the eyelids burned;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	 and the hair falls out, and on the head there is intense pain, and the patient sneezes;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	 then know by these signs that those matters and that catarrh come only from many veins, and the best treatment for it is this:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And it is that you instruct the patient to shave his forehead, then make a great incision in the middle of the forehead, and another from the left eye.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	 And begin from the cleft of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go down to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	 and keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that move during eating;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	 and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then dry between the two lips of the cleft and put in old cotton wool and linen cloths;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	 then lay upon him moistened cloths in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 when it is removed, then you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents that cause the flesh to grow.
En teil maniere:	 In this manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	 take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice with it;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	 and administer it to these wounds to promote flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 Of ear blockage
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	 All that falls into the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	 or grain, or animal, or mineral stone or similar thing like iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	 or seed, such as peas, beans, lentils;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	 When something flows like water and is easy and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When something falls into the ear that does not belong there and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	 If you see the stone, then drip some violet oil or sesame oil onto it, and then perform an extraction.
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	 And make him sneeze with a stimulant, and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	 and stretch the ear upward.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	 Often this cure is successful;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 and if it does not succeed, then apply an extraction with fine tweezers, of which the form is this:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	 If it comes out well with the tweezers, that is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	 if not, then apply an extraction with a fine hook of small size;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	 And if it does not jump out by itself, then make a tube of brass and insert the end of the tube into the opening of the ear firmly, and stopper that which is around the tube with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter along with the tube;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	 then pull strongly on the tube, for often it comes out as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	 and if it does not come out in this manner, then take the birdlime with which birds are caught, and put some on a suitable instrument for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	 then press the birdlime onto the foreign object or whatever it may be, and pull strongly.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	 And if it does not jump out from all these things that we have said, then you should hasten to cut open the ear before a hot abscess and spasm arrive there;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	 and the manner of the incision is that you first anoint the patient with cephalic, and let out blood according to its measure of virtue, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upward, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty place where it depends;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	 and let the incision be like a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, and suck on it hastily to your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and the treatment until he is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	 And if it is grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction.
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	 and if it cannot come out, then administer the subtle, gentle sputum according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision for that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	 But do not do this when you think the grain is wet due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces.
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 then strain it through fine sieves and press, as we have said, so that the extraction may be clear.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 In the case of water falling into the ear, it is necessary that the patient first use sneezing condiments, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let him lie on that same side where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If she jumps through the roof, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	 if not, then take many stones according to the length of your thumb, light and thin, and heat them a little over the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	 and place the patient in a kneeling position with one knee under his ear, and have him stand on his other foot, and strike another stone over the stone that is in the ear.
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	 and do not stop striking stone after stone until all the water comes out, and thus it jumps out completely;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	 And if you see it, take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and set the other end on fire until the larger part of the reed is burned.
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 Then do the same with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said about stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	 In extracting the creature, if it is of small body, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	 but if it is of large body that can be felt, then use a puncture for extraction;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	 and this is the lightest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	 In the extraction of worms stuck in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not work, then you must look at the ear to the sun.
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	 Si il y a des vers, retire-les avec des pinces fines. Et s'il n'y en a pas, prends le couteau pour faire une incision.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	 Et mettez délicatement le bout le plus fin dans l'oreille, en fonction de la tolérance du patient à la douleur, puis tirez fortement tout le couteau.
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 Faites cela plusieurs fois jusqu'à ce que tous les vers sortent.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	 Et s'ils ne veulent pas sortir, bourrez autour du couteau avec du coton, comme je l'ai dit pour la pierre.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	 Et s'ils ne sortent pas comme nous l'avons dit, administrez des distillations que les anciens ont prouvées pour tuer les vers. Vous trouverez comment préparer ces distillations dans le traitement des distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And so drip your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, of which here is the form as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	 And whether it be of silver or bronze, it should have a small hole at the bottom and an opening on top to drip through.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	 And to press the distillation inside, use an instrument of bronze well-made for this purpose. And if you wish, take a scraper and wrap tightly around its point with cotton.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	 Then cast your oil or juice, and whatever you wish of your medicines into the reed, and let the reed be in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	 Then insert the scraper with all the cotton inside, and press your hand gently until the oil is dripped into the depth of the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	 And let the patient feel within him, and let there be the distilled juice in a heated pot over the fire before it is dropped into the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	 And ensure that it is not too cold, for then the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 Of ear blockage
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	 No child is born without a small opening in the ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	 and the same thing happens to men due to the obstruction of a wound or growing flesh within the ear, and this obstruction sometimes goes deep into the ear, so that it cannot be seen;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	 And sometimes the pot overflows through the opening, and one can see it clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	 That which goes deep within and cannot be seen is difficult to treat in many ways. And that which one can see must be placed in the sunlight by the patient;
et regarde dedens:	 and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 if you see the hair obvious, then do all this operation with this instrument of which here is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	 And let it be sharp and cutting both in front and behind completely, so that it does not wound the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	 if the hair is of flesh or body of the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers and cut lightly until all that flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the hair has grown deep into the ear, take a fine and light razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it on the cartilage of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	 If you feel the hair of which the patient feels pain when hearing, prick lightly and take care not to harm the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 then place in the ear a plug according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	 Pour ce remède, fais cela chaque jour jusqu'à ce que la plaie soit guérie: prends une étoffe et trempe-la dans de l'eau de rose, puis saupoudre dessus du vitriol broyé.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	 And if you see the ear swelling, it is necessary to remove that cloth and replace it with another cloth moistened in a salve made of rose oil and wax until the swelling disappears.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	 And if bleeding continues, soak a sponge in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding, which are discussed in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	 of the skin of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	 This ulcer, which comes on the eyelids when they are moist and then dry, you must extend it with tweezers and scissors, and cut it off with a spatula from its roots.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	 Then place vitriol powder on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	 And if it comes off, then cauterize with a subtle lenticular cautery, and afterward cauterize the incision in order to move (it).
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	 and often they return, as long as something remains of their root;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	 and when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burnt and do not come back.
de la gresle	 of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	 Often in the eyes there come things that resemble hail in their form and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "hailstone," and it is a collection of thick moisture above and below the eyelid.
li ovraiges est telz:	 The workings are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	 watch if the hailstone moves from one place to another, and this is easy to know.
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Wound it then broadly, then gently scrape each part, then take it with tongs, and cut it off.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	 if you cannot cut it without slightly piercing the skin, it will not harm the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 and if the split is large, join it with a stitch, and treat it until it heals;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 and if it is small, do not apply any pressure, for the ointment will restore it quickly and promote flesh growth.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	 And if the sty is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, invert the skin, and hold the sty with tongs, and cut it off while pressing on both sides.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	 and if the skin is separated by the incision, it will not harm anything;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	 And when hail is struck, lift the eye with salt water, and heal the place of it which injures flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	 of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	 Exinach is a fat that is inflamed in the membranes of the eyelids, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it greatly harms their eyes, and catarrh comes to them in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 and therefore they always lie on their faces, and sleep with them swollen, and their eyelids are moist beneath their eyelashes where the inflammation and appearance cover the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the place between your fingers and feel the exinach there.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	 And the manner of the work is such that the patient places his head in your hand;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	 And then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains each part, then place it on him;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	 And press with your two hands from both sides, so that the parts are assembled within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	 Then in the middle of the moisture make with a sharp scalpel an incision wide enough, but not larger than the wound that is made for venesection;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	 And pierce the skin thoroughly until you reach the parts;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	 And in various positions pus comes out of the incision, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	 Pull it out then all at once with a piece of cloth between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is spread out.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	 And make sure you do not push into the slit, so that you do not reach all the way to the eye and injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	 And if the sty does not open at the beginning of the slit, then slightly widen the slit until it opens.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	 Then pull it out as we have said, then wet the cloth in vinegar and water, and place on the spot, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And there are such men who grind salt and place it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the patient until he is cured.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it comes to the place of a hot abscess, then treat it with soothing poultices until it is cured.
des poilz des papieres	 of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	 When hairs grow on the eyelids that are not natural, and they become irritated, they harm the eyes and bring about various diseases such as constant tears and softening of the eyelids and pus, so much so that it leads to the loss of sight.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	 And the treatment is according to four ways:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	 Or by fire cautery together with fire, or by medicinal water according to what was said in the previous chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by chains, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	 You must place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the eyelid of the eye to your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	 If it is turned inside out, that is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	 If not, then insert a needle all the way to its eye;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	 And let it be near the edge of the eyelid where the hairs grow near these hairs, and draw the thread all the way through the eyelid, and turn it to the razor.
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	 Then they make an incision in the part below the skin, under the hairs, covering all the flesh, from the large tear duct to the small one.
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	 Then they pull out a thread, and place under the skin a small tent of cotton and cloth, then sign on the skin a figure of ink, such as the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you wish to raise the skin that is divided into all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	 And for those who need it, cut a large quantity of the skin according to how the skin is softened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	 Then they make an incision along all the flesh on the two lines you have marked, and begin from the large tear duct down to the small one.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	 And let one of the clefts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then apply oil to one of the two corners of the heart, then scrape it all off.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	 Then join the two lips together with a seam of one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and let the excess of the threads dry on the two corners with any sticky substance, if you wish to do this.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	 And if not, then pay no heed, but leave the seam and the threads for three or four days;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	 Then treat the wound without seam with dry and astringent substances, for the skin revives at the healing of the wound and its union, but the seam is harmful (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	 And there is another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 and it is that you should mark the paper with a shape like the leaves of myrtle, as we have described, in three empty spaces according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	 then cut the one that surmounts the small equal forces according to the form that is here
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	 And if you cannot hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with one thread, and insert it into the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	 and insert another thread near the large eye, and the second thread near the small one, and bring together between your fingers the threads equally;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then raise your hand equally, and lift all the leather on which you have marked, as we have described, then join the two lips of the wound by stitching, and heal it until it is healed;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	 And if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar calming ointment;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	 And sometimes it happens that the hair of the skin is converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	 then you should use what we have said about incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 but the sewing in one and the other is more technical.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	 The treatment of dogs is as follows:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	 and it is that you convert the skin and open it inside as I have said, then make two dogs with skill, and two fine threads as long as the length and width of the spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	 and cut off the ends of the thread in two parts where you hold the threads; etime la cure est moult bele, et moult prodoment faite.
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	 Then carefully bring together the two parts above the papillary layer of the eye, and firmly pull on the two canthi from the two sides.
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	 And leave it this way for some days, and the skin that is pulled will die and blacken and rot, until it falls off on its own.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 If it delays, then give it some strength, then treat it until it is healed.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	 And when the wound is healed and the papillary layer has been lifted, then the hairs will no longer grow.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 And these are the shapes of the two canthi that you should make according to this figure and according to this measure in length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	 The procedure is such that you take a fine needle, and insert one thread of soft and fine silk into it.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	 Then gather the heads and tie them together subtly, and let the length of the thread be a palm long.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	 then order in the sheath another thin silk thread briefly, and tie the heads of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	 then have the patient place his head in your hand.
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	 and let it be near the sun so that the work may be illuminated, for this is a subtle and small operation. Then push the needle all the way into the sheath at the root of the hair, and make it pierce the skin quickly until you draw it out above the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	 then pull the hair until it reaches the sheath, and push into the sheath that hair, if there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	 Then pull your hand until the hairs come out completely from the skin with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	 And if the skin is stretched and the hair does not come out completely, you will draw the skin down to the bottom of the thread that you have placed there, so that the skin comes out from the opening above and that you can see it with your eye.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	 Then draw the skin and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair hardens in its place and the flesh grows.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	 And if the hair is small, accompany it with one long natural hair from the head, and raise it with that one until it is lengthened, then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	 of the infection of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	 When this disease called "aleacrati" or purulent infection comes to the eye, there are two types.
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting, or from cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And the way to work on it is that you split open that union, and undo its lips, and put inside linen tentings, and let it rest until it heals.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And it is not necessary to use in the cure of it things that dry out and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	 Because if you do this, the disease returns worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	 but working with softening things, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 and the juice of water or ale and flaxseed boiled together, and melted onion in some oil, and wrap it in a tenting, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	 And the treasure of your care is such that you must take caution that it does not heal in a manner different from what it was before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	 and these works that we have spoken of are not outside of the remedies for this ailment, so that it may heal according to its original form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	 of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This illness which is below and is truly called "axacrati," and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	 The accident comes from wounds and cuts and burns and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	 and the way to perform this operation is such that you take a needle with a double thread, and insert the point into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left margin as far as the right, so that the thread comes out in two places in the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 then press the flesh down over the entire needle, and cut it to a wide spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	 And if the shape of the stone returns as it should be, this is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	 if not, then take a razor and place it in the crack, turn the stone, and make two cracks on the inside of the stone;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	 and the heads of the two cracks should be at the two corners of the cut that you have made, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter which is called "I Greek";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	 then remove that piece, according to the quantity that its sides are sharp underneath, from what follows the stone, then join the two separated parts and sew them together with a thread of wool;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then care of what we have said about softening medicines, and tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	 And if the illness comes from a cut or stitching or cautery, then you must make a clean cut under the skin of the paper, according to what is said before.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	 Then sever between the two lips of a tent, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	 and one should perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares an engine with all his power how he may bring back the figure to its natural form;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	 and the patient himself, according to what is necessary for him in work and instruments, in many situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	 of the suddenness of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	 When this joining occurs in such a way that the skin on top is joined with the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a razor beneath the skin, and lift it up.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	 and stretch it with pincers, until you cut off what is attached to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp or cutting, so that the patient cannot tolerate the spatula being too sharp hurting the eye.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	 and let your incision, by which you peel off that assembly, be light, so that the skin returns to its natural shape.
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	 and all that assembly is healed, and sometimes the eye becomes inflamed with salt water, and lift it with fresh water, and with honey.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	 Then place a linen bandage between the paper and the eye, and put plenty of wet wool on top of the eye.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And after three days, use cold compresses and astringents until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	 of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	 Know that the nail is according to two kinds:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	 the first is nervous and similar to hard stone, and the other is not nervous but resembles white frozen moisture, which when touched with iron and one tries to take it with pincers, no one can.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	 And both resemble the growth beginning towards the large tear duct and grows little by little until it covers the entire eye and all its light and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	 And the manner of the incision is such that the patient places his head in your lap, then closes his eyes.
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	 and lifts the paper to your hand, then winds the nail around small forceps, and stretches it upwards.
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	 then take a needle, and put a horsehair, or cow hair, or ox hair in it, and the thread strongly.
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	 and double the point of the needle a bit and insert it into the nail, and pierce through the entire nail, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it upwards, and peel off all the skin on the side of the nail that follows the fingertip and the silk along the hair down to the root, then cut off the remaining part at the root of the tear duct with all the delicate spatula and small forceps, and leave the natural flesh in the tear duct, so that through the incision the body does not usually come to tears.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	 And sometimes the nails extend to the fingertips, and to the thread, as we have said.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	 Then scrape off all the soft part from which this form comes:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	 And be sure that the soft part does not touch the flesh and tear it, and that the wound is not pierced.
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	 And after the incision, put in the wound a little bit of crushed salt and from the vitriol made of lead, and leave it until the next day.
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat this until it is healed as needed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	 And if the nail is not fleshy and you cannot insert the needle, and the fingertip cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail can be cured with medicine.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	 And they are born like I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, work the eye of the patient, and take a small knife with a sharp point according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	 And lift the nail gently on top, and if you see that it does not thin out at all and the reason presses there, then drip from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of lead oxide and red collyrium, ground together, and plug the eye until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	 Then resume the other work according to this same procedure, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If nothing is against you in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then let it be, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	 And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear duct clouds the eye with great annoyance, then suspend it to the upper eyelid, and cut off a part of it but not all, so that tears do not come into it;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	 then pour into the eye red choleric [substance] made from lead.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	 of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	 In the eyes of some men there sometimes appears red flesh, and it covers the pupil and extends onto the eyelids, and it turns outwards, and it resembles a rosette of a baluster.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	 and the work is such that the patient should place his head in your lap, then you should open the eyes, and all this flesh is collected into suitable receptacles, and it is sustained with force.
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	 then cut the first flesh, and continue cutting everything down to the end with the razor, and be careful not to damage the eye in this work.
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	 and let the incision of the [instrument] that we have mentioned in the incision of the nail and in small forces from which one removes the splinter be as described after this chapter shows it.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	 and when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed, fill the hole with hot oil from a burnt seal, where you drip red colocynth and similar corrosive medicines, and place over it cotton soaked in egg white, ensuring the abscess is warm.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	 and if anything remains, and the pus overwhelms you, and you doubt the abscess is warm, then leave the hole and treat the abscess with soothing remedies.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 then return to your work until it is healed, and do the same when flesh forms in the hole by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	 Yet you must lighten the treatment of each weak hole according to its natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	 And by the way of an accident, in ironwork;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	 And do not put your hand in any of these workings until you see that this limb is tolerant of the working.
des voines des eulz	 of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 If they are red veins that cover the eye, they take away from sight its function and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	 It is necessary, therefore, first to examine whether the eye in which it is located is sound and there is no other disease besides the cataract;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	 then cauterize the eye in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 instruct the patient to place their head in your hands, then suspend those veins with all the skill you possess, and let the needle be fine, double, according to this form: ›
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	 And let there be two marks by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	 then cauterize the veins strongly and subtly, and wipe away the blood hour after hour, until you see the veins move outside of the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	 And be careful not to wound the eye with the tips of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not cut deeper than those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	 And when you have done this, instill in the eye green and red choler to corrupt what remains of the black bile.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if you cannot collect all of it in that hour, then make a poultice for the eye with soothing substances to relieve the pain, and leave it for some days until the pain is relieved and an abscess is certain, then begin again according to this manner until he is healed.
et c’est li forme des forces:	 And this is the shape of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	 of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	 The physicians call these «arissati» fistulas:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	 when you cure it by cautery and by burning medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a trick in it that you should cut over the abscess where it must die, and draw out all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	 And when the bone is exposed and you see the decay and blackness, then take away all the instruments of which there is the shape;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	 and it is called an "asharpened head," and should be made of iron or steel, and should be pointed like a file as it appears in the following figure:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	 And put on the spot of the corrupt bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press with your hand for a short while until you know that this corruption is remedied.
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	 And do this several times, then restore the spot with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	 If the spot is healed, and flesh grows there, and the body of the wound is healed, and it remains so for forty days, and it does not reopen and is not infected, and no bad incident occurs, know that it is healed.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	 If not, then there is no other device than to bring the fistula back to the puncture of the knife according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 And it is that you uncover the bone for the second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered then take a drill according to this form, and let the head of the iron be three-sided, and let the shaft be tapered up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	 Then place it on the bone next to the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye socket, then turn the drill until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it because the wind escapes if he holds his hand over his nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	 and then restore the place with dry medicine as I have taught you, and when the flesh heals and the spot hardens, the material goes to the nose;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 so it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	 Of the eye issue
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	 When the eye is fully open and there is no obstruction or narrowing of the nose, then you must bind the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	 then let him heal, then place cupping glasses on the temples without pricking to suck out [humors], then put on the eye a poultice made of iron filings and aloe and frankincense and sarcocolla, and then bandage the eye with bandages and cloths;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	 And the manner of bandages is such that you take bandages soft enough, and fold each one in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye may need.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	 Then press firmly with a hard bandage on top, and start the cupping again to draw without hurting.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	 Then remove the cups and leave the eye bandaged day and night, and if the bandage becomes loose, you must tighten it very much.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	 Then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see the eye improving, that is good;
se ce non;	 if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then begin again with the poultice and the bandages and the bandage and the cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	 of the dislocation of the toe
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	 When discharge comes from the bladder, it opens, and comes forth from the flesh like a grain of resin, and is terrible to see.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	 then if you see it covered, the work is such that you insert a needle at the root of the lower part up to the upper one, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the eyelid;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	 and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position.
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	 then cover the place of the double thread and tie a part of the vein around it, and tighten it well, then remove the needle and place on the eye a wet cloth soaked with egg.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	 and leave it until the thread dissolves with the vein, then treat the eye with soothing things until the wound is healed.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And sometimes the wound is bound with wool on each side of a circle of cloth until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	 And if the eye appears to be badly infected, pierce it with a fine needle deep into the eye, and drain the cloudy liquid from the eye, and insert it immediately;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then withdraw it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	 from the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	 This disease called "alcunny" is nothing other than an inflammation that forms in the eye, resembling descending water, and it is not water.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	 And the manner of performing this work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take their head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the inflammation rise above your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	 Then let it be pierced, and do not descend, and let the light be dimmed, and let the patient see things as he used to;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 And if it does not descend below, know that it is acute, and if the descent of the wound is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	 Then make the patient sit between your hands, then take a thin spatula and pierce on the hardened tissue at the junction of the sclera with the scleral ring, until the wound exudes.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when it has exuded, then instill in the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that has been boiled and mixed with honey, and then let it be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	 of the eye's waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	 We have the likenesses of needles in the division, and those which are necessary for perforating;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 do it according to the healthiness.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	 You must make the patient sit between your crossed hands, out of the light from the sun, and bind the healthy eye very tightly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	 then put the eyelid of the affected eye in your left hand if it is the left eye, or in your right hand if it is the right eye.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	 then take in your right hand, if it is the left eye, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand, if it is the right eye.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	 then place the tip of the instrument near the cornea by the thickness of a ray in that white part of the eye towards the lesser tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" firmly and turn your hand until it perforates the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty space.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	 And it is necessary that the measure of the almond-shaped eye should be at the depth of the measure from the pupil to the end of the iris.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	 And this is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 You will see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the horny tissue, and then place the instrument where the water is, then press it under one eye after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If he has weak vision now, then the patient sees what is before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	 After resting for a while, and if the water rises in the second eye, place the finger with the instrument, and when it is inserted and does not rise, gently extract the almond by turning your hand little by little;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 And then put in a little bit of pure water, and leave the eye inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then apply outside the eye gauze or cloth soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg, and bind with healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 Now, and those who are of our time, apply a poultice with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	 And if Almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men who have eyes that are too hard, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	 And then pierce only the conjunctiva, do not go too deep, but make the place subtle, then put in aloes, as we have said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	 and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a warm pillow on which he can sleep on his back in a dark place.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	 and he should be still from all movements, and take light foods, and not move his head to the right or to the left, and let him rest according to his condition for three days.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	 then unbind him in that same dark room, and test his vision, and show him some things, and then bind him again until the seventh day.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 and it is not necessary for you to do this at the time of the treatment or immediately after the incision, but you should wait until later because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	 If an abscess comes to this, that you release the eye before the seventh day, and apply a remedy that soothes the abscess;
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 And when it is soothed, then release the eye and place on its face one gold coin to cover it for some days, and let it always be in that darkened room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	 And then go out of the house little by little, and turn back to its usual activities;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	 And one came to us who was from Jericho, who told us that in his country they make an almagda perciet, with which they draw water, but nevertheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I read about it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	 And perhaps this is something new.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	 And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	 and they should be made of brass properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	 And their heads should be of the same subtlety, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	 of the flesh upon the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	 Sometimes there are also various types of chariots, which is why some seem to have many feet like scorpions.
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 And there are such that they have a wagon engraved with red color, and there is also a smooth wagon of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	 In that wagon then, which is smooth and not engraved, you must have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	 and open his nostrils, and cast the unguent on those wagons, and draw them out.
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 Pour couper cela, soutiens avec un stylet subtil et aigu d'un côté, jusqu'à ce que tu saches que cette chair est entièrement coupée.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	 And if any part remains that cannot be cut, open it with all the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	 And if swelling or pus forms, then drain it as necessary;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	 And if it is a malignant abscess, then hasten and cauterize until the pus is dried up and all the flesh removed; then throw into the nose a mix of salt and vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	 If the nose drips, and moisture reaches the palate, know that he is healed;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	 And if moisture does not break through as it should, know that there is flesh born in the bone above, which prevents the instrument from coming to cut.
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	 Then it is necessary that you insert a little thick thread of linen, and let it be tied by hand, and have between each knot a finger's width or less.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	 And let the patient put the end of the thread in his nostril as best he can, and pull until it comes out through the mouth.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	 And many times children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 Then hold the end that comes out of the nostril with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and know each one after the other by feeling along the thread as we are in the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	 Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe off the blood, and wet the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nostril as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	 Do this for three days or more, until the ointment has dissolved all the remaining flesh.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	 and then put in the nostril a piece of lead for several days until it is healed, and if dry medicines are needed, use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 and this is the shape of the instrument for cleansing the head, into which one distills the oils and medicines into the nostril:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	 And let it be of silver or copper, resembling an open lamp, like a rod, and the tube likewise.
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	 and if you see, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full to cleanse the head.
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	 and have one handle at the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	 of the flesh upon the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	 Many times at the head of the nose a disease arises which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large often, so much that it is a visible thing to look at.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	 and because of this you must cut it at the beginning, and remove all the pus, then place on it the cautery or burning medicine.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	 and if one delays cutting it until it is large, then beware if it is hard, of dark color, and lacks sensation.
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	 do not touch it with iron, for it is an infected abscess, for when one cuts into it sometimes, great harm comes to the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	 And if the abscess is of a soft touch and not of fiery color, and you see that it can be entirely covered, then let the patient fast and cover the lancing without fear, and treat the place with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	 when the nose is cut and severed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 know that when the solution of continuity comes in one of these cartilage works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	 Therefore, when this happens to anyone, look to see if the wound is fresh in all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and then bring together the two lips with one stitch, and then treat it until it heals.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	 and if the lips have already separated from one side to the other, then it is necessary that you cauterize all the parts of their heart until they heal, then bring together the two lips with one stitch, and hold it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood and crushed incense on top.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And put on the powders a piece of emplastrum made of strong glue or other adhesive plaster, and let it stay until it falls off by itself, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	 The way to stitch is that you gather the skin together:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	 either with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	 or with thread, as I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	 of the lips' abscesses
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	 In many people, there are hard abscesses inside the lips, similar to peas, both smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	 then you must turn back the lips, and slice into each knot, and take with tweezers and cut into every part;
