puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 Then take lupin seeds after the vitriol incision, grind them until the blood is clotted.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then take flax seed oil, and cure the wound with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	 of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	 Many times there appears on the gums hardened flesh, which the ancients call "albulus".
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	 so you must hold it with tongs, and cut it at its root, and let the wound or blood flow.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	 then apply vitriol powder, or other astringent and drying powders, to the wound.
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	 And if that flesh returns after incision, which often happens, then cut it a second time and cauterize it.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	 If it does not return after cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	 And these are the forms of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	 of boils
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	 Sometimes they are gathered at the roots of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scabs that are unsightly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	 And sometimes the teeth turn black and yellowish green, until the decay reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	 Then you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be in your lap, and clean the teeth or scabs until nothing remains.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	 And do the same for the blackness and greenness, and the yellowness and other stains, until they are cleansed.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	 And if what is there at the first stage is removed, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	 If not, then begin again on the second day and the third, until you have all healed.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	 and know that the teeth require various types of instruments for healing, according to what the work shows, because the scrapers with which one cleans outside the teeth have other forms than those with which one cleans between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	 and let these forms and others be ready with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	 It is necessary that when you treat the tooth of its pain, you delay the extraction as long as you can, because one should not do this.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	 for it is a very high substance until such time that one has no excuse to extract it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Therefore, when the patient is forced to draw out the tooth, you must be certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	 Often the pain deceives the patient and he thinks it is in a healthy tooth, and has the good tooth extracted;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	 et yet the pain does not leave until the evil spirit is expelled, for we have already tried this with these sick people.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	 and when you are certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you burn around the tooth in every direction with strong cautery to protect the gum from all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	 then move it with your fingers or fine tweezers at the first knot and notch, until it is well loosened, then firmly secure the tweezers.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 and let the patient's head be between your knees, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 Aprés remove the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and push it gently into each side, and remove it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	 And if the tooth is decayed and hollowed out, you must fill it with cloth where the holes are.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	 And if you delicately hold it like tweezers, so that it does not break when pulling.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And it is necessary to work very wisely around the gum to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And take good care not to break it, and leave a part behind, and the patient will suffer greater pain than before due to the root’s malice.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	 And be careful not to act as do the ignorant surgeons, who through their haste and boldness sometimes break the tooth and do not achieve what we have described.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	 but they sometimes cause great illness due to the roots left behind or the broken tooth, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	 and when the tooth is removed, wash the area with wine or vinegar and salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	 and if blood continues to come out, which often happens, fill the area with powdered vitriol.
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	 The shapes of the instruments that one uses to first pull teeth should have long points and thick handles, so they do not bend when you pull out the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	 and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	 And let them be of thick metal so that they do not bend when pulling out, and let them be well-made iron, and let them have teeth to hold firmly.
de la racine des dens	 from the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	 When the root remains after pulling, you must put moistened cotton in butter on the place for one or two days until the spot is softened, then insert tweezers called "algefri," which make it look like a bird's beak;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 and inside they are made like a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pincers, then you must uncover the flesh completely around the root, and place there the instrument called "althali," which is actually pincers.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	 And let it be thick and strong so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with this, that is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	 If not, then use all the instruments, which are described below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	 And one helps oneself with this instrument which has two teeth, of which here is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	 and other irons that are in front for the reason of teeth, and with this instrument which looks like large pincers, of which here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	 And let this instrument be such that it cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	 and similarly, other instruments which are not counted here.
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	 and the wise and subtle master finds his own instrument by himself, according to what his works and the illness show him, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instruments due to their diversity. And if one breaks the cartilage or other bones, he should look for the necessary instruments that I have mentioned, and use the following gestures:  as shown in the figure below.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	 And let it be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, that it does not slip away, but can hold and remove it.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	 And then restore the place with appropriate medicines, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, then remove everything from this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	 When the teeth appear not according to nature, and their form is ugly, especially in virgin women, you must know if the tooth is new after a lost tooth, and is not in its proper place, and it cannot be filed or ground down.
adonques lou raie;	 Then draw it out;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	 And if it is attached to the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, and is made of iron, sharp at the end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	 And the claw bites little by little each day due to the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others; and if it is protruding such that it can be filed, then file it with a file like this form.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	 And it is like the limb from which needles are made;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	 And in the limb where the tooth pokes little by little each day, gently so that it does not move until it falls out;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	 then the plain at the end of all razors, and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, it is necessary to file down the roughness until it is even so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	 And when the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	 When the front teeth loosen, either by impact or by falling out, and the patient cannot chew what he eats without them falling out, and you have treated them with restricting medicines, and this does not work;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	 then they must be restrained with a gold thread, for the silver thread turns green and rots, but the gold never moves;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	 And let the wire be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	 And if you want to straighten the teeth, take the wire and double it between two healthy teeth, then put the pliers between the misaligned teeth, whether there is one or more, until you wisely reach the other healthy tooth.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	 Then begin the covering again from the part where you started, and gently and wisely tighten your hand until it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 And let your wire be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	 Then cut the wire from the pliers with shears and reassemble it, and put it between the healthy tooth so that it does not harm the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	 And then leave it tied tightly as long as it can stay, and if it comes undone or the thread breaks, tie it again with another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 if it stays and serves thus all its time, this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of two healthy teeth and two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	 And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, fresh by fresh, as we have said.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	 and let no one interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes a tooth is made from the bone of an ox, and it is placed where the gap is, and it is tied as we have said, and stays and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	 Of copper to the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	 Sometimes this ligament comes from under the tongue at birth.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	 or by accident of a closed wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	 and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your lap, and lift up the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	 then cut the nervous ligament from the wide part, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or a knot, and this is due to the sudden closure of the wound, then insert the hook and cut the ligament widely.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	 and be careful that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery beneath; xspace
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	 and when you have done this, raise the place with rose water and aloe, or cold water, then place a linen compress beneath the tongue;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 And the scabies should be treated by the patient every night, so that the place may not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	 And if bleeding continues, then apply ground vitriol to the place;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	 and if the blood is thin, then cauterize with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 then continue to care for it until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	 and if you see a dark or hard color, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	 and if it is inclined to turn black, and there is moisture, then apply onion juice, and make an incision with a subtle spatula, and release it from both sides;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	 And if your blood fails you in your work, apply a poultice of vitriol until it is stained, then return to your work until you draw out all the strength.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then lift up the place of ease and rest, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	 of the throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	 Sometimes there come into the throat certain ulcers called "godath," and they are properly called the two almonds. And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 If it is a hard abscess of small feeling and greenish color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also to prevent bleeding;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	 but let it be until it is ripe, and then you will separate it, lest it should burst of its own accord;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 and if it is of pale color again, and the root is delicate, then prepare the instrument to cut, but first look whether the hot abscess rests and is quieted.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	 Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his head be in your hand, and he open his mouth and you take the root between his hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument, which has this shape;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 and let it be of silver or fine brass as thin as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	 And when you have pressed the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take a hook and insert it into the almond, and draw strongly upward more than you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	 And pierce something through the cloth with it, then cut with the instrument, whose form resembles a forceps.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	 And nevertheless, the heads are curved and one against the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then use the tongs, which has this form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	 And let them be cutting on one side and notched on the other.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 And when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner. After the incision, gargle the patient with hot water and cold water and vinegar. If there is bleeding, then gargle the patient with water or boiled pomegranate rinds, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is healed.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then cure until he is healthy;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	 and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut them off in the same way as the two tonsils equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	 And I treated a woman of an abscess that was located within her throat, namely one small abscess;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 and it had almost completely closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had stayed like this for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two eyes through the two nostrils of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	 I hurried then quickly, and inserted in it one oncine [a small lancet], then drew out forcefully, and drew out a great portion of pus;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	 Then make another incision in the other nostril, and open the mouth and press the tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	 Afterwards, I inserted the probe into these abscesses and drained some of it, and only a little blood came out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	 And thus the woman's throat passage was opened up, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting away at that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	 And the abscess would always grow back and fill up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	 Then I cauterized it from within the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	 and thus it remained without growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 And I am separated from these parts, and let God make of them after me.
de l’uve	 of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	 When water descends into the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 And if it is below and thick and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	 When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that this abscess is calmed down, and it is subtle, then you must cut it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	 And that which is round and gathered together and is not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 And it is bloody or of a blackish color or black, then you must avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 Because there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	 Therefore, when you see it according to the manner I have said, of its whiteness and length, you must make the patient sit facing the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we have mentioned before;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it out from below, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	 And you must not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	 for if you cut more, then it will harm the voice and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of being cut, then it is necessary that you use anesthetic for the cauterization to reduce their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the manner of the cautery should be very sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	 And it is that the patient places his head in your hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and cauterize with hot, fresh water, neither too thick nor too thin.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And in the use of this instrument, which has the following form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	 And at its end is a lock where one places the medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	 And let the patient lie on his side so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine, so it does not descend to the throat or wound.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	 Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour until you see it moistened and the irritation from the medicine is soothed.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	 And if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton into the corner of the eye, so that the cotton dries on the eye.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	 And do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and it will fall off after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	 And if you need to repeat the cautery of the medicine, then repeat it, and after the cautery wipe around the ulcer with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And let it be rinsed with cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	 This treatment is more effective for incisions than the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	 if it is cured with fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and horehound and similar herbs, and gather all or some of them in one pot, and put asafetida in it, and boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	 And let the jar be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the jar there should be an instrument made according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	 And let it be made of silver or brass, and one of the heads should be inserted into the mouth of the patient until the vapors rise through the neck, until the vein is suppressed.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	 afterwards it is often repeated until the vein dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, because many things can happen.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And do not perform this unless at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	 And if this instrument is not present, then take a reed and insert into it the yolk of an egg, so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 for the head of an egg or milk does not allow the vapor to burden the mouth, and this is a good cure together with salt.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	 Many times something sticks in the throat like a bone or fishbone;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	 so it is necessary that you extract what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing move;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	 and that which does not open to you and is lodged in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	 perhaps it will expel the harsh thing through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	 or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a crumb of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	 And tie a thread to the sponge, then make it pass through.
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	 and when she comes to the place, she will harden, and then you will draw the hair;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	 and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument of lead in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	 And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it may enter the throat more easily, and have its tip raised up;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	 and take care not to touch the epiglottis, so that the entire throat does not swell, nor push a bone into it;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	 and it is better that the patient inserts the instrument himself, because he can feel where the thing is difficult;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	 If the bottle is empty, or if he draws strongly with all of the instrument equally, until it is strong.
de la sansue de la gorge	 from the blood of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	 Anytime bloodletting is performed, as I have said in the section on divisions, by means of medical treatment;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 And when this does not benefit at all, then look into the patient's throat in the sunlight, after you have pressed the tongue to the instrument that I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 Et si tu vois la sangsue, alors traie-la avec une très petite aiguille, ou des pinces fines qui conviennent à cela.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if this does not work, take a horsehair and place it in the patient's throat, then put a hot iron at the end of the hair, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if the patient has a fever all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	 Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without choking, and move it around in his hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 And as soon as the blood feels the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	 And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the instrument that I have mentioned in the section on fumigating the eye;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 Do this many times, for she will fall without hesitation.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	 And the manner of the fumigation is such that you take a pot in which there are live coals, and let the lid be covered with a perforated cloth in the middle, and through that hole place the head of the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	 then cast your fumigation, and the patient should place the end of the reed in his mouth, and close his mouth so that no smoke escapes, but let it go down to the lungs.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	 and then the phlegm will fall now, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	 and let the patient be thirsty, and chew on salty things and such, and do not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And then he will need to come out by this rule.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	 And the shape of the instrument with which one draws blood is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved pincers for entering into the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	 and let it have the appearance of a sparrow's beak, and let it have the roughness of a file, so that what it takes, it cannot leave behind;
et vez ci la forme:	 and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	 the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	 Many appearances of abscesses are, according to the memories that come hereafter in this book, one and another, and they differ in perforation and cutting;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 and it is in two ways, one of which is in its appearance itself, and that which holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is according to the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 because the abscess of the head is different from that at the base, and the abscess of the fleshy place is different from that which comes in the joints, and each should be judged accordingly in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	 And so with abscesses that one must not pierce, until the boil is dead according to its course;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And so with those that one must pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their course, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 Because when an abscess comes near the joints and it is left until it is purulent around, it may happen that the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	 Or if the abscess is near the principal member, and you delay the piercing until it is dead, it will harm the principal member.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	 Or if it is near the fundament, one should pierce it as soon as it is ripe;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	 And one must not pierce a ripe abscess without completed digestion, except for those near the fundament, lest it putrefy within, and become inflamed inside, and a fistula develop.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 And it cannot heal within a short period of time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	 And it is necessary that you know the hour of the maturation of the abscess according to its completion, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of the fever, and the diminution of the pain and redness, and the softening and the improvement of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	 And it is necessary that you make the incision sit in the most dependent part of the abscess, and where it opens moves;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	 And let the incision be long along the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in the joints and near the nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no folding.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 En those that bend, according to this limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you leave the opening until it is confirmed by completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	 Because if you pierce it before this, the body will be elongated by the venom from it, and it is full of much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 And perhaps it will harden the lips and deepen them with it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if any abscess is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb needs from it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	 And it is necessary that you bring forth in small abscesses, small openings;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	 and in large abscesses, large openings, and many slits according to the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	 And if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to remove the core and cover it;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	 When they become old like cloths, and are dead, then one must do as one does with boils:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	 And if there are such that are split into three corners, and some that one cuts like the leaves of myrtle, as boils of the corners.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And if there are such [conditions] when one makes a circular incision, and other incisions and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	 Those who have no head, as with a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it fully;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	 And when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at once in that hour, but draw out part of it;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	 Then plug the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more again;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	 do this many times from large to small, until all the pus comes out.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Similarly if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old feeble men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit may sometimes jump out with the issue of the pus, which could accidentally kill the patient, and you would not notice.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	 Avoid this chapter with great caution. When you have perceived your abscess, then clean the wound, and look to see if the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	 And if it is a deep cut, then apply linen or old cotton bandages.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	 And if it is a large abscess and there are many openings, then you must insert a bandage into each one so that they meet each other.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	 And if you have cut into the abscess a piece of leather and you have wrapped it around, then you must fill it with old cotton or scraps of linen without moisture, and bind it until the third day.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, then bring cold and easy water, and moisten the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	 Et si le saignement persiste, administre un traitement et des soins appropriés, ainsi que les poudres dont j'ai parlé dans ce livre. Si cela se produit pendant l'hiver, et que la zone de l'abcès est très nerveuse, il faut appliquer des tentes et des draps humides avec du vin et de l'huile chaude.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	 et si cela se produit en été, et que la zone est charnue, il faut appliquer des draps humides avec de l'eau et de l'huile, ou du vin et de l'huile froide, pendant trois jours, comme nous l'avons dit.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 et ensuite, incise l'abcès, essuie-le et soigne-le comme il convient, jusqu'à ce qu'il guérisse.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	 And this is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	 and as I have told you how one should proceed in the treatment of abscesses, see here the chapter.
des soros	 de soros
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 When the veins of the head cause small abscesses, and they are like those that are in tissues, similar to the pouch of a chicken, there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	 There are those that are fat and such where there is moisture like poultices;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 and there are those that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the surgeon does not make a mistake.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of cutting is such that you should try any instrument that is called an "entromissoire," which causes the shape to come hereafter, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 Car if it contains moisture, then open it from above the long [bone].
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	 And when the moisture is emptied, scrape off without leaving anything the skin that contains this moisture, because it returns immediately if one leaves something there;
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	 then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	 if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And this will happen to those who remain in the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	 And then resume cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know well that it does not remain in the night;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then treat the wound with ointment according to what is suitable, until he is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	 And if the abscess holds the night oil, cut it according to this form, lengthwise;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	 and put your claws in it, and skin it all around, and put all your effort into drawing the coat where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the art [or craft] makes you uncomfortable, do as I have told you afterward.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And do the same for a pustular abscess, in cutting and cleaning as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cut above the pustular and moist abscess, for it is lighter because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	 And if there is one of these abscesses in the head where there is no moisture, and it is like the abscess that I cut on the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	 And I found the abscess like a deaf stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if one had struck it, one would have made as much of a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	 In other abscesses that come to the head, except for those that come to the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should always be in the most dependent place, so that the pus may exit;
et les cure si com il covient.	 And treat them as is necessary.
des scrophules	 from scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 These abscesses often occur in the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and there are many of them, interconnected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	 And each scrofula is properly inside its rib, like the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And the likenesses of these scrofulae are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and there are also malignant ones that do not want to obey healthiness.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	 And then in that which you see of good disposition to touch, and it is similar to the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not harsh to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery or duct, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	 then you must cut above it, and scrape each part, and stretch the two lips of the heart with tweezers if needed, as we have said in the case of head abscesses.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 and draw it out little by little, and be sure not to cut the nerve or vein, and let the instrument not be sharp or cutting, lest the hand slip, and do not go too far forward, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	 And if you cut the vein or artery, and this prevents you from working, then place in the wound vitriol paste, or some powder that stanches blood, and tighten the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And leave it there until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to fester.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	 And when the blood is stanchioned, return to your work until you complete it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 Then inquire at your fingertip if there remain any small scrofula, and cut them off and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, then it is not proper for you to cut this scrofula at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself, without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 Then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut the entire scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound, and stitch them now, since no excess remains due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 so it is necessary that you take care to cut the root of it, and pull strongly, and stitch as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	 Those scrofula that hold excess, pierce there where it appears dark;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	 and pierce it in the same way as was said before, hanging downwards, then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the wound is well cleaned, dress it with healing ointment until it heals.
de squinance	 of a splint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	 The ancients spoke and discussed the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	 but I have never seen anyone in our land who has done it, and this is a record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	 For those with stridor, the split in the throat called "epiglottis" must be cauterized;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	 And that no aid is given through this, because all the veins and the flesh of the patient are hot with abscess in the mouth or throat or both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	 When the illness is in the tonsil channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid death from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	 Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it between three or four small transverse slits, between two circles, or by the amount of the cartilage slice;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 and the patient is suitable for cutting the epiglottis if there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	 And if the master is fearful, he must extend the skin of the throat to the very end, then cut the heart until it reaches the chin.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	 And pour out the vessels of blood, if you see anything, then cut off the sinew, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	 And it is demonstrated by the cutting of the phlegm from the brain which escapes strongly through the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	 And when the time has passed in which strangulation is feared, join the two lips of the heart wound, and sew it all alone without any padding.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely stuffed, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect is healed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	 Then cut off the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is preserved from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	 And therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease had passed, and it passes in three days or four. Then they commanded to close the wound and heal it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	 I saw that a maiden took a knife and thrust it into her throat, cutting part of the cartilage of the larynx.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 And I was called to heal her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	 I revealed the wound, and found the blood that had come out of it, although it did not pierce a vein or a large artery except for the throat, and the wind was coming out strongly through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	 I hastened and sewed the wound, and healed it until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	 And nothing happened to the maiden except that she lost her voice, which later returned to its original state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 for this reason, I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis, there shall not be fear.
de la grosse gorge	 of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	 this abscess is called "goiter," and it is a large abscess the color of a sloe, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	 and it occurs in two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	 naturally, and accidentally;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 or naturally, there is no humor present.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	 And the accidental [type] is in two ways, of which one is similar to our fat, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	 and there is fear [of operating], and it should not be done by fire, except in the small one, and test and search throughout the entire [affected] area; 
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	 If you find it thus as we know from fat, and it cannot be bled by any vein, then cut it, like one cuts the nose, and draw all its hair, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And bind well immediately, and treat it as needed until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	 of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	 There are many types of noses, from which I will describe all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 and now it is necessary that I speak about all the differences that exist between a nose and an ulcer.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	 I say that an ulcer is hot and feverish as long as the inflammation lasts, and the pus has matured;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	 then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	 With the nose there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains the syfac, which is its own sack and corresponds to the body's color, and begins like a little bag, and grows. ‌
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 And they are according to two likenesses, either fat or moist, and of many colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	 Il convient, quand tu viens à la cure du nœud, que tu éprouves et enquêtes d'abord de tout l'instrument qui est appelé «entromissoire», selon ce que sa forme sera dans le chapitre suivant.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	 And the manner of the examination of abscesses for us is that you take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has perceived the heart, then according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 then draw out the probe, and be careful in this, lest it should jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	 If running moisture occurs, whatever color it has, then pierce it as I have said about other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	 and if after the probe comes moisture, know that it is fat, then pierce it in a cross shape, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape from each side and beware of the coat where it lies, so that you draw it out whole with the knot;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 And if you cannot remove it whole, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	 For if anything remains, the injury returns many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if even a little remains and the wound troubles you, then fill the wound with some corrosive and hot herbs, hold the wound tight, apply soothing things to the abscess, keep it warm, and care for it with other remedies until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 And if the wound is large, sew together the two lips of the wound, and care for it as one would for a flesh wound.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	 And if the beating of the veins is against you or something else, then hurry and fill the place with crushed vitriol, and leave it there for two days or three, until the wound putrefies and the boiling of the blood ceases.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	 Then return to the copper what remains of the nut.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	 Behold here are the forms of the intromissory instruments, and they come in three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	 large, medium, and small.
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	 And there are three quarters which are called "albarets," and one that is called "breb," and they come in three kinds.
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	 large, medium, and small, to enclose the abscesses of fistulae.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	 And they are like the needles used to sew sorcerers, and they are made of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver. Those that are yellow in color are worth more, and those blackened with lead are better suited for enclosing the scabs of fistulae;
et sont de III manieres:	 And there are three types:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 large, medium, and small, according to the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	 The shapes of the nails are very diverse, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	 large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	 And there are nails that have two curves of three types as well;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	 And there are also nails with three curves, which are of three types.
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	 And there are also nails with two curves, and single-curved nails, all of which come in three types.
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 And all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	 The heads of these tools are sharp, and some do not cut more than from one side, with which we scrape the nails so that we do not cut the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	 And of these intrusions are the amputated hands, so that the patient does not notice them at the opening of abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	 and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	 great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	 and one should not use them except in fleshy places, such as the legs, arms, breasts, and the groin, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling the scrapings of pus, in this form, with which one stops bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	 And it is placed sometimes in the location that heals quickly at the veins and the arteries, and sometimes according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	 Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much so that they resemble women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 And they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must follow this form of these lines from b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 Then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with meat-enhancing medicine; then sew together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	 And if the nipple sags downward and is made thin by its size, as happens to women, then make two cuts above it, through two similar openings.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	 so that one is attached to the other at the end of each, making the larger line contain the smaller one according to this form, from this line b to this line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then peel off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for the treatment, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	 And if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely done, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood loss, you must fill the wound with dampened cotton and caustic ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 And leave it until it dissolves the rest and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	 of the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	 These abscesses that come under the armpits are hard like scrofula with ribs, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those that contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat it with ointment appropriate for this purpose until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if the abscess is like scrofula, then cut it as we have said for cutting scrofula, and if the wound discharges pus, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	 of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	 When the articular surface is damaged and the skin above it is healed, it often results in abscesses, and similarly, an inflamed vein can cause abscesses.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	 And if one recognizes it thus when it is due to the artery, then the abscess is long in depth.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	 and when you feel it with your fingers, you sense a tightening;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	 and when it is due to the vein, then the reason is clearly apparent.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and in the groin and in the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	 Therefore, it is necessary to avoid the iron cure, and that which is on the head should also be avoided, and in that which is from a swelling of the artery, make an incision above the skin along its length.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	 then cut the flesh as usual, and separate the artery beautifully from the tissues until it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	 Then insert below it a needle, and make it pierce to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	 then prick the place that is between the two ligatures with a lancet until the pus comes out, and let the abscess be relieved;
