puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	 then prepare the dressing as I have shown you, until the ligature falls off.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then treat it with an ointment afterwards, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	 And if the abscess is as large as the vein, then it is necessary that you hold in your hand whatever you can of the abscess all the way to the skin, then insert the needle below the place that you are holding in your hand, and make it pierce, and there should be a double thread, so that you pull it out from the other side. 》
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	 Then bind the abscess, as I have told you, with a thread on one of the two parts to the two shoulders.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	 And if you doubt that the thread might come loose, then sew another needle through all of the first thread below the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	 Then cut the abscess until the pus comes out, then cut the pus from the core and leave what is tied.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then place a cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply dressings of lint and onion until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	 of the abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	 Just like abscesses come in the artery and vein, so too they come in the nerves when they are pierced, or by excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	 And this happens most often in the shoulders and the thighs, and in all places where there are joints, and these are serious abscesses, and their color resembles that of flesh, and it is in many positions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	 And when one pulls it strongly, the patient feels pain, which is not entirely in the body, but below the heart.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	 And it moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor below or above, and those in the joints should not be struck with iron.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	 Perhaps there will be contracture.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And those that are on the head or on the forehead, break the skin with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	 If the abscess is small, hold it with pincers and cut into its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it is large, suspend it on the nail of the little finger and skin it, then remove it and close the wound with stitches, and care for it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	 of hanging swellings
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	 Sometimes it happens in bellies and not elsewhere, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, with subtle roots and a large head.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	 And there are some that are small and others that are very large;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 And I have seen in a man who had two in his belly that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were always wet with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	 I cut them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces and the other six, and the work in the incision is such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the tumor is white and moist and has fine roots;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 If the wound is wide at the shoulder blade, and there is a fire cautery in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	 For in cutting, blood often flows too abundantly, and if the bleeding overcomes you, then hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	 And if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made thread of linen, and tie it around the wound as we have said, and leave it for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	 And then tighten it, and do not stop pulling the linen thread until it cuts through the wound, and thus it heals without pain.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	 And if the roots are large, there is fear to cut directly into the abdomen, but you can safely cut halfway, then cauterize so it does not return.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 then heal the wound, and be careful not to cut the skin that is of fiery color and poor sensation and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	 Because this is an embedded carbuncle, and I will come to the treatment of carbuncles afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	 when the abscess has become hot
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	 If the swelling of the wound comes from the cautery of a wound or cleft in the intestine, and it is on the belly and goes to some of the bladders, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries as mentioned above, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 and if it is from the rupture of the intestine and the exiting of the bladder, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens in various ways.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	 And if it is due to the outlet of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with two fingers, it returns to its place, and then comes back, and perhaps it will become hard, and swells greatly at the entrance of the bath and due to strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, but does not constrict;
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	 And if it is due to blood, the abscess will be large and hard, and will have a fixed size.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to gas, it will be soft to the touch, and the operation is such that you should look to see whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery or a vein, or gas.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 Therefore, you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 Because there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	 And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the belly, then you should instruct the patient to lift his leg and be stretched out straight, then press all around the stomach.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	 Then have him lie down gently between your hands, then go around the place you have marked with all the spatula, then extend half of the abscess upwards with the whole large incision.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	 Then tie around it with a strong thread or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the knot be secure.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	 Then work on half of the abscess spread out over the cord, and insert your index finger, and search for the intestines.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	 If you find it caught in the cord, then free it, and push the intestine out of the stomach;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	 And if you find the swelling, then take it with tweezers, and cut off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	 And if the artery opposes you or the vein, then go around it carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two fine threads, and insert the two needles around what you have done in a cross that you made pierce.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	 Then hold the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the place until it turns black, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	 And cut it when it is softened and blackened, then treat the wound as needed, and remove the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And drain the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound as needed, and heal the wound.
dou chancre	 of the cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	 We have said in the section on the similarities of cancer, and how one should work with medicines, and how to avoid the use of iron.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	 And we say that cancer begins in the flesh, and great care is needed in the treatment, and the ancients said that when cancer is in a place where it can be scraped off, such as cancer in the breasts, and in the thighs, and similar places, and one should remove all of it when it is at the beginning;
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	 And when it is large and old, then you must not approach it, for I have never been able to heal any.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	 nor has anyone ever healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	 And the work, when it is in such a place that it can be removed, as we have said, is that you first purge the patient of black bile;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	 then let him fast if he has an obvious fullness, then place the patient in a good position to perform the work;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	 then throw away your clippers and cautery iron, and remove all hair from all around it, leaving nothing behind;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 and let the blood flow freely, and press well on the area with your hand or some other thing, and if the flowing of blood hinders you from making the incision in the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal him with another treatment until he is healed.
de ydropisie	 Of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	 We have already said in the division the similarities of hydropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the treatment that is done with medicines, and that which is treated with iron:
si est eclites soulement;	 it is only an eclipse;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	 and one should not use iron in these two similarities:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	 that is to say, tympanitis and hippuritic swelling, because they are deadly things;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	 therefore when you treat this similarity of hydropsy which is called "eclipse" with medicines, and the treatment does not benefit, then look to see if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides hydropsy, such as a burst belly and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	 If you do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	 And if you see the patient of great strength, and he has no other illness except dropsy alone, and is not too young nor too old, then you should act as follows:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 Lay the patient flat on his back in your hands, and have an assistant press on the abdomen just below the ribs, then take the spiny spatula according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	 with a point, but nevertheless it should not be so long that when inserted it could reach the intestines and cause injury;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	 Then check if the dropsy has spread towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	 If so, you must cut open three fingers wide straight down to the groin;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	 And if the dropsy is due to liver disease, let your incision be on the left side of the navel three fingers' width.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	 And if it is due to the spleen, let it be on the right side. And it is not necessary that the patient lie on the incision so that the excesses do not flow to that weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	 Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and discharge it, and lift your hand to the entire subcutaneous tissue between the skin and the fascia just as in scraping to the thickness of a nail or thereabouts.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 Then pierce the fascia until the subcutaneous tissue reaches the desired place, which is the watery area. Then draw it strongly, and into this place insert this instrument, the form of which is as follows:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	 And it is similar to a fine silver chain, and it is made of light brass or copper, and has in its lower part a small hole.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	 and on one side there are three holes.
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	 and two on the other side, and one on another.
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision which the scribes cut into the quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	 at the top there is a small handle, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it will immediately rise above the water.
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	 empty then half or a third of it, because if you empty more than is necessary at that time, perhaps the patient will die from the loss of spirit from the weapon, or he will fall unconscious, or he will approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	 But according to its emptiness, according to its power, according to what the patient's constitution indicates, and his pulse;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	 Then withdraw the instrument and hold the water, which is now held by the kerf that stops up the hole on the syphac, as I have mentioned, that you should pierce in this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	 then resume the instrument the next day, if you see the patient tolerating this, and draw out a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 do this every day, and be careful not to empty it all but leave only a little bit of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	 And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave much water in them, then treat with burial or hot sand, and by much sweating or bathing in the sun, and let them drink wine.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And the treatment with drying medicines until it is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	 of the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 Then it should be pierced as soon as possible with a very fine needle in this manner:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	 Then put in the opening a thin cloth of linen, and tie it and hold it thus for three days or four. And when he wants to make water, let the cloth be removed, and make water, and then replace it.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 And perhaps it is not necessary, because the water that comes forth does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 He whose opening is small, let him be treated with a lead weight as we have said, so that it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	 Those who do not have the opening in its place are afflicted, because some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, which prevents them from urinating before they lift their penis upwards;
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 And cannot heal because the matter cannot reach the bone, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	 And the manner of working is that the patient lies on his back, then stretch the head of the member and the foreskin like the width of a quill, so that the hole is in the middle, as it should be;
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And beware of bleeding that often occurs there, and if it happens, staunch it as one staunches blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	 of the boils of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	 Often these baths come to the member, and it is an appearance of ugly flesh;
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	 And there are malignant and non-malignant ones;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	 if it is necessary that you take them at one time subtly, and cut and clean all of them, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment on top
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then continue the treatment with fine-tuning ointments until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the abscess is malignant, with foul color and odor, then you must bring a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	 When you have cut it, and if the plant is partially inside the vein and partially outside, then you must first remove the part that is inside.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 And when it is joined together, then treat the outer part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	 Because when you treat them together, the head of the vein is not assured to not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come into the vein and in the flesh.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then you must cut away all that is black and corrupt, then apply a plaster made of honey, flour, pomegranate rind, and beans, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cautery as follows:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	 The cautery helps with two conditions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	 that is to say, for the flow of blood and for corruption.
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	 And if the head of the bladder is corrupt and retracted, then you must insert a cane made of pine into the bladder's channel, and let the patient urinate through it.
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	 And when the hair is adherent to the head of the bladder, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, due to a wound or an abscess, then you must scrape it off with one sharp instrument until the tissue is loosened and the head of the bladder is freed on all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	 And if it is difficult to scrape this away, then you must burn it off with a hot spatula at the head of the bladder and the skin.
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 Then cut well between two (joints), and place one subtle linen cloth soaked in cold water, that it does not dry again.
de la circoncision	 Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	 Circumcision is not a separation of continuity like other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	 however, when we perform this work of our own will, especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best and lightest work for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	 I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they do not practice it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	 For I have seen most of the masters and surgeons who perform circumcisions do it around the penis, on the foreskin, and on the entire glans.
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	 if the skin is cut because there are two layers, and perhaps one cuts the upper layer and leaves the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	 And there it swells up, and the pain is doubled, and at the end of the day, the point of the limb is not secure.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	 and at the incision of the nail perhaps the iron will slip away, and the work will be ruined, and many times it happens that they do not need an incision, and I want it to be so.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	 Of the amputation that is done at the joints, I have found the benefit of the experiment, for the scissors cut equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	 Because when you press your hand, cut equally in all your strength.
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	 but let the thread be well tightened around the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	 and the manner of the first operation is such that you make the child, if he understands, think that you are not doing anything to him but tying a thread around the wand, and then let him rejoice in all the ways you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	 then make it stand upright between your hands, and respond to the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments;
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	 then put your hand on the stick and blow into the heart, and pull it up until the head of the stick is inside;
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	 then clean it well from the gathered dirt, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it under the pocket to another ligature;
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	 and hold it with the two fingers of the second ligature at the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two ligatures, then lift the heart quickly and pull out the head of the stick;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	 then let the blood flow little by little, for it is the cure.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And put powder on it and on the powder a cloth stuck with a little of egg white cooked tempered with rose water, infused with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and treat it again until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	 The form of the plaster for cleansing is as follows:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	 both ends must be sharp and equal in size.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	 the mistake of cleansing is when the heart within is at the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	 therefore you must spread it with your finger before the place forms an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	 and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with tweezers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	 And if they exceed three days, and that which is below the penis is swollen, leave it until the abscess is appeased, and lightly skin it.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	 If you can move the head as you please, and be careful of the part of the penis, it will not harm him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	 Then cure the place with a sudorific wound powder, as we have said in treating powders, and if the head goes beyond measure and moves upward, it will not harm;
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	 of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	 The retention of urine is due to a stone, or frozen blood, or bone, or dead flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	 And if the urine is not released, and you see that it is retained due to the stone which is in the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	 And let his feet be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the upper part of the back, and the patient should hold himself upright as much as he can.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	 And then the neck of the bladder is constrained to push out the stone from above, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	 And if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument that is called "syringe," of which this is the form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	 And let it be of fine silver, lightly hammered, like the feather of a bird.
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 And let the chain be one and a half handspans long, and let it be thin at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	 And the manner of urine evacuation is such that you take a double thread, tie a wool or cotton bag at one end, and put the thread end into the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	 and trim the excess wool and insert it into the syringe until the end, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and yolk of egg, and make the patient sit on a chair, and raise his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	 Then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis back towards the scrotum.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	 Then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and the patient will feel it until it reaches an empty space, and this is not done correctly unless because the passage through which it passes is twisted.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	 Then stretch the thread all along the wool strand by strand, and the urine will follow the wool, then extract it firmly, and make the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And repeat with the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	 of the illnesses of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	 When there are scabs or blood in the bladder, or an accumulation of pus, and you introduce water and medicine, do this with all the instrument called "clepsedra," and it is shaped like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	 It is closed, and has three holes:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	 Two on one side, and one on the other, as you see.
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	 And let the leather chosen for the surgeon's purse be such that it stops the tube well without additional material, so that one can draw out the moisture and insert when needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	 And when you place your medicines in the bladder, put the head of the funnel into the moisture and draw what is inside.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	 Thus you will draw out the moisture with the funnel, then strongly reinsert the drawn tube.
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	 Then the moisture will enter inside and go to the bladder immediately, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	 And this is the form of a subtle enema by which one enemas the bladder.
si est ci:	 Here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	 It is made of silver or copper and its head is higher.
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	 And under the breast where the chain falls.
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	 Then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in it that you wish to enema the bladder with, then tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and warm this moisture on the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	 Then insert the head of the enema into the penis, then press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has entered, so that the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	 And if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment and make it into a circle, and pierce it all around.
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	 Then insert a strong thread through these holes, then close the circle like one closes a basket, and put inside what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument.
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And do as you did with the bladder, press to your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	 of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	 We have already said in the division the types of stone and their extraction along with medications;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	 And I have spoken about the difference between the rain-inflicted stone and all its signs, and in which stone one should work by cutting;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	 and in the bladder, and in the penis.
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	 and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	 I say that the stone which is inflicted in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the water from the bladder resembles water in its subtlety;
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	 and it excretes sand, and it causes the patient to urinate blood, and he frequently urinates, and then becomes paralyzed.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	 And to many of these jumps the foundation.
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	 And healing is swift in children until they are four years old, and it is very serious in the elderly, and it is of moderate difficulty for those who are between youth and old age.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	 And the treatment is easier for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with a clyster, in order to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes interferes with seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	 Then take the patient by the feet and bend him back and forth so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and sometimes comes out from above.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	 Then let him sit between your prepared hands, with his hands under his thighs so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	 Then seek and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 If you feel the stone within, then hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	 And if it does not fall upon touching the whole of it, then moisten your finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adult.
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	 and place it in his rectum, and seek for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, draw it up to the neck of the bladder.
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 then press with your finger upon it, and draw it out at the place where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	 And command the attendant to press upon the bladder with his hand, and order him to raise his right testicle with his hand, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the testicles in the place where the cut is made.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	 puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	 Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	 et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; ›
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	 par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	 et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:
si est griés a issir;	 It is necessary to go out;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And if it is under, similar to a bulge and round, its exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	 For that one, therefore, where there are angles and edges, make the cut larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	 And if it does not jump out, then you must pull with tweezers that are like a file at the top, to strongly pull the stone so that it does not escape;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	 Or you put under it a subtle curved instrument at the tip;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	 And if you cannot trick it this way, then widen the pouch where the hole is, and if the vein tears, then pinch it with a caustic.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 And if there is more than one stone, first insert the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut on it, then draw it out strongly, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, it must be sewn, and a larger wound must be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	 Because two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	 either he dies, or the urine always comes from there where the wound cannot heal;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	 but nevertheless you must strive to draw it out, or to break it with pincers, until you remove it piece by piece;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	 and when you have completed your work, then fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it, and put on top a moistened cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 then lay the patient on his back, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you dislocate it, wash very well the place with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of diafincaon and ointment of basilicaon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	 And if such abscesses and corrosions come to the wound, and blood clots in the bladder, causing the urine to be retained in such a manner that it does not pass with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	 Pour in the wound, then draw out that blood, because if it remains, it will run to the bladder and cause putrefaction.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then lift the wound with water and vinegar and oil, and help him in all the ways that you know, until he is healed.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 and it is necessary that every time you treat him, you bind the two thighs together, and place the medicines on the spot.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	 And if the stone is small, and it is in the duct of the penis, and stuck inside, so that the urine cannot come out.
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 then the treatment that I have mentioned before, which you cut many times, is excused from cutting in this case.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already proven it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	 Take a rod of iron according to this shape, and let there be three sharp points on one end:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	 Then take a thread and tie it around the rod under the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	 then put the punch in the rod lightly, until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	 and turn the punch in your hand in the stone little by little, so that you can pierce the stone from the other side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 then the urine will come out, and press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	 Then it is immediately broken, and it jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	 and if you cannot do this due to any obstacle, then tie a thread under the stone and another one on top, then bend the rod at the stone between the two ties, then pull hard, and untie the thread, and clean the frozen blood that is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and the treatment until he is cured.
de la piere des femmes	 of the woman's stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	 It sometimes happens that a stone becomes lodged in women, and if it does happen, the treatment is difficult. It is forbidden for three reasons:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	 one reason is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	 and the second reason is that one cannot find a skilled woman who will expose herself to the doctors, especially when she is virtuous.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	 And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a skilled woman in this hand-based art;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	 and the fourth way is that the stone in a woman is more deeply embedded than in a man, which requires a deeper cut, and it is very frightening. And if necessity demands it, you should seek a skilled midwife, and they are rarely found, and if you cannot find one, then look for a skillful and subtle chaste doctor;
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	 And it presents a wise midwife with experience in women's lives, or a woman who knows some of the art, and instructs her to do what you command regarding the investigation of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	 and looks very carefully if the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	 then she must insert her finger into the anus and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 and if she finds it, she constrains it under her finger, and recommends that she insert her finger into the vagina of the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand strongly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	 If she finds it, she must move it bit by bit from the entrance of the bladder downwards until it reaches the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	 then cut into the stone on the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the knee, in the place where it is convenient to operate, and feel the stone in that area.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	 and do not move your finger on top of or below the stone, and make the first cut small;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	 then press the reed into the cut, if you feel the stone narrow the wound until the stone can come out forcefully; and know that there are many types of stones.
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 that is to say, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and with furrows;
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 If you know the similarities in order to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 And if the blood flows profusely, then apply ground vitriol to the place, and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	 then return to your work until the stone is strong, and have the instruments that I have told you about for extracting stones in men to help you in your work;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	 and if the blood overcomes you, and it is from an artery that has been cut, then place powder on the spot and compress with bandages and cloths, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, for fear the patient may die.
puis cure la plaie.	 then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	 And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the place becomes cool, return to your work until the stone is weakened.
de hernie carnouse	 of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	 Ramic acid is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white syrup that is beneath the heart of the testicles, which contains the semen.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	 and it is called "syrup," and sometimes it is properly in the fabric of the semen, so that one might think it is another egg.  /> and when this occurs, it should not be done, but rather left alone to avoid harming the patient.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	 And this is the leather of the egg between the white as we have said.
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	 And this does not happen if it is not a pox.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	 And the formation of this collection comes from weakness in the kidneys, and that matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	 And sometimes it comes from bruising on the eggs, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	 or it is a yellowish color, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens most often.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 and these are the signs to recognize this collection, because if it is in the white as we have said, the abscess is reasonable, the pox long like the shape of an egg, and the egg does not open, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	 And if there is moisture in the very fabric, then the abscess is reasonable with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	 And if the moisture is between the skin of the eyelids and the white surface, one feels it well.
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 Therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, test all the surrounding area, from which its form comes before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	 According to what follows the probe, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	 And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be bled according to our ability and the fullness of his body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	 then place him on his back, on something a little high, and put many blankets under him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	 Then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on his right, and extend the rod along one of the two ribs beneath the corner of the eye.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	 Then take the spatula, and cut the skin of the eyelid lengthwise from the long part down to near the corner, and let your incision be straight in dividing the skin of the eyelid until the white surface, and delicately peel it according to your ability.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	 Then pierce the sponge full of water through a large hole, and drain all the water, and then put your fingers, and swell the sponge upwards;
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	 And do not touch the heart of the kidneys, but only the sponge.
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	 Cut all or in pieces, however, the sponge very carefully, that if you do not cut it well and wisely, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	 And if the sponge jumps too much at your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the sponge's work.
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then sew the two leaves of the kidney heart together with one stitch, then heal it as you would other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	 And if you find the egg corrupt with another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flow of blood;
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	 then cut the skin all around the suspended area, and remove the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	 And if water is collected in two parts together, know that these are two veins;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	 then cut the other part in the same way you did the first one, then wipe off the blood, and put a cloth moistened in rose oil on the wound;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 and put another cloth moistened in wine and oil on top of the two skins, and put double-layered cloths on top of that, and bind it all together with all the bindings as shown in this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	 Then take two cloths, and fill them with wool in the following manner, and they should be sewn together at the waist of the breeches, and one of the ends should extend from the buttocks to the back, and the other to the elbow part;
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	 and the other two ends on the two angles, and let all the assembly be restricted in the belt loop;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	 and sometimes this bandage is used in place of an iron caustic, and it is that you take a delicate cautery blade, cut the skin of the testicles, and heat it as we have said, so that the white surface containing water is exposed.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 then take the cautery in this manner, and pierce that surface at the testicles, and scrape it with this hot delicate blade.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	 Et pour couper dans toutes les manières que tu peux, autant que tu puisses.
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	 And ensure that the fire does not touch the eye;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	 and know that this work is safer;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	 and avoid excessive bleeding, and be aware of the operations for cutting.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And if anything goes wrong, such as an abscess or excessive bleeding or something else, then treat what is going wrong, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	 And if the patient is frightened and does not wish to undergo this operation because of its horror, then you should make a perforation, as I tell you. It is that when you are certain through the signs that we have mentioned that aquous humor is there, then let the patient sit on a high seat;
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	 Punch through the abscess at the base, all around as wide as possible, and place the puncture along the length of the body.
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	 And let the openings be wide so that all the pus flows freely;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	 Then place cotton on the spot, and bind it, and let the remaining pus flow out. Once the wound is healed, treat it until the wound is clean.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	 And if the white cloth does not allow the pus to flow out of the wound's mouth, then you must insert a feather or an instrument used to draw water from hydropics, as described earlier.
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And widen the opening of the wound, and know that the pus will return, and it will gather again after six months or thereabouts, and when it gathers like before, the patient will pass his days thus.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	 You should know that in cutting this vein, there is fear in many situations, which is why it seems better to leave it alone.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 and I will tell you the work and similarities of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	 I say therefore that many abscesses come in the body, especially in the joints;
et c’est par mout de cas.	 and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	 This is to say, from an excess of acid or acute humors that spread to the joints, either from a blow; ‌
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	 and the color of the abscess varies according to the color of the body.
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	 and if there is no pain, the abscess is serious.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 and sometimes an abscess is dangerous and painful, with a red color, and sometimes it comes from a nodule of artery, or from the swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	 When it is due to a stoppage of an artery, it is known by the hot swelling of an abscess, when you press it against your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 And you should not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	 That which is caused by an inflammation of the vein is known by its appearance upon being touched by the fingers, and one can make a cut in this manner, as well as in other cases.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 And it is that you cut the heart of the testicles, then raise the egg up, and make a strong incision in the white, and release the ligament from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	 If the egg is already hardened with these scars, then you must draw out the egg and cut it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 And if it is in the air passage, or within a vessel, then you must remove all that substance, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	 And if the base of the flesh is in the posterior place, then you must cut all of it, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when your work is completed, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until he is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	 This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling a bud, with the softening of the kidneys, and the patient is very sick when he walks.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 And the treatment of this disease is almost as dangerous as that mentioned above, and nevertheless, we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then put the suspension of the kidneys down to your feet, at all the vessels near the bladder, and let the master take hold of them, and stretch them very strongly;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	 Then cut the sputum with a sharp blade across the vessels until they are exposed, and then strip each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	 Then insert a needle with a double thread, and tie it first to where the vein is located, and then tie it again to the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	 Then cut them in half straight across, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupt moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	 Then treat the wound as with others where bone is injured, so that no vessel escapes that nourishes one of the testicles.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	 For by this no harm comes, and if all the vessels come with blood, then it is necessary to draw out the testicles for all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 if the bird does not lose its nourishment due to the cutting of vessels, it dries up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	 From the rupture of the shoulder
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	 The events of this branch are by the section that comes into the abdomen or the extension on the belly in the part of the groin, for which the intestines descend from this opening to one of the testicles;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	 and this opening is in the abdomen or the extension of it, and these two types come from many causes.
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	 by striking, or jumping, or falling, or lifting heavy loads, and by similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	 and the signs when it is an extension of the abdomen are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 And the abscess is equal all the way to the bottom because the pus presses against the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	 And the sign is when it is of the section of the hypochondrium, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears diverse, under the skin near, and this is for the exit of the intestine and the body from lack of the hypochondrium.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	 And sometimes the intestines descend with the intestine and are held back, causing the patient to suffer great pain, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	 And in these treatments with iron due to fear, for which it is necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	 And the manner of working is that you instruct the patient to push the intestines back with his hand into the wound, if he can reach it;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	 Then have him lean on his neck between your hands, and lift his thighs;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	 Then place the heart above, and cut all the skin of the testicles lengthwise.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	 Then insert into the wound of the belly some hooks according to what you need to open the wound, and so that the intestines may come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	 Then scrape off the pus that is under the skin of the testicles until the white hard pus is exposed on all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	 then place your finger in the hollow that follows the joint, in the one that is between the white fat that is under the skin of the egg, and between the second fat, and separate that which is behind the egg, and between the second fat.
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	 and then move to the right hand inside the heart of the joints, and stretch the white fat up towards your left hand, and lift the egg with all the fat towards the waist.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	 and instruct the assistant to stretch the egg upwards, and loosen that which is tied behind the ligament.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	 and check with your fingers if there is any part of the intestines wrapped in the hard white fat, and if you find anything, push it into the belly below.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	 Then take a needle with a thread made of ten threads, and push it into the rear part of the sinus, which is behind the skin of the knees;
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	 below the waist, then cut the threads that appear from the needle until there are four threads remaining;
