puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 then treat the wound with medicine, and replace the skin with hard flesh, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as heads and cooked wheat, likewise bones, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	 And if you find rottenness in the skin, and it does not reach to the bone, then cut away all the rottenness, cast it out, and then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	 And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by cutting it off, and it cannot be stanched with medicines, then seek the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if this does not help at all, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	 And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	 And it is that you put this powder in before the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	 And the manner of the powder is thus:
pren encens une partie;	 take incense, one part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	 blood of dragon, two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	 quicklime, three parts, and make the powder very fine, and fill the wound, and bind it strongly, so that it swells well and adheres to all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	 And then bandage it well, and leave it unbound if it does not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 For one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	 And sometimes one does this only with quicklime, when one has neither frankincense nor dragon's blood, but the fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	 And if the fire has moved the wound, even if it was summer, then do not put this powder on it at all.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	 but apply some soothing salves, or poultices made from barley flour with water and honey, until it produces pus.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then treat the wound with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	 And if there is a bone fracture along with the wound and it is small, then draw it out with fine forceps.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 and I will tell you about skull fractures later on.
de la plaie dou col	 from the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	 If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head; but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	 If it is a nerve, then there is no other treatment than to leave it alone and not put anything constricting on it, for it harms the nerves and causes them to recede.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	 And do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water in soft water, and mixed with rose oil, and cut herbs likewise in soft water, and other small stones according to this manner, and moist onions.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound is large, sew it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	 And if the wounds are deep and it is swollen and full of pus, then pierce it in a lower place.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	 and if an artery is cut and blood flows out of it, then dry it up, bind it, and cauterize it if necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	 and if the windpipe of the throat is cut or the heart, and the passage is kept safe, so that food can pass through, then sew the skin over the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back in its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And then he restrains it properly, and leaves it for some days, then treats it with dry onions until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	 And if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then he should pierce it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	 And if there are bone fragments, then extract them all if you can, and those that you cannot obtain, leave them until the wound suppurates, and let the opening drain and heal.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	 And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	 of the lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	 If it is a blow from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then see if there is any gas coming out of the wound as the patient exhales:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	 Know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	 and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put the powder in at the first hour, nor bind it for the blood that may bite deeply and return to the heart and kill the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	 but put an attracting poultice on it and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	 and if you do not have a poultice, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	 then there will be no spasm, no evil trembling of the heart, nor swelling from the wound;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 And when you see the bones in their proper position, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Heal it then with tents and other treatments, until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	 and if it cannot heal, and works, know that there is a fistula.
si la cure si com on doit.	 so treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut and it is simple, either worse or on the back, treat it as you would for one in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	 if it is large, stitch it up;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	 and if it is small, with powder, and if it presses against the bone and has splintered, seek the wound, and remove the foreign bodies if they are visible.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	 And if they are not drained, let the wound fester, thus making the extraction easier;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And for other wounds in other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	 Of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	 The rupture of the belly is large and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	 of the large wound sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, come out, by which their introduction;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	 and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because it is harder to put the intestines back in, unless they are done one by one;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	 because the intestines swell quickly when they feel the cold, and so it is harder to put them back in, and therefore the medium-sized wound is worse, because one moves the intestines to their place less than the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	 And know that belly rumbling is according to four ways:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	 the two common sutures occur in the belly suture and in the sutures of other wounds of the body, and the other two proper sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 and yet they are more specific with the belly suture, and I will say each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	 I say that when the wound is small and something of the intestines has come out, and this thing is difficult to put back in, it is by one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	 And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	 Soak a sponge or a cloth in hot water only, where you cook in boiling water with wormwood and hyssop and spikenard, and rinse the intestines until the swelling has subsided.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And sometimes make this wine constricting, and it is better to use alone for reducing inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	 And when you see the swelling subside, then moisten the intestines with water where mallows and hollyhocks have been cooked, for by this means the entry is made easier by a little.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	 And if it cannot enter, then make a small opening in the wound with the instrument used for removing hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	 And the first treatment is better than cutting, because no one should cut unless there is great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	 And this is the instrument to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 if you cut inside the curve and not outside, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is opened and the intestines leap out, then reset them carefully according to their natural form in their proper place, if you can, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	 When the wound is wide and it is in the lower part of the belly, you should make the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	 and if it is in the lower part of the belly, place the head and the feet higher than the lower parts, and also if the wound of the belly is in one of the two parts, direct your attention so that the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 And thus you must proceed as I have said for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	 In small wounds, apply what you have prepared, then have in your hands a skillful minister who can hold all the wound at his hand, and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	 and that is the common manner of stitching, and it is that you take one or more needles, according to the width of the wound, then from the head of the wound leave two spaces, and there insert a needle with which to have a good strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	 and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the hypodermis, which is under the skin inside, until you have it pierced from that part, and assemble the two heads of the hypodermis together in four.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	 then pull a double thread around the needle of two parts, then gather the two heads of the wound together, and then leave two spaces, and there insert another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	 then take the thread of the needle just as you made the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you need for the needles, until all the wounds are constrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	 and let the needles be of medium size, between fine and thick, for fine needles cut all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well;
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	 therefore they must be medium.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	 and it is not good to push the needles too deeply into the flesh and skin, so that they do not cut and open the wound before the stitching.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	 and then cut the heads of the needles so that they do not wound the patient while sleeping, and put bandages or cloths over the heads of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them there until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	 And this manner of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because it requires only one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	 The second stitch is common and is done by bringing together the two edges of skin and the two lips of flesh with one needle, threaded with a strong middle-sized silk.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	 And when you have pierced all four edges together, then pull the needle back to the place where you began, in the manner that clothes are sewn.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	 And leave a space between each stitch as thick as a minor finger.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 This stitching is approved by men, and I sewed up a wound that a man had in his belly, which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and the intestines protruded about two palms, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 Je remis son intestin après qu'il avait été en dehors pendant vingt-quatre heures, puis je pansai la plaie jusqu'au quinzième jour, et ensuite je soignai la plaie, et il fut guéri.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	 And the physicians had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	 And I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	 Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	 Take the needle and pass it from the outside to the inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	 When it has pierced the skin from inside to outside, leave the tip of the thread or suture where you passed the needle, and have it pierce from the other side, from inside out.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 And the understanding of this suture is that you sew as the furrier makes the furs, and that you leave the thread on one side once, and take it up again on the other, until the stitch is entirely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	 The second method of suturing, which Galen calls properly, is like some do, who join the two parts naturally together and apply one end of the thread to the other end in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	 Insert a needle into the nearer end of the thread and make it pierce only that spot, leaving the two ends of the thread;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	 then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outer part to the inner part at the two ends of the thread;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	 Then make one of them pierce through from the outside part to the inside, in two other places on the mirror that are opposite each other.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 and this is the most common method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	 Galen said these words, and some testify to this, that one should stitch the belly with two needles, each having thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	 and one must insert one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew belts.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the abdomen, then the stitching is more difficult than in other places on the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	 The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	 And it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the fire has moved it, then stop applying heat to the intestines and the skin.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	 then apply soothing powder, and if the fire has moved it, then apply some ointment that is available, until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	 and stitch the skin, and close the sinuses, and the intestines.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 and if you do not have medicine, then apply, as soon as it begins to heal, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	 For in many cases, no other medicine is needed when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	 And if you doubt that the wound will spread to the main limbs, then you must wet a light linen cloth in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the joints and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	 And if he feels pain or inflammation in the belly, which often happens, then give him an enema of warm red wine, and likewise if the inflammation reaches the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 And puncture it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is because of the thinness of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	 And if the intestine protrudes from the wound, then replace it back in as with the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	 And if the hairs are old and turned gray or black, then you must tie the blackened area so that blood does not flow there, because there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 Then cut that which is between the tie, and place the two heads hanging from the lower part of the wound until it is sufficient to ease the extraction when the hairs fall, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	 of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	 When the intestines are cut and the wound is small, then it can be restored in some men, for I have seen that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	 and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became ulcerated and turned into a fistula, from which issued the excrement and the flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 I took care of it according to what I could, and did not stop until it was healed, and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	 And when I saw that it was sealed, I feared that the patient had an ailment in his stomach;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	 and there was no illness there, but he remained in better health, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	 and some experts said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	 take a bandage with large ends, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the bandage has opened its mouth, place it on top of the two lips, so that it pulls its mouth shut;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	 and then cut the end of the bandage, and this holds so that it cannot be loosened, then place another bandage afterwards in the same manner as before, until the entire wound is completely covered.
et cout la plaie.	 and cauterize the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	 And these heads, if they remain in the intestines, and no harm comes to the patient, then one can tie off the intestines with a fine thread cut from the intestines of an animal, in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	 take the head of this intestinal thread and make it very thin, then tie to the head of this thread a fine twisted linen thread, then put the thread into the needle, and sew up the intestines, and return it to its place;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	 and this manner of stitching for fractures is nothing other than according to the way of trust and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the narrow intestines, there is no skill or sense, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	 Of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it has healed, is universally called "fistula," and also when it has burst and flows with pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	 And a fistula is according to the truth a hard and white knot, where one does not feel pain, and it is as deep as the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	 and sometimes it appears clear and shallow, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	 sometimes it is hollow, and other times filled;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	 And I have spoken of it in the section on wounds that every wound which is not healed and has no flesh, it is not cured except for one of the NINE causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	 that is to say, by the scantiness of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	 or because of its defectiveness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	 or because there is hard flesh within it, and on the edges, which prevents new flesh from growing; ?>
ou il i a trop de bowe;	 where there is too much moisture;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	 where the place is rotten, and the substance is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	 where the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	 or because the corruption is a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	 or because the property in the region delays digestion and healing, and is swollen by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	 or there are veins in the bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	 Or it is necessary that I make you know the treatment of fistula which is made by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	 Know that fistula occurs in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	 for there are fistulas that come from the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or in the face, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or in the spinal column of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet; 》
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 And so it happens to some where it reaches the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	 And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of serious illness, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	 And if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I have said, and you trust in the cure, and you wish to test it, then take a tent of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, then pierce it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	 And if the fistula is crooked, then seek a subtle tent of pine, for pine bends more easily around the curvature.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	 And if the fistula has many openings and you cannot easily probe it with tents, then administer an enema through one of the openings, for moisture thus passes from one opening to another, and cleanses it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	 Then wisely and with all your power, examine if there is bone or nerve, and it is cut deeply. Ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press your hand, and where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	 And when you know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the putrefaction and the corrupt flesh that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	 And then treat it until it is healed. And if the fistula is well deep and straight, it is necessary that you cut deeply, as much as you can, then put moist tents in ague medicine, and push them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And then put on dressings of fresh meat, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 and if it is not healed by this method, then cauterize as we have said; and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it off.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	 If veins or nerves trouble you in the main members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then clean it until all the corruption is removed, then treat with fresh meat dressings until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	 and if it does not heal, and pus comes out again as before, know that you have not reached the source.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	 search and dig until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then fill the place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 And if he is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	 If not, know that the corruption is too far advanced, that you cannot help it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	 there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	 and if there is a little rotten bone, and you can pull it out with tweezers, then draw it out with the suitable instrument, and if there are many bones, then pull them all out, leaving not one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 and if moisture hinders you and there is no mistake or fear, then cut flesh, moisture, and skin, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	 And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then apply a purifying agent to the wound, and let it sit until the place around the bones is rotten, and then the bones will be easier to extract; 
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	 And if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, then clean away the corruption until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	 And if there is a large part of it that is corrupt and reaches to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	 then you must cut and scrape all the way to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	 There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to an internal cause, so that the matter came out into the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no other reason for opening it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	 But the doctors in their foolishness worked so much that they opened the abscess, and from it flowed much matter, and a fistula formed, and there came much pus that all threw off stench and moisture of the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	 and many doctors tried to treat it for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine, so that I was called upon, and saw his leg and the medications with which he was treated, and what flowed from the holes in great quantity.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 and the young man's body turned red, and had a lemon-yellow hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 Je planted a tent in one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings, and found that one met the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	 So I hurried and cut into one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the rot reached the inside of the bone.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	 I was that which appeared to me from the corrupt bone, and I thought there was no other corruption except for what I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	 and I began to treat the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but it could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	 and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I saw it, and then removed it, and tried to heal the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	 but I could not do so until I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and then pulled it out entirely, after which I treated it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 and it healed and was joined quickly, and I did not need to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of my fear of his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Car for the evacuation of blood he often fainted, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone grew hard flesh, which had a good disposition and caused no harm or opposition at all, neither when leaving nor when arriving.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	 Take a thread, and tie it to the end of the bone that is exposed, and instruct someone to pull it upward;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	 and place another thicker wool thread above the first thread on the flesh above the bone, and extend the end so that you draw the corrupted flesh downward, and expose the flesh in the place where you wish to treat, ensuring that the thread does not injure the flesh;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	 and place a hot coal or on a table under the bone to further burn the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 and one must treat until the corruption can be seen and felt, and then treat it again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	 And if the bone is corrupt, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	 Then place a burning coal underneath, and then sew from one part to the other where the corruption is, and let the suture be as long as the length of the corruption, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	 And if the corruption is in the joint, then cut away the corrupt joint and sew the bone where it attaches to the other part.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	 And if the corruption is between two joints, there is no other remedy than to cut it out.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	 And if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or in the ankle of the foot, this thing is very difficult, but nevertheless you must seek to discover how it opens.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	 And cleanse it in all ways you can, but let not the vein or nerve do otherwise;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	 And know that the incision tools and the brushes for covering these bones are many, according to the placement of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	 And therefore it is necessary to prepare for each type of work its instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	 And know that the work will show you the instrument of which you will have need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 If you think of the instrument that you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	 from fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	 The head becomes dislocated either due to an internal cause or due to an external cause;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	 and when you have treated that corruption with the remedy of medicines, and they do not profit at all, then it is necessary to amputate that limb up to the place where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater evil of the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	 and the signs of this are that the limb becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corruption passes from one member to another, and spreads throughout the body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 so hasten to amputate, and if it is due to the bite of some venomous creatures, such as sea scorpions or vipers, and similar ones, if the corruption is at the top of the arm, then cut it off, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	 And if it reaches the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the rotting does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	 and if it reaches the arm, cut it with a knife;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	 and if it goes beyond the knife, death occurs, and no other remedy is of use except in accordance with its power.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	 and thus do you act when the rotting comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	 if it reaches the first joint, cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	 and if it reaches the foot, cut off the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	 and if it rises to the leg, cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	 and if it reaches above the knee, there is no other course than to leave the patient to die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	 And the manner of covering or binding the limb is such that you bind it above and below, and extend one minister downward along one of the ligaments, and another minister upward along the other ligament, and you divide the flesh between the two ligaments into a broad spatula, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 then bind or tie, and place on each side a linen cloth, so that the bandage does not touch the healthy area, and the patient will have another injury and an abscess there.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	 And if blood begins to flow when you work, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some restricting powders.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it heals.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	 And I will tell you what happened to a man on his feet
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	 There came a blackness upon him that seemed like a burn from fire, and this corruption first came in his big toe, so much so that it spread to the entire foot
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	 And when the man saw the corruption, he hurried to cover the foot, and was saved
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	 And a long time after the corruption returned to the toe of his hand, and he came to me, and I put on repressive things after the cleansing of the body, and still the corruption could not cease  :
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	 And he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, because I hoped to suppress the matter
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	 And I also feared that if I cut off his hand he would die, for the man's vitality was weak
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	 And he despaired of all, and returned to his land, and covered his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And I have not told this account except for what one does with another part, if one needs it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	 Sometimes an abscess comes to a fleshy place, and stays there so long that it causes a great swelling;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	 And then it breaks through and bursts, and the swelling jumps out, and the place remains hollow, like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	 And the skin that is above it is as thin as a well-woven cloth, and does not extend to the bone or the nerve. Such an illness is called "sinus", and is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	 mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusques à l’os en parfont, si est appelée «fistule»;
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	 et li cuirs s'est endurci de telle manière que tu dois couper ce cuir tout autour, et même quand il est fin, comme un ruban.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 et ne s’aggrave pas à cause de son infection.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	 And if you believe that the skin is getting worse, and the infection is not severe, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with an enema like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	 examine if the breast is large and the pus coming out of it smells foul; then treat it with an Egyptian medicine enema made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	 Take asafetida, oil, and lead oxide, in equal parts, and put to cook in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	 And then take some of this according to your need, and make it into water or honey, and use it as an enema in the chest, and constrict the anus.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	 And let the medicine remain inside for two hours, then remove it by pressing out.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	 Do this many times until the chest is cleaned and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	 And sometimes you should use an enema of ash water when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes from vine wood, and pour water over them, then strain it, and use it as an enema until you know that the chest is well cleaned.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	 And if the patient cannot endure it, nor the Egyptian medicine or water of ashes, then enema with water and honey in which there is a little bit of lead powder.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	 or you enema with honey and mulled wine, so that the honey has the property of cleaning and washing, and the wine makes the flesh drier;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	 and when you have done this, and you are confident that the wound is well cleaned, then enema with what causes flesh to grow in it, and that you take a definitive plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	 or you enema with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken the properties in the treatise on ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	 And if the opening of the breast is small, and the pipe of the enema cannot enter, then widen it a little with an iron, and place inside a tent of Egyptian ointment or Basilicon ointment, until it is widened.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if the wound is too large, then sew it and leave an opening only where the enema can enter; and if the hole that the intestine exits is high up, then cut it lower down where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	 For when the intestine is in its entirety, do not let any flesh enter.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	 And if you cannot cut the breast as you wish, then prepare it in such a way that the intestine runs to the lowest part of it; for when the intestine is whole, do not let any flesh enter. And if you cannot cut the breast as you wish, then prepare it in this manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	 What li bowe means
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	 Et puis metez sor le plaie un drap de lin pur,
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	 puis coveint que tu face tant de drapiax come tu veux ainz que tu aies mangié ne béüs;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	 et s’il est venimous ou malade, ou trop, ou digeste, ou non digeste;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	 et se li sieins est apert, et li santés approchiers.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 And then unbind it in the morning or on the third day; and when you unbind the wound, change the dressing and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	 And if the chest throws out undigested matter after many days, know that the chest is not well-aired.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poison comes out after a long time, do not despair of your health, for the health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	 For there are men in whom it takes a long time for flesh to grow over their wounds, and others who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	 And if undigested food comes up from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach does not open.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	 And if the stomach is slow to open and is constipated, use drying medicines that are moist in nature but dry in action, such as refined ointment, for it contains a great deal of vitriol, and this is the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	 Take refined ointment, and make it with rose oil, and mix it with equal parts of old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	 Then crush it and use it.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	 And the same thing, when onions are not present, you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and crush them, and sprinkle the powder over honey when it is on the fire.
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	 And then put it in a cloth and place it on the chest, and sometimes add a long clyster, and roots of heavenly iris, which are like vetch flour and fenugreek.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	 And use either simple or compound medicines:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	 Crush them, and make into powder, and put on the honey that I have mentioned, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	 And if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption is deep-seated, and has made an impression on the bone, or on hard members, or on joints.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 If the cure of the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	 of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	 Panarice is an abscess that occurs beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or sometimes in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	 and when it is neglected, and one does not take care of it, then an abscess like this forms, and it runs and throws pus so much that it runs to the root of the nail, and sometimes it runs all the way through.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 and the corruption reaches the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the tip of the finger or toe is swollen, and its color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail with an iron instrument, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	 Cautery is very helpful if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	 And if the nail presses into the flesh and begins to prick and wound it, you must place a reed under the nail that touches the flesh, and push it upward, and carefully and lightly cut off the flesh, and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then cure with onion until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	 And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and draw strongly, for as long as the corrupt bone remains, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and if you see the finger corrupted, cut off one of the fingers as previously said, then cure it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	 and if it is struck or bruised and causes great pain, you must first heal it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	 Then cut the nail of the big toe obliquely from above, and beware that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if it happens, place something on top to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	 The pain of the shoulder of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two bones that grow in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and sometimes there is one with bone, and sometimes there is a claw; and sometimes they grow at the root of the joint, where the growth appears on some fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	 He who is born under any knuckle of the toe does not move, and he who is born at the toe's joint, perhaps moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	 The cut of one who is fleshy is light in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 Cut it at the root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	 He who is born in the root of the joint is difficult to cure: xspace
si te tien dou coper.	 so hold yourself from cutting (it).
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes primer la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	 The sudden meeting of the two [bones] occurs at birth, or from a wound, or from burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	 You must cut that suture in such a way that they may be reconnected according to their natural shapes. xspace ‌
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	 Then place between two tents or wet cloths with rose oil, so they do not stick together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 Or you put between two thin pieces of lead until the place is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	 If suddenly it happens to one of his fingers with the palm, then strike that knot as is necessary.
des vils	 Of the filth
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	 The veins are large wounds full of excessive black bile, which come to many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	 It is therefore necessary that you administer some purging of bile to him, and then heal him with basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	 The treatment of iron is according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	 one is that they are cut out and strong black blood is drawn from them.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 And the other method is to raise the wound and draw it all strongly.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	 The cut is according to this method:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	 rose the first the leg of hot water very strongly, so that the large vein be made subtle, then hold the leg of the patient from above the thigh to below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	 then cut the vein in one place, or in two or three, with a wide incision, then lift up and draw out strongly the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the virtues of the patient can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	 and then bandage it, and command him to eat blackening foods.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 and repeat the evacuation and cautery when the veins are full, and benefit the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	 The raising of it is according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	 Pull the hair from the patient's leg if there is much of it, then place it in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it turns red, and open the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	 And if you do not have a bath, then heat it over the fire, and then cut towards the vein along the length of the leg from the knee to below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	 Then cut through the skin with scissors, and scrape the vein from both sides until it appears when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	 And one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	 Then push the blood downwards so that it is raised from the skin, and then cut it lightly with scissors, then cut in another place above three fingers.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	 Then peel back the skin on the vein until it appears, then lift it with the razor, as you have done, and attach it to another hook, as you have done first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	 Then make another cut, or several if you need them, then lift it and cut to the foot's big toe, then draw it and lift up to the second cut;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	 Then pull it from cut to cut until it comes out completely, then cut it off.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	 And if you cannot pull and lift it out, then thrust a very strong double-threaded needle into it, tie it off and pull, place it under the skin, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	 And watch that it does not cut, for if it cuts, then one cannot draw or lift it, and it causes harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	 And when you have drawn it all out, then place wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound site.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And tend to it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	 And if the vessel is twisted and bent together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it obliquely, but do not cut it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And draw it out as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	 The shape of the iron used to cut the vessel is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cut the vein; ‌
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 And it is of large size, for if it were fine, it would cover the vein; but let it be thick as we have said. Here is its form:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	 This vein is found in the legs, in hot places where no grass or tree grows, and on dry land.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 And perhaps it appears elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to corruption that comes under the skin, just as snakes and worms appear inside the body, lodged between the skin and the flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is such that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to come out like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	 When the head opens, it is necessary that you wrap around it a piece of cloth from one and a half cubits up to two and a half cubits, and the knot, and leave the cloth hanging on the leg. And every time that some pus comes out, wrap the cloth around it and the knot;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	 And if it is too long, then cut off part of it, and wrap the rest, and do not cut it at its root, until all of it has come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	 for if you cut it, then it enters the flesh and causes an abscess and putrefaction in that place, and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	 because of this thing it is necessary that it be treated little by little until the head, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	 and sometimes this vein when treated is fifteen palms or twenty long, and a man came to me once whose it issued twenty palms long, and when you cut it, then it spurts out one or two streams, and pierce it until the bottom, so that all of it comes out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 And let the matter that is within be emptied out, and apply to the place medications that prevent putrefaction every day, then treat it as you would with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	 And sometimes this vein is smaller, especially when it appears in the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and there is much pus, causing swelling.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 Treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	 This disease is called in our land "ox disease," because it often affects oxen, and it is a small worm that grows between the skin and flesh, traveling throughout the body up and down, and one feels it well as it moves from limb to limb until it desiccates the skin where it goes, causing swelling.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	 And is infected by putrefaction of certain humors, such as worms, serpents, and roundworms or ascariasis in the belly;
