et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	 And one doubts his wickedness, for when he goes through the body, and he rises to the head, and he comes to the eye, perhaps he enters, and destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	 And this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	 When you see him cured and drawn out, one cannot avoid it except when he goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	 Then it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong bandage very tightly, then cut into it and pull him out strongly, and if the worm is deeply in the flesh, and you cannot find him, then cauterize him with fire until he dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	 and the greatest harm that it does is that it affects the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	 and if you see it coming near the eye towards the head, hold firmly beneath it the bone, then cut above, and pull out the arrow forcefully;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 and it is necessary to use the patient for body cleansing with dissolving medicines for bad humors, and to abstain from foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	 This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes in certain limbs, and then moves from one limb to another;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	 And afterwards, the wound swells up on the shoulder like a worm, faster than anything else, just like quicksilver when it changes place.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	 The pain leaves that spot and lodges in the shoulder, and then a little afterwards it runs throughout the body until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 Then she told me that it continually moved around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	 Je me merveille beaucoup comment elle se déplace ainsi d'un membre à l'autre, car je n'ai jamais vu cette maladie de cette façon auparavant.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	 However, I had seen many who had well experienced pain moving from one place to another, but I had never seen it as I did in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	 and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were exposed, and for this reason these windy constriction appeared.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 And do not follow this method for those who are delicate, and have moist bodies and full veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	 And when you see that this disease is being treated and the patient feels this pain, if it appears as we have said, then apply quickly above and below, and then cut into it until that windy pressure forces out from its place.
et cauterize le leu;	 And cauterize the place;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it with those that expel windiness, such as stinking pills and pills of serpentaria, and similar others.
des saiettes	 of the arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	 The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places on the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	 The diversity of them is such that there are some with large tips, and small ones, and hooked ones, and joined ones.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	 And of those which have two angles, and of those which have tongues, and of those where there are parts.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	 And that which falls upon any member does so in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 Or it falls upon a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	 When it falls therefore upon any place of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you afterwards appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	 then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for death follows in many dispositions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 And when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not embedded deeply, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	 And the signs of the brain when an arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and jumps the sutures that are on the brain, are headache and stupor and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	 and perhaps there is an issue from the nose or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	 and perhaps speech and voice are lost.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	 and from the wound comes white moist substance resembling pus, and it also spurts like boiling flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And if these signs appear, then tend to the wound, and remove the arrow if it is still there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	 Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer = The signs of the stone when it falls into the heart are that it is near the left nipple and feels as if it were embedded in something hard, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	 et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz = and perhaps the stone moves like the finger, and there is black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent. = know then without doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	 And the sign of an arrow that never leaves a foamy spittle from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	 Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; = And if the stone falls into the bladder cover, it is near the small ribs.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	 et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; = and causes great pain and great sighing.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 And all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	 And if the arrow falls into the stomach, by chance some undigested flesh may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	 And if the arrow falls into the belly, and a little feces come out through the anus, there is no hope for the cure or the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	 And if an arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels strong pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	 The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and elbow and spine of the back and pelvis and hips and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	 When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	 It happened to a man, an arrow fell on him in the armpit at the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 I pulled it out and drew it from the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	 And shot with an arrow that fell into the fat of the eye under the membrane below, and the arrow was broken off, and he could not reach anything but the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large for a Turkish bow, all iron except for the light feathers.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 The youth was healed, and no evil accident befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	 And he drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian in shape.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 I shaved off my beard, and acted so skillfully that I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	 And I drew an arrow from a man who had it in his belly, and thought that he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	 and after passing thirty days, his condition did not change at all.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 I cut around the arrow, and pulled it out, and drew it out strongly, and he had no evil accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	 And I saw a man upon whom an arrow fell in the back, and the wound was sutured shut;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural disposition at all, nor found harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	 And I saw another man, to whom an arrow fell on his face, and the wound was sealed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	 and remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	 and many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	 And he drew an arrow from one of the king's leading men, which had fallen into his nose, and it was slightly slanted to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	 and the arrow was completely bent.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 I was called to tend to it after three days had passed since it fell.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	 I recognized it as a subtle arrow and did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 And he felt a prickling pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	 I thought it was the tip of an arrow, so I applied a plaster that is astringent and healing to prevent swelling.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 And the place of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	 I put the plaster on for fewer days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained thus for a long time until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose.
et il le me dist.	 And he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	 I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open, and then I probed it, and felt the tip of the arrow which had settled in place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	 then I approached the opening of the wound with that sharpened instrument until the head of the arrow became clearly visible to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	 and the wound healed well for three months, and then I opened it where I placed the forceps, and pulled from one side to the other, but it would not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 then I did not stop trying and devising ways to use tools until I grasped it with well-made forceps, as described at the end of this chapter, so that I could pull it out and close the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	 And physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 I then closed it and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	 Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you may focus your care on what I do not say, for the book cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 but the wise master considers well a small thing, and that which is present and failing, finds new work, and nine instruments, for the resolution of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	 I say that arrows should not be removed from the members into which they are fixed except according to two methods:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	 either through the place where they entered, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 and the one which should come out by the way it entered is an arrow entering into fleshy places, and this should be done at times.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	 And if it does not heal now, then leave it until the flesh is rotten all around, and the exit is healed;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	 and so if it is lodged in the bone, and cannot come out, then leave it for some days, and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 and then it heals, and if it does not heal, then pierce all around with the finest awl, until the place around is enlarged, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	 And if the arrow is lodged in the skull bone, and reaches one of the brain's chambers, and some of the symptoms I mentioned appear to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 do not draw it out, but leave it until it becomes even after some days, for if the arrow reaches the brain, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not reach as far as the marrow, and the patient remains for some days without any bad incident, then use the device to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	 And if it is very lodged thus and cannot come out by force, then administer cauterizations around it, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then heal the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	 And if the arrowhead has returned to its place in the body and cannot be seen, then seek it along all the course.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	 and if you feel it, then draw it out with some suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	 and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then widen it until the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	 and draw out the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has barbs that catch, then remove as much flesh from around them as you can, and then break or bend the barbs of the arrow until you can draw it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And be careful not to break the arrow, for you would draw it out more harshly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	 And if you cannot do it all at once, leave it until the place around is rotten, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	 And if the flow of blood goes against you, then use what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	 and beware of the incision of the nerve and vein, and devise a way how you can carefully draw out the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 and put the patient in the same position he was in when the arrow struck him, for that is the greatest help there can be, and if you cannot do this, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	 The arrow that comes from another place, or where something protrudes from it, or the skin is swollen in that spot so that one can clearly see or feel it:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	 Cut away until the tongs can grasp it, then pull.
si saut fuer maintenant.	 If it leaps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	 And if it is lodged in the bone, turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	 And if it cannot emerge, then leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it emerges;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	 and if there is any shaft left, push out all the shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	 and if the shaft falls out, and you see that a pushing tool is needed, then administer the pushing tool, so that the tip of the arrow enters into the groove of the tool;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 and then push strongly, and if the arrow is grooved, then push in the pointed tool, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is poisoned, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	 And if the arrow falls into the chest or the stomach or the bladder or the side, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut through, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	 And guard against cutting the vein and nerve, then extract it, then suture the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And tend to it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	 The shape of the pincers used to remove arrows is like a bird’s beak, and see here its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	 And there are many kinds of them:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the arrowhead is like the feather of a bird, to insert into the tip of an arrow, as here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	 The shape of the pincers for inserting and extracting is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	 common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	 There are 31 veins from which one can bleed, and there are 16 in the head, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	 Two that are behind the ears, which are called the "herb" veins.
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	 and the two arteries that appear in the temples;  />
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	 and two veins that are in the corners of the eyes, which are called "aspirs";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	 And the vein which is within the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	 And the vein which is at the top of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	 And the two jugulars which are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	 And the two veins which are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "aujugularis";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 And two veins which are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	 The veins that are commonly bled are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	 one is the cephalic and it is on the left side, and people call it the "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	 and the middle one is called "fastus", and it is made up of the cephalic and the basilic veins, and people call it the "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 and the bladder is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the pubic bone, and it is that which is healed, which appears clearly on the vulva.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	 And the little vein is the one between the auricular and the ring finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	 and in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	 one is below the pubic bone on the left side, and the second is the saphenous vein at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	 and the vein called "greater saphenous" which is in the other ankle;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 and in the other leg there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	 The bleeding of wounds after the ears helps against old fevers and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	 And the quality of the bleeder, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head and rub the place where the wounds are with a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	 Then have the patient clench his neck with a rope, so that the two wounds appear behind the ears in two hanging places from the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	 Then seek them out with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, sign there. 
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	 Then take the lance and thrust it under the vein until the bone, then raise your hand to the top of the vein, cut through both skin and vein well twice across, and let out as much blood as you wish.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 then hold and bind it until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 And I have already spoken of incisions and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	 The bleeding of the two arteries located in the two temples is good for chronic migraine, gout, and habitual blindness; and for violent weeping of the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	 And the qualities of the bleeder are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	 and it is that the patient should hold his neck, so that the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	 and feel with your thumb beneath your finger, and then press down on it.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	 then place your heart on the vein above your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath, and lift the vein up, and cut it, just as you did with the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	 Then dislocate the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And then tie it tightly, and leave it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 And we have spoken of them in the beginning of this book, concerning their tying and removal.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	 The vein of the forehead is worth as much as the cephalic vein for ancient diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	 And its quality is that the patient should twist his neck until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 then take the instrument called "fosseur," of which here is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	 And place the tip on the vein, and strike with your hand or another object, and allow blood to flow according to the amount you wish.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Then untie the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healthy again; sometimes use a wide flame for the work.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	 Nevertheless, it should not be that the flame is too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 and the saw slantwise, because the bone is close by, and perhaps the flame breaks when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	 The sawing of the two veins that are in two temples is helpful for the eyes, and for ringworm, and for redness, and for the little vein in the eye, and for diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	 and the qualities of their sawing are such that the patient should twist his neck with some cord, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 Then heal it, and let the wound be from the crossbow, a little long and a little wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	 And if the flame is delicate, perhaps it will break.
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 Then make it bleed with blood, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	 The wound of the vein of the nose is worth against fever, and madness, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	 And the quality of the wound is that the patient stretches his neck, then presses his nose to your left hand, and takes the delicate, long flame, and places it in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	 And do not go too deep, let the blood flow according to your need, then leave it for a night, for it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	 The fennel of two kinds also helps in the constriction of the nostril, and in the beginning of headaches, and in many illnesses, and in ringworm, and in corrosive sores, and in shingles;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	 and the quality of the fennel is that the patient should tighten their neck under both [fennels], as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	 and let the master be standing over the patient's head, and the patient sit on one seat, then cut the vein of the arm widely for a short time, then draw blood moderately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	 then make another incision in the other vein, then release the ligature, and gently compress all the veins so that the patient is not strangled;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 and leave it until morning, so that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 de la saignée des veines
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	 The bloodletting of the veins of the lips above helps to cool the mouth, and to heal gum infections, and lip cracks, and of the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	 And the quality of bloodletting is to have the patient sit before you and compress their neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	 then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is at the right lip and the other at the left, and they are recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 therefore cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, then cut the largest one on each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	 The bleeding of wounds that are under the tongue also helps after bleeding of the cervical [region], and this is for narrowing the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	 and the quality of bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and he raises his tongue, and looks under on each side at a black wound.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 bleed then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	 The wounds of the knife with which one commonly bleeds are bled according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	 either by pricking at the entire flame of a large myrtle leaf or an olive leaf that is thin and sharp like a cutting knife, and it is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 And they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	 The form of the merlin flame is very renowned, and it is broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	 And it is necessary for opening large veins full of large, visible blood, and which contain coarse and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 and this is the form of the olive-flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	 And it is more subtle in its aim, and it is for healing the subtle veins, where there is subtle citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	 The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases under the throat, in the neck, in the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 and it is necessary for the bleeder to bleed wisely, and to beware of the artery which is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	 And if he cuts the artery, and blood begins to flow, then he must staunch it, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And the flame should not be piercing, but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	 And if the blister does not open clearly, then you must press it and change another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	 or where you want some veins of it, or you heal in its place the vein into the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	 it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 and cut with the knife like a blade, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	 And if you want to find the vein, then first press on the arm so that you touch the spot until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	 then mark the spot with ink, and then tie off the arm, and cut the vein with the knife like a blade.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	 And beware that you do not strike an artery when you see the spot swollen, for it is of the artery.
eschui la donques.	 then avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	 And if you see it protruding like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	 then hurry up, and place your finger on top for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	 if it is in an arm, leave it like this, and let the patient not move it;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	 And if the bleeding does not stop, and you are alone, and the physician is not present, then cut the artery if it is open, for the head of the blood will retreat.
et estainche li sans.	 And bleed the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	 And take a piece of fig bark, and split it, and take one of the halves and tie it on well until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	 if the wound is bled, that is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	 if not, then treat it, as we have said, with powders that bleed.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 and bleeding is not good in many conditions due to the small area of the wound, and the power of the ligature around the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	 The bleeding of the vein in the middle thus helps that it draws blood from above the head, and from below the body, because it is composed of the basilic and the cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	 And it is necessary for the physician to be careful of the nerve that is below, and if it pricks too deeply, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the wound becomes inflamed, and perhaps it cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	 And this nerve often breaks open, and if it does not break open in some men because of its subtlety, then you must cauterize it with the silver instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 And avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	 And if there is a vein between the two nerves, incise it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	 The vein of the head is useful because it draws blood from the head and helps with vision;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 And it is necessary to cauterize with the olive or myrtle flame because this is the safest of all veins because there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	 Indeed, one must look for the most suitable place, and if it fails the first time, do not worry, and try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 And perhaps the place swells in some men, when it fails the first time, but do not worry.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	 The quality of the bleeding depends on your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	 The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is practiced only to maintain health and to prevent future illnesses.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	 And let the bloodletting be done in one of the three veins that are on the wrist.
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	 that is to say, the cephalic, fast, and basilic veins.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	 And one should bleed at the beginning of spring for children, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 And one must cauterize on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	 The cautery that is administered for illnesses has no fixed hour, but when the need arises during the day or night, at all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 And one should not cauterize children until they are fourteen years old, nor women who are pregnant from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	 The old who have passed LX years should not be treated.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	 And when someone wants to be cauterized, in whatever manner it may be, they must cleanse the intestines with a light enema if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw the harmful excess from the intestines to the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	 And he does not heal at all who is too excessively fed with foods, or drunk, as long as he remains intoxicated, nor those suffering from dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	 And if he purges himself after suffering from colic, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and increased sexual activity with a woman, and from labor, vigilance, and fasting, and those who have completely lost their strength, either due to weapons or bodily injury.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	 Then refine the humors if the blood is thick, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	 Then enter a bath, if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood, and heal from the vein on the third day, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	 And guard yourself that day from work, and pain, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	 and be happy and joyful, and let the healers be higher than those who are being healed, and rub the arm two or three times, then pull the ligament moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	 and then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 then moisten the healer's hand with a little old oil, then place his left hand thumb over that vein below the spot where he wants to heal, so that the vein does not catch fire or break when pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	 For there are veins that flow like ropes in a basket, and there are such that are full of windiness, so that when one brings up the flame, it draws back from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 And if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for this reason it is necessary that the surgeon be wise in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	 And if the vein opens on the first try, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	 but if not, then again a little lower in that place or quickly above, if the spot is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	 And if the spot is swollen and the patient is frightened, let him wait one or two days and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	 par aventure i venra apostemes chaus
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	 ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’ele li plait;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	 et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	 et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 car ceo avient maintes foiz, quant li plaie est petite.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	 Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	 And thus administer the juice of oil into each wound that you open the veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	 and the same acts as a triple drug and cures them when applied to the place.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 if it thins the blood and disperses when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	 And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, especially when it is not opened except at that time when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and place on the spot a sponge moistened in water and a little hot salt, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	 and you must do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if some blackness or greenness remains on the spot after several days, it does not harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if you see, apply some aloe or myrrh mixed with calamint juice, mustard, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	 And often there occurs an abscess and swelling at the wound of the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 Then place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft under pressure from the hand, then that swelling is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	 Therefore, do not apply anything of what we have said, for it may be coming from an artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Instead, make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	 And draw on each according to the amount of its virtue, and according to the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	 For if the blood is black, let it bleed until it becomes red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	 And if you see it thick, leave it until it is thinned.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 And if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	 And it should be for the full and robust person who needs bloodletting, that one make a larger wound for him, and the flame should be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	 And for the weak person, do the opposite, and one should bleed little and often, and one must bleed by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And this manner of bleeding is safe from bleeding too much and cutting a nerve, and it is worth more than the long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	 And for the one whose body fails at bleeding, it is necessary to give him soaked bread in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 If it is inflamed, draw blood three or four times; and if of a cold complexion, eat before the wound bread soaked in syrup mixed with mucilage, or honey-flavored syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if he faints from blood loss after a great deal of blood has been let out, then it is necessary that he drink broth made of meat and subtle, fragrant syrup, and use the other things we have mentioned in the section on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	 And if he wants to bleed from the arm and bleed again another time, then it is necessary, when he is weakened by great blood loss, that he be bled little by little according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	 And if one wants to bleed from the arm after the first bloodletting and he has a strong body, then let him be bled seven hours after the first bloodletting, or after nine o'clock.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	 And who wishes to heal from another place, must heal on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	 For it has much blood inside the body which is already inflamed, and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	 so a large quantity must be drawn from it, and enlarge the opening until it reaches the bone marrow;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	 then, when you have considered all the conditions of wound treatment, and place your hand over the patient's pulse while it is bleeding, so that death does not occur from bone marrow exposure, which happens often when the physician is careless;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	 And it is not necessary that when you see the arm dislocate, and make blood come out a second time, and the hole is closed, that you press very hard.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	 Nor if it is crooked, that he extend the arm quickly, for that would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	 But let him be until he heals the second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 Or you prick with the tip of the flame until the frozen blood comes out of the vein's hole and put on a little silk soaked in water and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	 And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not compress it until the abscess is calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	 And if there is a need to bleed a second time, then heal it in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	 The vein in the arm is healed in the place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	 And the way of the healing is such that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the scar tissue turns red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	 Then let it be bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then heal now across, not wide or long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	 And let the opening be wide, and let it be pricked well near the joint of the hand, and if pus does not come out, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	 And if it is summer, do not put the hand in hot water, for it is more needed in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the pricking of this wound is safer than any other wounds, for there are no veins or nerves therein.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	 The pricking of the little finger of the right hand is worth all the remedies for liver disease, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	 Press the hand, and put it in hot water until the wound swells up if you see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	 And if you cut it diagonally, and you cut all of it through to the other side, then it is not harmful.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 And do not go too deep into it, for the nerves are bare under all the skin, and then put your hand in hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	 And when you have drawn blood as much as needed, place oil and salt on the vein to seal it quickly, and do this for each time.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	 The bleeding from his left hand is as valuable as the illness of the mouse, and does everything similarly to what I have told you about the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The bleeding from the saphena is as valuable as all the illnesses that are below the body, such as illnesses of the stomach, and retention of urine, and diseases of the kidneys, and of the thighs and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	 And the quality of its bleeding is such that the patient should bathe his feet in hot water and rub on the wound until it opens, and then tie it over the foot joint.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	 And the wound is at the ankle, and above the foot go many nerves;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 Therefore, cut it then in the widest nerve, or at the ankle, because that is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	 And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are beneath, and heal from side to side like in cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	 and let the flame be slow.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	 And if the pus cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and allow the wound to drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	 And if the healer fails the first time, then start again the second time a little higher, for the place is burnt.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 and do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and so do with the sole of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	 The place of the sciatic wound is at the ankle on the outside, and its cauterization is worth the pain of the hip, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	 And the quality of his healing is such that the patient enters the bath, and pulls on the ankle four times while twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	 and if it opens, then heal in all ways that you can, and by crossing over;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And it is better for you to cut it off, because the place is empty, and it is very abundant in many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	 And if you cannot find it, then incise some of his flesh that opens onto the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	 and let the blood flow as much as you wish, then release the ligature, and apply cotton and bandage it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	 it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 of cupping bleeds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	 Cupping glasses are made of horn, or tin, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	 and cupping is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	 And this cupping, which is done without pricking, is done in two ways: 
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	 Or it is all fire, or without fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	 And scarification, which is done by cutting and extracting blood, is performed in fourteen places on the body, one of which is entirely at the top of the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	 And another is in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	 And two others on both sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	 And the cupping beneath the chin.
et li ventouse des II espaules;	 And the cupping at the shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	 And the cupping on the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	 And the cuppings in both arms.
et les ventouses des II jambes;	 And the cuppings of the two legs.
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	 And the cuppings of the two ankles.
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	 And scarification does not draw blood except from the small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore it weakens no one at all, unlike venesection.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And it is not appropriate that it be administered, by any fire or without fire, in any illness caused by fullness, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	 And if it is necessary to bleed due to illness or habit, then we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, in the middle, and at all times;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	 for there are some who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	 and there are those who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	 and there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And there are some who dream of blood, wounds, death, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	 And when we see these signs, especially when it is mid-month, we order them to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	 The bleeding of the nose helps with the lightheadedness of the head … that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	 and this venesection is in place of the bleeding from the head, and it is not necessary that those who are of cold temperament use it, or have catarrh, because it does great harm to them;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 and therefore the old should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	 And those who bleed often become stupid, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower out of fear of becoming stupid.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	 The venesection in the neck is in place of the bleeding from the head and the basilic vein, and for this reason it is good for constriction of the chest, and for fissure of the esophagus, and for coughing, and for fullness;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 And there one should put a little, for if it holds too firmly, it injures the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	 The ventosations at the two ribs of the neck are good for the pains of the head, and for migraine, and for suffocation, and for the pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the incision of the basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 And you should instruct the surgeon to press with his hand while cutting, so that he does not cut the artery, and blood does not flow out continuously.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	 The ventosations under the chin are good for diseases of the mouth, and for corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 And it is located at the junction of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	 Ventosation on the shoulders is effective for illnesses caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	 The cauterizations of the ribs are worth as much as those of three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 and instruct the physician not to strike too deeply into it, for the place is bare of flesh, and underneath are nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	 The cupping on the rump is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases below, and it should be large and made of brass, so that it can draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	 and perhaps, if it were delicate, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	 and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	 The cuppings on the legs heal openly, for they draw blood from all over the body, and they are worth for old pains of the reins, and of the womb, and of the bladder, and remove the humors.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 And they are in the place of the two spleens and the two ankles; nevertheless, they weaken the body after long use, and bring on paralysis in many parts of the body.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	 The manner of placing the cupping glass is such that you first place it empty, and then suck immediately, and place it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the redness of the blood;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	 then fire, and replace the cupping glasses, and pay attention to the condition of the body, for there are those who have thick flesh and clear pores;
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	 thus it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and one deep hollow.
et suce legierement.	 And suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	 And if the blood is thick, it must be struck twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 The first time to make the path of the thick blood finer.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	 And if the blood is very thick, it must be struck a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 And when we want to draw blood little by little, we only need to strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	 And if we want a lot of blood, then we must strike often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	 And if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the ends should be such that the heart is suddenly pierced, and for those who have thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, you must anoint the places of the cupping glasses with opening and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	 If it is inflamed, use oil of violets, or oil of sweet almonds, or oil of cucumber seed.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if it is swollen, use oil of watercress, or lily, or chamomile, or any similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	 And if the excess is large and cold, then take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the one whom we heal has tender flesh and large pores, then no oil should be applied, but it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or mallow water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar waters.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	 And the one who has much moisture should be treated with easel, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	 And those who have large superfluous growths should rise from old wine, or water of juice, or decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar ones.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	 And it is not necessary to use a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he washes, both when he should be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	 Et (and) warde (beware/take care) se (if) cil (that person) qui (who) se (himself) saine (heals) est (is) coleriques (irritable), et (and) se (if) li (the) sans (blood) est (is) trop (too much) agus (sharp/acrid) et (and) enflamez (inflamed).
