si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	 If it is necessary that he take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce in vinegar, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And minced partridge, and lean meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	 And if one has a cold constitution, let him take syrup of honey, and wine that is moderately fragrant, which is between old and new, and minced peacock, and minced partridge and small birds and thrushes.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	 And on the day he sweats, he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	 and it is necessary to give some men some tricat or muscat before sweating, or after, to strengthen the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 and let the blood be thinned, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	 The cupping glasses that are placed without cutting are those placed on the liver, and on the bladder, and gout, and on the stomach and the navel and the kidneys and the hip, because these members do not tolerate being cut over the eyes, and it is only done to draw blood from member to member, as we place on the breasts when the baby sucks;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	 for to remove the stickiness that is on the limb, just as we place cupping glasses on the abdomen and on the buttocks to reduce the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	 and removes pain, when there is a blister or stone, for perhaps by its attractive power it draws out the blister, or moves the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	 and thus it does when placed on the liver and on the bladder when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to draw out only as much.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in cases of pleurisy, and in such manner that the cupping glass is filled with only hot water or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	 The shape of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	 And let it have two fingers in width and half a palm in depth, and let there be on the side around the middle a small hole, just like for inserting a needle, and let it be of bronze, soft at the front so that it does not hurt the patient when placing it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	 and let there be in the middle a crossbar of bronze or iron, to place a bandage wrapped around it, both large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who use them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 because the cupping devices for children are different from those for adults, and for thin people than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	 And one should place this cupping device on the limb in this way:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	 take a cloth of wax or linen, and place it inside the cupping device across the crossbar that is inside the cupping device, so that the heat source is at the bottom of the cupping device and does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	 And then place it on the limb, and your fingers should be over the hole that we have mentioned, so that when one wants to, the vapor goes out, and remove the cupping glass.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And apply the poultice again as before, and repeat it often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	 In the cupping glass used for pleurisy, there is no rod or hole, and it is not applied until it is full of water, and is placed only on the limb.
et c’est li forme:	 And this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	 Leeches are not applied except in places where one cannot place a cupping glass due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	 And in naked flesh, such as a finger or nose, and other similar areas.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	 And the quality of the cautery is that when you find blisters that are in clear, clean water without any impurity, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	 And put them into a vat of clear water until they become familiar, and have nothing in their stomachs.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	 And then have the veins and vessels bled with a cupping glass, then rub the member until it is red, and place the blisters upon it.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 And when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where one can put a cupping glass, then put it there, for that is very effective afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	 If not, lift the place easily, and then with water, which is good, and then press it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	 And if the healthy flesh swells too much after the leeches, then moisten the linen cloth in cold water and place it on until the leech is exhausted.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	 And if there are many leeches, then place ground vitriol or gallnut, and similar things on it until it is exhausted.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	 Or place half of the shelled beans on the spot and leave them until they dry out in place, it will exhaust now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 And if you need more, then take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	 And if the leeches do not want to attach, then rub the spot with fresh blood or stick a needle in it until the blood comes out and then place the leeches on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will attach.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And when you see that they are falling out, then sprinkle a little aloe and celery on them, or ashes, and they will fall out now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	 Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	 This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and it is for the treatment of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	 Know, dear son, that the foolish physicians of this chapter threw away all ancient books and read none of them;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	 And for this reason the science is strange in our land, because I never found any good ones.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	 And I know nothing about it except for the knowledge from ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have learned the skill, and by experience, and by the practice of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 And I have already described in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	 Il is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	 Je dis que quand brisure ou dislocation ou torsion ou fracture arrive à quelqu'un, il faut que tu te dépêches de soigner le patient d’une manière et d’une autre, si aucune chose ne t’en empêche entièrement, comme la faiblesse du corps, ou l'enfance, ou la vieillesse.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	 ou si le temps n’est pas très chaud, ou trop froid ;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	 et ménagez des aliments froids, c'est-à-dire des soupes froides, et du fromage d'oiseau et de chèvre, et ne buvez pas de vin, et mangez aucune nourriture grasse, et ne vous remplissez pas trop de viandes qui remplissent les veines de sang, jusqu’à ce que vous n’ayez plus de doute sur la chaleur de l’abcès, ni sur l’expansion de la matière dans le membre.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 If the patient returns to his original state of health.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	 And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to feed the patient with foods that promote heavy nourishment and have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, heads, feet, calf's pancreas, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	 For with such nourishment, the bones heal better and more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	 And know that old and frail broken bones cannot be well repaired or fused according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor can those which are too soft, such as the bones of young children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	 but do not worry, reset the broken bone with strong ligaments that hold and bind the limb together until it is as strong as before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 and do not completely deprive him of his work, and for this reason he should be fed with rich foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	 And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	 For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	 For there is a fracture that goes awry, and another in slanting, as the cut of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	 And so there is a fracture with wound, and a fracture with all a small cleft.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	 And each type should have its own device and proper tool for restoration, according to what is remembered in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	 And it is known that the fracture of the bone occurs because the place is twisted, and it becomes well apparent by feeling, and sounds when pressed with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	 And when there is no twist or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 But it can well have a twist, or split, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	 If you do not need to move it by hand, but apply medicines that come hereafter, and then hold it delicately now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	 And know that the fractures that go awry, and are the two parts disjoined, it is now necessary to set them equally in place, lest abscesses come there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	 And if hot abscesses come there, leave it alone for some days, until the abscesses are appeased.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	 then make it equal to the bone that you can easily and wisely adjust, and know that its restoration is more light than that of one where there are parts.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 then hold it, as will be explained later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	 And if there are broken pieces in the bone, then hold it with two hands, if it is the foot or hand, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	 and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, then adjust all the additions in their places to the bone as you can, and be careful not to cause the patient injury or pain through your work.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And adjust the two heads of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	 And feel it well with your hand if you think that it is not right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	 If it seems well to you, set it beautifully, and do not squeeze too much or press as those who cause hot abscess and contraction in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	 And when the limb is set, advise the patient well that he does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 and take care that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	 For when he feels any pain, it is not set right, and one must put it in such a position that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	 And take care that it is placed correctly, so that crookedness does not occur when it is reset.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 And the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	 Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	 For there are small members, such as arms and fingers, and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	 so it is necessary to wrap them with soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	 and those that are large, such as hips and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	 so it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bandage embraces the entire large limb and holds it equally on all sides, so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	 then bind around light padding, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little all over the bandage, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break moves away a little from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	 And soften the ligament little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy area, then take the other ligament and turn it around again on the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	 Then return to the part below the fracture and fasten it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first ligature above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 Then place linen wads or cloths between the ligatures until they are all even, then tie everything together with a bandage on top, and then place your splints well on top, unless there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	 And if there is swelling or abscess, place something that soothes the abscess and removes the swelling on top, and leave it this way for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 then draw up thy hands on thine shoulders, and let them be of half the width of a thick rope, skillfully made, or of wood from which one makes cleavers, or of palm fronds, and let them be according to this figure
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	 but it is necessary that the splint placed on the fracture should be a little larger and wider than the others
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	 and let it also be as long as is necessary for the limb, whether small or large
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	 then draw up the splints in the same manner as you did at the first time, then tie over it a thread evenly, as at the first time upon the fracture
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	 tighter is above, always less
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	 and it is necessary that the thread be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and let it be made of soft flax
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 for if the threads are thick, as I have seen done by fools who make their ligatures from twisted linen cord, and this is a great mistake, for the ligature cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it should not be that there is less than two finger widths of space between each knot.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	 And if the patient is wounded by the heads of the stars after being drawn into healthy places, place cotton or shredded wool under them so that they do not become bloody.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	 When the wound is with a fracture, and the heart is broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	 And know that it is not right to draw out all the broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	 for when the limb is large, it is not necessary to place ligatures stronger than after five days or seven, or more according to your surety of a hot abscess occurring;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	 and see here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torse;
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 and it is that you take the flour that adheres to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and place this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and apply it, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring fracture in many conditions, especially for women and small children, for it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	 Another manner of plaster restoring the fracture, dislocation, and twist:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	 Take three parts of barley and ladanum, helenium, asafetida, gum Arabic, and mastic; in total, twelve parts.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	 Honey and aloe, five parts each.
alechil VIIII З.;	 Garlic, nine parts each.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	 And make it into powder, and mix with the white of an egg;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	 if the man's constitution is warm, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition and quickly restores broken bones, and it is valuable to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	 Another manner of plaster that is good for twists:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	 Take mastic and mallow, twelve parts each; iety
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	 myrrh and aloes, nine parts;
acaice VI З.;	 ginger, six parts;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 mastic of Armenian bole, ten parts. Grind well and mix with plenty of egg white, then administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	 Another method for a plaster on dislocations and displaced bones, which relieves the resulting pain, and is used for bone fractures and breaks:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Take new linen, soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the site.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not restore [the joint/bone], but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and effectively relieves pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	 Another method of plaster that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	 Take dried fig leaves and wild peony leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method for plastering to restore bone fractures and to soften the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	 Take root of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, chickpea flour, of each one part.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, then mix with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of plaster stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	 Take roots of mallow, and linseed, mullein, melilot, ivy, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 and grind, and mix with salt water or fresh water or wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	 Ypocras says in his book that one should not put anything over a broken limb to restore force except for wax made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	 And it seems that Galen says one should put over a broken limb, to restore it, dry and slightly warm things, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	 Another method of plaster that is good for injuries and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	 Grind poppy seed and henbane, or bird feathers, and madder root, and celery equally, and pound them, and make a poultice and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	 And then dislocate the joint again afterward, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	 if it is not dislocated by hand.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	 And if pain or itching comes to the place, without rest or swelling, then hasten and dislocate again, and remove the poultice now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	 and take light cloth, and wet sponge of the sea, and dip it in water, and lift up the place, until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	 then let the member rest for an hour, then place on it a dry linen cloth, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it onto a nut, until you are sure of a warm abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	 and the inflammation of the member will rest, and the pain will be removed. Then begin again with a delicate bandage, and a little poultice, and do not bind it as tightly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and continue gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	 And if you see that the abscess is swollen and red and painful and inflamed, I have removed it all, and you need a plaster and a bandage, begin again as you did first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	 And if nothing happens to the member as we have said, do not untie it until after three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	 and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on what is seen, until the break heals, and the union of the flesh approaches;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	 then he will be constrained more than before, and his flesh will swell, as I have said earlier;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	 and if you see the place drying more than necessary, know that nutrition cannot reach there;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	 then apply hot water poultice every time you release him, and this should be every third day, and loosen the ligature a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	 by this procedure, nourishment is restored to the limb, and it quickly heals as if done by foolish physicians who incorrectly reset the limb;
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 this is harmful, and such practices are fearful, and I see nothing in it but to let nature take its course and work properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	 Of the various types of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	 Many types of fractures exist, and various shapes, and the causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	 because it has fractures that are caused by the impact of a sword, and the neck removes all the bone down to the marrow which is beneath the bone, just as an axe or log does.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 and for this reason this manner of fracture is called "axe-cut.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	 Or if the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, this manner of fracture is called "simple.
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	 and the wound from these two fractures is either large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	 And if there is a blunt impact, or splitting, or blow from a stone, or falling on a rock, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	 Et si il a fracture penetrante, qui atteint jusqu'à la toile qui est sous l'os, ou elle est sur l'os, et cette blessure peut être grande ou petite.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	 And there is a wound that is as fine in the bone as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "hairline.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	 and if the wound is caused by being struck by a stone or by falling or something similar, and it causes the bone fragment to go downward, and the place is sunken in like how blacksmiths do when they hammer on cauldrons;
si entre li piere dedens.	 If between the stones inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	 And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their heads, like a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	 and it occurs with all these types of fractures where small fragments are separated like stars;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	 and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	 And let us recognize all kinds of fractures by the drawing out from them, and the inquiry with probes, and by the corrupt flesh that is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	 The similarity to a hair is known because when one has uncovered the bone and rubs over it, a black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	 In the treatment of a fracture, beware of the patient's accidents, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, seizures, fainting, fever with chills, and eyes coming out strongly and reddening, and other similar things in many dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	 And if you do not see a frightful accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	 And when the wounded comes to you first, and this is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	 And if this is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh under the bone does not become corrupt, and the accidents that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	 And if the bone fracture reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the part to be split like this:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	 and it is that you should take the patient's head and uncover the bone in all ways possible, especially on the wound's shape as gently as possible. And if bleeding occurs when uncovering the bone or if there is an abscess, then aid him with what is necessary. And it is that you fill the place with linen cloths moistened with rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	 and let the wound rest until the abscess is appeased, and you are sure of a stoppage of blood;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	 then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done in two ways of working:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 one way is that you cut with a narrow incision at the front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	 And then there is another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	 And the second way is that you have several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and made of iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	 and work lightly to avoid injuring the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	 And if the bone is hard and tough, then you must first bore around it before you administer cuts with scrapers, not so deep that they do not go through the bone of the skull, and there should be a margin or circle above the point so that the point does not pass through the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	 and you must have several of them, so that each one comes into its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you may have tests for all.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	 and there are three kinds of probes:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	 The quality for piercing around broken bone is that you place one probe on the bone and turn it with your two hands until you know that the bone is pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	 then place the probe in another spot nearby and do this all around, then cut with incision tools the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this more subtly and lightly than you can, as we have said, until you draw out the bone into your hand or with any instrument you have such as pincers. ︎
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	 And beware that you do not touch the brain or the spleen.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	 And when you have pierced and removed the bone, it is necessary that you clean the remaining debris from the bone with another instrument similar to a chisel, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other chisels.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	 And if there is any remaining small bone fragments or scales, remove them lightly with an instrument;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 then treat the wound with linen and onions as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	 And another way of working is that which Galen says is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	 and he praises it greatly, and these are his words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	 It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone where the break appears, so that when you have exposed this part, you will place under the head of this lancet-shaped scalpel, which has this form.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	 And do not cut from one side only, but the cut should be on both sides, so that the cutting instrument is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	 Then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly tap the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 If it is close to the bone, lightly remove it, for it can be removed well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	 And if the bone fracture does not penetrate through to the skin, and the bone is broken only on top, and there are small pieces, then you must smooth over that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine scraper which you should have in various quantities, to administer in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	 First use large scrapers, and then finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	 In each of the other hair-cutting incisions and delicate fracture, you should apply treatment according to its location;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	 And this is something that cannot be taught to one who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	 And if the ulcer is exposed, then you must take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	 Then take another cloth folded into two or three layers, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	 And do this more lightly than you can, so as not to weigh down the sponge. Then place another bandage on top and do not tighten it too much so that only the wound is compressed.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	 And leave it this way for a day or two until the abscess subsides. Then remove it and administer medicine such as lily roots, vetch flour, frankincense powder, and similar substances.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	 And from these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and administer medicine that is soothing without any irritation.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	 And ensure that the wound is always clean, so that you do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow any pus to gather, because when pus gathers on the veil of the brain, it will run and spread, causing great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 For when you apply a stinging substance, it hardens from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	 Pren warde donc, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	 And if blackness occurs due to the medicine applied, then take one part honey and three parts rose oil, make it into a plaster, and apply it on the stinging substance.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then continue with the manner of treatment until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	 Know that sometimes both parts of the nose are broken, or one alone, for these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	 And those beneath are cartilaginous, and they do not break, but only cause a swelling or twisting, and then heal.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must insert your little finger or probe through the nose, and bring the break even with your index finger, and outside at the thumb, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And do this gently, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	 And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and your finger cannot reach the place, then you must place a small amount of thick cloth at the tip of a reed.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	 And if the break is in two parts, do the same again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then insert into the tip of the nose a piece of linen cloth, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	 Where you push one against another, if there is a fracture
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	 and let the tents be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some say that one should moisten the tents with butter, and change them daily.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	 It does not seem good to me, but they must be moistened in the preparation of an egg white and flour mixture.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 then leave the tent until the bones are healed, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	 And sometimes, feathers are put in the nose instead of tents, and there is a soft cloth around it, and if there is a fracture, the patient blows through it.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	 Or do whatever you want.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	 And if such abscesses come to the nose while you work on it, put there a salve of cotton moistened in rose oil or in a little bag of diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	 And if an abscess does not form, then apply an external plaster made of flour of linseed and powdered incense, mixed with egg white, then place light bandages on top, and do not tie the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	 And if the break of the nose is small, and it is broken into many pieces, extract it with suitable instruments, then sew up the fracture, and care for things affecting flesh, and healing, such as suitable plasters and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tents, and place leaden weights there until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	 of the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	 When the jaw is dislocated downwards, and there is no wound on it, and it is only broken apart, and not broken in two, except for a small piece inside, then it is easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	 It is necessary that if the break is on the right side, you insert your index finger into the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	 and if the break is on the left jaw, then insert your right index finger, and gently push the break inside, and align it with your other hand from outside, and set it straight.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	 And if the jaw is broken in two parts, then you must provide traction in both parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	 And if there is movement of the teeth or loosening, bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken jaw cataplasm, and put on a double cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	 And place on the cloth a well-made large strap, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it above the mouth as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	 And if you see that the swelling changes, then release it on the third day, and then set right what has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	 And place a plaster on it, of the powder from the mill with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after you have removed the cataplasm.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	 And put on a light woollen poultice, and if the poultice dries out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	 many times it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	 Et s'il vient des abscès semblables, alors agissez comme nous l'avons dit plusieurs fois.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	 And if there is a fracture and wound together, be careful that no piece of the bone has been removed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	 then remove it with instruments suitable for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	 And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you have removed all these pieces and nothing remains, then sew the wound if it is wide, and place suitable plasters on it to promote healing until it heals completely.
de la forcele	 of the trepan
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	 The collarbone has been broken many times before, towards the shoulder, and the break is according to three types:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	 or it is broken and dislocated in two, and there are parts, and this is the easiest to restore. ️
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	 or there is a break with a wound. ️
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	 And the work is thus when the break is without wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the fracture feels strong.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	 and the other extends the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	 then place the break evenly between your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor displacement of it.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	 And if you need to extend more, place under the patient's shoulder a round ball of cloth or wool, and let it be thick according to your necessity;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 and stretch and lift the fracture, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you place the break evenly as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	 And if you cannot pull the head of the bone out due to its depth, it is necessary that the patient lie on their back, and place under the shoulder a medium-sized pillow, and let the assistant push the shoulder down until the bone of the fracture is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	 And then bring the break to your fingers, and if you find it is displaced, it is necessary that you split open;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	 And draw forth the bones lightly, and if the bone cannot join due to some obstacle, then strike it with one of the chisels you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	 But place under the trestle this instrument, to prevent slipping.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	 And it resembles a spoon, and is not hollow, and should be as wide as needed, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	 And it should have two heads, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, like the shape of the wound that you made when you drew out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And when you are sure of a hot abscess, then close the wound, and if the shape is small or you doubt a hot abscess, then fill the wound with lint and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	 And if abscesses come here, then soak the cloth in rose oil and in ashes and in wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	 The compression of the bone, when it is without wounds and without fractures, is to place on the bone a plaster made of milled powder and egg white, and put light wool on top, and place a sphere under the saddle, if you need one.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	 Then take a very wide bandage of about four fingers wide, then place a double cloth on top of the wool and the plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	 Then take a fine linen cloth of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the ends of the bandage hang down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	 And place the cloth over the break, and turn the bandage up over the healthy side, and under the saddle, and under the unhealthy side.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	 And there you reset each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the star does not move on the broken bone, then you splint it daily, and when the ligament loosens, then you bind it again;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	 and make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under their head when they sleep to lift the shoulder upwards.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	 thus the fracture will heal more easily due to the relief of the shoulder, where you bind the arm to the neck, and do not unbind it unless a bad accident occurs, for up to twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	 then begin the plaster again, if you see that it is necessary, and bind and leave it thus until it heals.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 And she is restored within twenty-eight days, and less so for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	 About the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	 It sometimes happens that the shoulder breaks in a wide place or in the middle, and it is noticed only by touch;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	 so assemble it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	 then place on the site powder of a mill with plenty of egg, and light dressings, and put on two cloths;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	 then put on a broad and delicate bandage, a little wider than the shoulder, and if there are creases under the bandage in any part of the shoulder, fill those creases with linen dressings so that the bandage sits evenly;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	 And then he binds it tightly with a large bandage firmly, so that the bone does not move from its place, and checks the bandage each day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	 And every time it loosens, he binds it again and sets the bone straight if it is out of place, and the patient lies on his side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	 And the shoulder is restored in twenty days or twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 And when this number is complete, he unbinds it and be assured, for it is not the bone that easily goes out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	 And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward and touches under the heart, it causes pain, extracts, and does what we have said in the case of breaking the rib to treat a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	 of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	 The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 But it often breaks at the toe.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken in the middle, it shifts downwards, and the patient feels great pain, weakness of breath, and convulsions, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens the passage in the broken bone, which can be felt well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	 And the restoration is such that the patient often lies on his back, and he puts one pillow between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders together, and aligns the ribs from the second rib down to your hands, and carefully ensures that it is set straight in all ways possible until the bone is properly aligned;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	 then place plasters and stuffing on top of a subtle layer of salt, or another light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and bind it onto the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	 and turn the bandage around to the back, and secure it firmly, and check every hour if the binding is still tight, and if it loosens, then tighten it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	 and if it is necessary to unbind him, due to suppuration or itching that occurs at the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry and unbind him, and remove the plaster, and apply what has come of the methods of treatment.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then reset the plaster and bind it until he is healed.
de la brisure des costes	 of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	 Know that rib fractures only occur in large places behind the back, and inside the head, and they break only because they are slippery.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	 and one feels it well during the examination of two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the treatment is to set the fracture evenly, as is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then apply a plaster and bind it with a bandage if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	 And if the rib fracture is slanting inward, the patient feels very great pain and sharpness, as from a punctured lung, because the bone pierces the flesh.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	 and breathes with difficulty, and coughs up large amounts of blood, which is a sign of serious illness, and the ancients have given it great thought.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	 And there are those who say that one should administer foods that inflate the belly to push out the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	 We do not do this, lest hot abscesses come there, if they have not already done so.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	 And if they have come, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	 And some say that one should put cupping glasses on the place to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	 nevertheless, there is doubt whether the cupping glass attracts excess humors to the place due to the weakness of the body.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	 And some say that one should cover the place with wool cloth dipped in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the bandage even all around, then treat it with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and with medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	 And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to a bone that punctures the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument below to prevent the pus from spreading.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then one should cut the bone and gently pull it out, and then sew together the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	 And if an abscess forms in this way, place wet cloths soaked in rose oil on the spot.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And treat the area as if for an abscess, and let it lie on the side where it should be until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	 Of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	 Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and it often happens that they bend;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	 and likewise to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, take note if you see their hands are softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move them or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that he is mortal in many situations, and if he moves them and feels well when they are strained or pricked, know that the articulation of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one applies a remedy there.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	 And if something similar happens to the spine of the back, and you wish to know whether it is whole or not, then take heed if the feet are paralyzed, and if there are injuries in the hands, and on the back there is windiness and involuntary evacuation;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 and when one turns it over on its stomach, there is involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when he is placed on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	 Know that it is fatal;
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 unless you labor very diligently in his care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	 And if these accidents do not happen to him, then the case is more mild.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	 And the treatment is that you investigate if there is a hot abscess, then put on the spine oil of rose or oil of yolk of egg, until it is soothed;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	 Then apply one of the comforting and drying poultices, and secure it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	 And if any bone breaks out, then it must be covered with wax;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and remove the bone, then join together the two lips of the wound with stitches if it is large, and treat it with a healing salve until he is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	 And if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "bone head", then press your little finger of your left hand into it and make it even with the other hand to your power, then apply the poultice and bandage on top, if you need it.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Then hold it [still], and if there is a shard of bone, remove it and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	 of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	 It sometimes happens that the hip bone breaks, and if it does, it is usually only a small loss at the top.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	 And it stretches along its length, and slants towards the outside, causing pain and soreness in that spot, and swelling like a bruise.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	 The treatment is to extend your hand over it until you are above the break;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	 and know what kind of break and shape it has;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	 And if the break is only at the top, then set [the bone] evenly so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	 And if the break is lengthwise, or it declines inward, then make the patient lie on his stomach, so that you may be prepared to restore that break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	 And when you have set it evenly, place the poultice on it, then put a wooden or poplar splint over it, and hold the fracture steady so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	 And bind it under the ribs, so that the ligature is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	 Instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	 And if an abscess comes there, do not touch it until the abscess has subsided, and then put on what we have said before.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	 And then return to setting it, and hold it as needed if there is no bad outcome.
et c’est li maniere.	 And that is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	 of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	 The shoulder is what is between the armpit and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be set according to one of the two methods.
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	 whose one is that you take a stake of moderate thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	 And tie two stakes with two straps, and lift them up, and make the patient sit on a seat;
