puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	 then you throw his broken arm onto the stake, until it reaches the armpit, and has in the middle a curve of the stake, then pull up some heavy object where the assistant stretches downward;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	 then have the helper hold the fracture level with his hands together, so that the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	 And the other method is to have the patient lie on his back, and tie his hand to his neck; then command two attendants, one to hold what is above the break at their hands, and the other to hold below all the length, and each extend to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you see that the extraction is stronger, then hold firmly the ligament below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the instruments to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	 And if the fracture is near the shoulder's head, then you must place one strap midway under the armpit, and another towards the side, under the fracture;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	 And thus if the fracture is towards the bone, then a ligature should be placed lightly, without effort, until the fracture is equal on both sides and on the bone.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 Then set the fracture as it should be and bind it tightly, if any abscesses occur there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	 And if such abscesses occur, do not bind it for seven days, and place moist linen on top with rose oil until the abscesses subside.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	 Then bind it, and the manner of binding is that you place a poultice on the fracture, then raise the arm to the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	 And put the bandage, and hold it on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in the position of the stars, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	 And if you doubt that the bone will move, use stars, and place on the break a larger and stronger star than the others, and let there be two fingers' width between each star, and each star should be so large that it passes the break by three fingers on each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 Then hold on the stars as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the break, more tightly and less widely spaced.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	 And if you see the base of the stars and the tightening as we have said in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, leave it to bind until the seventh day, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 Then look at the bandage every three days, to prevent itching or swelling from occurring in that place, as this can hinder healing due to excessive tightness.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If you receive it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	 And if no such incidents occur, do not remove it before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	 and place a cushion full of wool equally under the bandage, and every hour of the day or night check that the shape of the broken limb does not change, or that the bandage is not loosened;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	 if it heals through the power of medicine, and give him the food that we mentioned before, in such a way that the food is first finely ground;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And when he begins to recover, he will be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	 And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset within forty days of everything.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 Then one must free him and administer baths and medications with onions to direct the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the constriction is ugly and swollen, it takes one day or two months to heal.
de la brisure du bras	 of the arm break
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "two phalanges," one of which is small and follows the wrist.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	 And the other is large, and it is the one that is below, near the little finger.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 It may happen that only the large phalanx breaks, or the small one, and it may also happen that both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	 When the small phalanx is broken, the setting and healing are easy;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 And when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more serious than if they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is only the small scapula that is broken, then it should be stretched slightly and made straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	 And if it is the large one that fractures, then it needs to be set more strongly;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	 And extend it on a cushion, and hold the little finger of the hand higher than the others, and the small toe lower than the others, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the cushion in front of him, higher so that the patient does not suffer any hardship.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 Then let the ministers extend their arms to the part below his hand or to the limb, and another minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then the physician will set him straight, according to his best ability.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if there is a break with pieces, place each one in its proper place; and if any of them sticks out and touches the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, cut above and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	 And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a separate chapter;
si pren la cure.	 Si pren la cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	 Si pren la cure. Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 Si pren la cure. Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	 Si pren la cure. Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	 And know that it must have six stars or arms in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	 whether the break is in one of the bones or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	 and holds more firmly on the fracture than elsewhere, and always less by lengthening, as I said at the beginning of the chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	 and let the cloths that are on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 and let the thread used for binding be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And wrap the limb and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	 And if any bad event occurs to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must rinse the limb with hot water until that itching is calmed.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And let the member not rest too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then resume the binding, and if the ligament is weakened and the bone dislocated, or similar things, treat it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	 And if you notice that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it with a poultice and leave it like this for some days, until the nourishment reaches it, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things we have said happens to the patient, then do not unbind them for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	 or in which case, he should put his hands on his neck, and let his neck be equal, and take care of movement and jerking, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 And know that this fracture is healed in 30 days or in 35, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the nature and constitution of the powers.
de la brisure de la main	 of the break in the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 Know that on the back of the hand and between the fingers there are few breaks, and only swelling occurs many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	 And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, then the patient should sit cross-legged, and sit upright in front of him evenly;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	 then place his hand on the spread cloth, and let the caregiver straighten the broken bones, and let the surgeon align them well until they are joined properly.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	 And place the poultice and the wool, if an abscess does not form, then put a needle according to the size of the wound.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	 And if the break is around the waist near the belly of the foot, make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken foot.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 And then bind it with a long cloth, and let the needle be as large as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	 And if the fracture is in the finger, you must place a bandage on top and another underneath the limb, so that the hand remains open and straight; then bind the whole hand, and secure the ligament between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	 And if the break is in one of the toes, if it is protruding, set it straight, as needed.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	 And hold it with the sole of the foot, and if you see thus, place a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and do not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	 And if the fracture is in the other finger, such as in the index or one of the others, place it equally, and tie it with the healthy finger that follows.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	 Or you bind all together in one bandage, which is better, or you place a splint on top, like in a pocket.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And take care in the restoration and arrangement of a hot abscess, and heal that which comes from it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	 Of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	 The thigh bone is often broken, and it is well seen when it turns forward and backward;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 And the restoration is as follows: one ligature on top of the fracture, and another beneath.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	 And the patient lies on his back, then each assistant extends their ligature equally to their side;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 and this is when the fracture is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the thigh, let one of the ligaments be towards the knee, and the other ligament below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	 And similarly if it is near the knee, then the ligature should be at the knee, and the extension downward.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 Then the surgeon should put the bone back in its natural shape with his two hands, and then apply the poultice, and bind it, if pus does not come out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	 And if there is hot pus, leave it to drain first, then return to your work and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 The incision is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	 It is necessary that you wrap around the break II or III layers of thick bandages, leaving some excess, then turn the leg until the heel reaches the base of the big toe, and pass a long thread between the thigh and the leg, near the knee below, and the ends of the thread should come out on top.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	 then turn the bandage around the leg and the thigh, then place splints on the break, and put a splint on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	 then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to make the bandage even, then begin to tightly bind III or IV turns around the break.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	 And when more goes above the break, and less it holds;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	 then place two fingers of the thread that you have passed between the leg and the thigh, and in it place three needles that are above, then go back below to the head of the thread, until you come near the foot.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 and hold it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, since there comes neither abscess nor swelling nor anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	 And if it happens, then dislocate it, and address whatever comes, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	 and if there are pieces of bone that prick, then you must remove them, if possible.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	 and if it is not possible, then one must split the place, and pull strongly;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 and treat as we have said, until he is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	 And sometimes the thigh is broken like one puts needles in it, as in the shoulder and in the arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 nevertheless, in such a restoration the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	 And know that the hip is restored within 40 days or a little less or more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	 from the calf of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, it is only a split or a hole, and this happens with any wound, and without a wound, and everyone feels this.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	 And the restoration is like one places equal to what is round on its two sides, so that it may be assembled together as one can.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	 then apply the plaster, and place a round needle in it if you need to, and hold it as necessary, then follow all the instructions we have given for other fractures, such as treating an abscess and similar.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 apply to each incident what is needed for it, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	 Of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	 You should know that in the leg there are two bones. One is called by its right name "muscle," and the other is called "fibula.
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 And there is the same kind of fracture as in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and all the operations are the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	 And if the smaller bone is broken, it turns to the front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	 And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it well.
et torne desoz.	 and turns downward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	 Then apply traction, and set it evenly, and bind the splints evenly;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	 however, if the fracture is ugly and there are several fragments, then the traction should be gentler and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 And align according to your power.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	 And when you have completed your work, take two splints of wood that fit the leg from one side to the other, and let them be as long as the leg from the knee downwards.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	 Then wrap two of them with a bandage on top and bottom, and bind it in the middle as well. At this point, the leg will not be able to bend to the right or to the left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	 And some add a splint the length of the leg, and it is made of wood. They place the leg inside to prevent movement. This is done properly in the case of a fracture where there is a wound.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	 And move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or other accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	 Of the breaking of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	 At the ankle, there is no breakage, but sometimes the bones of the foot break and the two feet, and only fragments are found in many cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	 And if there is a break in the foot bones, and you see these bones surpassing each other, then put this patient's foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and now put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their places;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 then put a poultice and bandages on top, and place beneath the foot a small board with two full nails, then fasten it firmly to the foot, after which you will wrap cloths around, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	 Et lorsque trois jours ou quatre seront passés, alors délie le ligament, car tu trouveras les os égaux, qu'ils soient cassés ou disloqués.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	 And if there are any of the fingers broken, set them, as we have said for the fingers of the hand.
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	 Then place a splint on the broken finger according to its length, and let it be a little wider, then place under the foot the table that I have mentioned, and bind it securely.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	 And if there are two or three, or more, broken fingers, place on each finger a splint according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and bind the table under the foot.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 And let it be standing at the head of the table, outside the foot's belly, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	 And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said before;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 And treat each incident as necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	 of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	 When the bone of a woman's natural structure is broken, have her sit with legs spread, then lean her towards the back, and let her be held from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	 then fill the woman's natural cavity with cotton, and place therein as much as a fistful.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	 then have the woman stand up, and lift her back bit by bit, and thus the cotton will jump, until it comes to the entrance of the vagina, and the bone will return with the fist.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	 And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or thereabouts.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	 Then the fracture will be healed, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder and tie a string to its neck, and insert the entire bladder into the vagina;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	 Then breathe strongly into the reed until the bladder is inflated inside.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	 the fracture will heal on its own;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then fill it with cotton and leave it thus for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	 And when the bone of a man's hand or a woman's is broken, restore it as we have said for the hipbone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 and these nearby fractures are not hidden from those who apply themselves and their skill, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	 For the fracture indicates in several dispositions the correct way of restoration:
enten le donques.	 understand it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	 In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's gullet and insert the penis into it;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 Then wrap it with cloths around, and leave it for three days wrapped around, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	 with break and wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	 It is necessary for one who has a break with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the thigh bone or the shoulder bone or similar, that he be cauterized now, so that the cauteries we have spoken of testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the wound heals, then close it with vitriol, if you do not have anything else, then begin again to restore the breakage in that same hour, or that day, if abscesses like these do not come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	 And if abscesses like these come there, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause evil to happen there.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	 And if the broken bone is protruding from the flesh exposed, then it is necessary that you place it lightly with your hands, with a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	 And if the extension is not ready to be applied equally to your hands, then reset it with this iron instrument that has seven or eight inches in length, and its width is according to the size of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	 And for this reason it is necessary for the physician to take three or four [of these], according to what he needs in each fracture cure.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 And it should be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend at all when pressed upon the limb during your work, and it should be pointed in front, and thicker from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	 And it is called "palanche," because the curved head must be placed above the exposed end of the bone.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 and strikes once, so that it returns and both ends are equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut the end of the bone until the instrument can hold it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	 And if you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, then cut with an appropriate instrument, either a scalpel or scissors, according to your ability;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 then remove that which remains in the bone of roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is brought back and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	 Do this until it is in its place, then moisten a cloth in black stiptic wine, and cleanly if it is in summer;  /> ici le couvres d’un drapeil, et puis de laine, et puis de bande, et puis de laigature de fil.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	 And do not put any ointment or other oil-based substance on the wound, lest it cause decay and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	 Then apply bandages after you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not strained with the fracture;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	 And often the foolish physicians do this, and cause the patient to die or be consumed by decay.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 And let the strain be gentler and softer than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that evil accidents may occur, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then do not put bandages on it.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 but wrap around it, in place of needles, hard rags, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one day or two enlarging the wound in the place, then remove everything you have put on at once, and apply a healing salve to the wounds, such as tetrapharmakon salve and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	 And you should unbind the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	 And the limb should be prepared in such a way that the wound drains easily downwards.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	 And if many days pass and it cannot heal but rather breaks open again, know that there are small pieces of bone causing this, so you must probe the wound with a tent, and remove all the loose pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if an abscess or other form of corruption occurs there, you must cure it according to what is said in the previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	 And when the bone is broken and protrudes from the limb, such as the thigh or shoulder bones and other similar large members, do not extract it, for many times death results; but leave it until it rots.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	 perhaps it will fall out after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 and if you cannot, leave it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	 of the wounds that come upon the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	 We often see health return after the fracture, especially when it is near the joint. It is a ugly sight to behold the shape of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	 Take care, therefore, if the nose is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	 if you administer styptic medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, take one of these things or all together, and mix them with styptic wine or plenty of egg or honey;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	 and place them on the nose in cloths, bind it well, and do not release it for many days;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	 and then remove it, and begin another, until the swelling is gone;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	 or bind it on a well-made piece of lead;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	 for the property of lead is such that it removes all swellings from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	 And if the swelling has already turned to hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut off the top of it, and make the excess apparent.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 or cut it with some scissors until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	 Of the limb which is weak after the cure
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	 When the fracture of the bone is healed, and afterwards the limb remains weak and delicate, this happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	 because one reason is that it was bound too tightly and was not bound as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	 or because there were too many bindings and the nourishment could not reach the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	 or for excessive application of ointments;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	 Or for too great a movement, not at all in its hour;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 Or because he has little blood in his body, he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	 And the treatment is that you make the patient eat and make the body tender, until the blood is abundant in him.
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	 and give him a bath, and bring him joy and cheerfulness;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	 then place pitch on the limb, so that the pitch draws great nourishment to it, and irrigate it often with warm water, until the nourishment flows into the limb.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	 of a twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	 When the limb is twisted after the treatment, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function.
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	 if not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb completely, and many foolish physicians have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	 and these works are blamed, and great evils come from it, and perhaps death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	 nevertheless, if the dislocations and tortures are recent, they must be softened with hot water, or cooked with softening herbs, such as mallow leaves, roots, mullein, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	 and make a softening plaster, like well-made diachylon, and take the marrow of mallow, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and apply the plaster on top; ・
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 You take fat figs, and grind them with colocynth juice, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes dislocation is removed by continuously and extensively rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And the member should be gently moved every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	 And if the swelling is hardened like stone, and needs to be removed with iron, then it must be cut down to the bone with a sharp, light incision.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And put cautery and poultice on the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	 Here begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	 Dislocation occurs when a joint is displaced from its place, so it cannot move, and the limb is deformed, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	 When dislocation happens to someone, they must immediately be brought back to their senses.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	 For if one delays, the place swells, and perhaps it is only barely reset in place.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	 Therefore, one should not move it at the time when it is swollen.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	 often causes spasm and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	 nevertheless, when this happens, have the patient bled, then leave it alone until the abscess has subsided.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Then soak the limb in hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each limb as it comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	 And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	 of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	 It sometimes happens that the jaws are dislocated together, and the dislocation of both is according to two ways:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	 or they are a little removed from their places, and softened a little;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, and the saliva runs from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is wrapped with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	 When the dislocation is small, it returns through many positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	 And if it is whole and complete, then you must quickly reset it, and do not delay at all;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	 And in such a manner that the assistant should hold the patient's head, and the practitioner should insert one of his fingers into the pocket of the mouth at the root of the mandible's dislocation, if the dislocation is of two parts.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	 And let the other two fingers be outside, to balance.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And instruct the patient to relax his jaw and move it in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	 And the healer balances it until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	 And if the joints are stiff, whether it be both jaws together, then soak them in hot water and oil until they loosen slightly.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 But do not force the joint, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	 And when they are equally realigned and the patient's mouth closes well without loosening, then place moistened bandages on a poultice made of rose oil and wax, and bind it lightly with soft bandages.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	 and let the patient sleep on their back, with their head resting between two pillows, so that it is not moved to the right or to the left, nor should they try to open their mouth, but let them eat light food, until the pain subsides, and the jaws are sewn shut;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 and then let him chew lightly what he wants, without trying to open his mouth for eating or drinking, until the jaw is well sewn and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	 And if the two jaws cannot be set correctly within an hour, and are not returned to their places, then fever and sudden faintness follow, and perhaps diarrhea, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	 And when you see that, know that it is a dangerous situation;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 and many times the one to whom it happens dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	 of the jaw
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	 The jaw cannot dislocate from the inside or from the end of it, and sometimes it is dislocated downwards, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	 And the restoration is such that the patient lies frequently on their back, with their arms extended;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	 And then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	 Then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it tightly.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	 And the head that is towards the knife cannot dislocate;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	 If not, and if it dislocates even once, reset it to its place, as we have said.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then apply the poultice and bind it tightly with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest until healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And in the same way is the shoulder joint reset when it has dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	 Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	 Know that the shoulder is only dislocated in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	 One of which is that it dislocates towards the lower part of the armpit; xspace
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	 And the second is at the part of the foot;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	 And perhaps it dislocates at the upper part, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	 And it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inside for the nerves.
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	 And many times it dislocates downwards towards the ankle, especially in those who have little flesh, for to them it jumps quickly.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 In those who have enough flesh, it hardly jumps and hardly returns.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	 And it happens to some men through a blow or break, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	 Therefore, you must test it until you are certain of it.
et adonques encomence la cure.	 And then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	 And the dislocation is known when it is downwards towards the ankle, and make a distinction between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a clear difference;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	 And you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and under the armpit at the top of the shoulder, as if it were an egg.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	 And the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor make any movement;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	 And also, if it is dislocated upward, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly under the armpit.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And this manner of dislocation is not easy to reset when it is new, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	 And the way to do it is for the attendant to lift the patient's hand up, then place your fingers under the armpit, and lift the joint with force upward to its place.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	 And the minister raises his hand, stretches it upward, then places it below.
si venra hastanment.	 It will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	 And if it does not come as we have said in fewer days afterward, then the patient must be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	 And the assistant should gently soften and soothe, as with a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and mallow in water, and it should be administered.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	 Then let the patient be made to lie on his back, and under the cushion place a cloth of wool, not too soft nor too hard. Then let the healer place his heel upon the cloth, and lift the chief of the sound shoulder vigorously, and pull the hand of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	 And another minister shall dye the patient's head, so that it does not move downward;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	 that shoulder returns immediately, and if you see this, then reset it in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	 And it is necessary for you to have a man who is taller than the patient be present.
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	 And he should stand straight by the patient's side, and push his shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit up, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And another minister shall pull the patient's hand downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too light, then put with him something heavy, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	 Or one can also reset it in this other manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	 And that is to fix a long piece of wood into the ground, so that its head be as round as a pestle, and neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	 Then let it be placed under the patient, but that he has soft cloths above him, and the patient should be standing along the length of the beam.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	 Then let his hand be stretched downward on the other side strongly, and the joint will return to its place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	 And if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 Take a brand of two spans long and four fingers wide, which has the head rounded to enter deeply under the heel, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	 Then place soft cloths on top of the head of the beam, so that the beam does not hurt the patient, then put it under the heel of the patient.
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	 And stretch his arm along the length of the beam, and place the shoulder on the beam, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on one step of a ladder, and let the body hang downward on the other side.
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 The joint swells now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	 And when it is inside, in whatever manner, you must place under the bottom a round piece of wool, then apply the plaster prepared with flour from the mill, with incense and egg white, over all the shoulder and around it, then tie it firmly under the bottom, and twist the ligature over the plaster, and embrace the hand to his neck, and let the hand remain so.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	 And it is necessary that he eats little, until the member is comforted, for it will heal more quickly;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	 and then eats more after 5 or 7 days, and moves it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is moved out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply three cauteries to it, as it is said in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	 And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint does not stay in place, and he cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	 The dislocation that is towards the foot and ankles, or from behind, is done by pushing and stretching of hands, and another method is used there.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And heal until he is cured.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	 Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	 De la dislocation du coude
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	 Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and at points returns;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	 And if it has dislocated from all sides, and especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not reduced, because one sees and feels it well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 And it dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick member with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	 And you must reset it before any abscess develops there, because if an abscess were to form, it would be difficult to reset.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	 and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 It is worse than other dislocations, and it causes more pain, and perhaps death may follow.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	 And the restoration is such that when it is possible to bring it back, you stretch his hand with your two hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 and his arms are spread, and the hands of the mirror according to the cut around, above and below, and push the joint together at its fingers or at the base of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	 And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strike with the root of the palm where it is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	 And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	 and two assistants extend the arm, and hold it in place with two hands so that it does not move during extension.
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	 then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	 and when the mirror has rejoined the joint to his hand, then anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint strongly until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And when it is in place, apply a dry dressing with some egg white, hold it firmly, and bind the arm to the patient's neck, leaving it for a few days before releasing it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	 And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	 And if you see that the joint does not hold well, then renew the dressing and the bandage, leaving it for some days until it is firmly set.
puis le deslie.	 Then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	 And if the patient feels pain after the joint is reset and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, pressing until the pain subsides.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	 Or place a greasy sheepskin over the joint, leaving it for one day and one night, then remove it and have him enter the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	 And when he sweats, wipe the joint quickly, then put the ice back on, and then enter the bath.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do this two or three times until it is healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	 And if you see [pus], put moist, heated cow dung with butter on it, and keep it covered.
si revenra a sa disposition.	 It will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	 The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	 The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the relocation is lighter than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 However, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the very hour that it is dislocated, before the place swells or a hot abscess forms. ¨
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	 And the resetting is done by placing the injured hand on a table, and having the assistant extend the hand, and the physician places his hand equally, so that he places his palm over the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	 Yet, you must check if it is properly in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 Then have the patient put the back of his hand on a table during extension and flexion.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and the physician should place their hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	 If it returns now, it is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If not, apply soothing poultices to the affected area, and leave it thus without reattempting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	 And if he cannot tolerate it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, the joint will remain dislocated.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	 And it does not harm the patient in any way except that while the hand is wet, he cannot grasp anything at all.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	 Then know that the nerves or vessels are cut.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	 And when the hand is in place, apply the poultice we have mentioned, then restrain it and leave for V days, then release it and let it be thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he cannot move it well and there is some stiffness, soak it in hot water and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	 of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on both sides, sometimes at the back of the palm or in the wrist.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	 Then stretch out the fingers and push the dislocation back towards you until it returns, then support the base of the finger and bend it towards the side where it is dislocated.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	 And let it be for two days, and then make it equal on the third day.
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	 And apply a bandage as we have said, and unbind it by day, and make it move, and reapply the bandage at night.
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do this frequently until it is healed, and do the same if it is dislocated in the wrist of the hand, and act as you did before, until it is healed.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 And do the same when it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	 of the dislocation of the shoulder blade
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	 When the shoulder blade or neck is dislocated, and there are multiple dislocations, then there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	 And the signs are that the excretion comes out without will or control, and many times some members are softened, such as the two thighs or the two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	 And often the spine moves in four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	 that which moves to the back is called "gibbousness":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	 The treatment for this is that you should reverse it if the gibbousness has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 If not, there will be no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	 And that which comes from a fall or blows or similar things, the ancients used to describe the methods of healing in great words, where there is not always much benefit;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 But I have summarized it according to my intention, and I have created instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	 I say that in the jaundice which comes to the chest beforehand, neither intelligence nor health has it;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	 And likewise that which comes directly into the two ribs, and one cannot cure except for that which specifically comes to the back, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	 And it is that the patient should be lying on his back in one equal place, and have restraints under him, so that he does not injure himself.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	 Then drive a log into the ground at the head strongly, and another at the feet, and tie one cord beneath the patient's shoulders, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	 And two assistants know the cords, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two logs.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 And let them be well tied, the logs as we have said, and the surgeon places his palms firmly on the spine until it heals.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	 And if it does not heal with this treatment, then take a table three fathoms long, and place it under the bed, and let the patient lie on his side, and push the end of the table under the bed, then place the middle of the table on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	 And let the surgeon place his feet on the other end of the table, and press firmly until it returns to its place.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if you see it, do the same for the vertebra that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	 And it is that you place two faggots at the head of the patient, one arm's length long, and towards the feet, two others, and there should be between each faggot, above and below, a hand's breadth in length.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	 And let there be one hole in each faggot, where the rope passes through, and let the faggots be firmly planted in the ground, so that they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	 And between each two faggots there should be one turning faggot, on which the rope turns, and in the two turnings there should be two small faggots of a hand's breadth in length, to turn the rope.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And then tie the rope that is among the horses to the rope towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other rope, and each of the helpers turns his rope all the length of the rope, and the master places the spine equally as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And when it is healed, place a desiccating plaster with an abundance of egg, then the wool, and then the bandage of a tablet of three fingers in length, which should cover the place of the yellowish color and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a thread, as we have said, and the patient should use subtle nourishment until he is cured.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	 And if anything comes at the end of the health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the bandage that we have mentioned before.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	 And sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes in the lower spine of the back, and it is thought that this is dislocation.
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	 And this is the bone that opens, which is why one should not have presumption about it.
